# Analysis of the sermon

<!-- section 1 (id=3577, raw_sort=1): عقل اور توحید -->

## Intellect and Divine Oneness

There is a fundamental distinction between intellect and reasoning. Intellect is the name of an infinite potential—a faculty that transcends the mortal realm and ascends into the spiritual world, capable of encompassing the realities that dwell there. Reasoning, by contrast, is a finite force; it moves methodically from one subject to another through logical procedure, and its operations remain confined within mental conceptions. Through the light of reason, humanity may perceive absolute realities; through reasoning alone, one can only contemplate these absolutes to a limited degree. The power of reasoning serves the intellect as its instrument and resource, which the intellect deploys according to its needs.[^cite-1]

Absolute reality is that which simply *is*—a self-evident presence that requires no comparison or analogy.

### Intentions and Actions

At the moment when the Battle of Jamal (⟪ar:جمل⟫) was about to commence, a Bedouin man approached Amir al-Mu'minin (Imām ʿAlī) and posed a question: "O Ali! **Do you say that God is one?**" Those nearby sought to silence him, arguing that this was not the opportune moment for such enquiry. Yet Maulānā Ali instructed them to leave the questioner undisturbed. "Surely this man wants to know," he declared. "We are fighting so that people may know!" With this statement, he illuminated the superiority of *intention* over *action*, and made clear that the knowledge of the Absolute Truth—its monotheism ⟪ar:توحید رب العزت،⟫—is the ultimate purpose underlying every deed, regardless of its outward form (whether acts of worship, remembrance, or warfare).

The fact remains: ⟪ar:علم⟫ (knowledge) has always been the true intention animating every external act of Ali (ʿalayhi al-salām). His declaration—"so that people may know"—demonstrates that the real motivation for every intention, thought, and movement is knowledge (⟪ar:علم⟫), whether the arena be a battlefield or a mosque. Therefore, the question of God's oneness is permissible at all times and in all places. During Ali's lifetime, the three great battles—⟪ar:جمل⟫, ⟪ar:صفین⟫, and ⟪ar:نحروان⟫—were waged precisely in response to this question. As the Messenger of Allah (⟪ar:محمد مصطفی صلی اللہ علیہ و آلہ و سلم⟫) said to him: "O Ali! You will fight for the interpretation of the Qur'an as I have fought for the revelation of the Qur'an."[^cite-2]

### Unity of Right

Upon the battlefield itself, Ali delivered a remarkable sermon concerning the monotheism of Allah. He addressed the Bedouin thus: it is impermissible to call Allah "one" in the sense of number or enumeration, for He who has no parallel cannot be comprehended through numerical categories. Not only is it forbidden to ascribe a partner to Him because ⟪ar:لا ثانی⟫ (there is no second to Him exists), but rather no other can be like unto Him.

This is ⟪ar:'الحق المبین'⟫ (the manifest truth). Beyond all things in the universe, it is evident to all things. And yet, simultaneously, it is both inaccessible and inescapable. With this utterance, Ali made clear to those possessed of spiritual insight that one must not assume God is "one God" merely *in comparison to* many gods; rather, He alone is ⟪ar:الحق⟫ (the Real), and all else is mere pretense and deception.

In Arabic, the word ⟪ar:'آیت'⟫ (āyah, sign or verse) denotes a mark, and every mark points to its maker. Hoofprints in sand are verses testifying to the horse's existence and presence; smoke is a verse for fire. Everything created serves as ⟪ar:'آیت'⟫ (a sign) pointing to the existence of Allah—an argument declaring His ⟪ar:'ھو'⟫ (His presence). The very meaning of ⟪ar:تاویل⟫ (esoteric exegesis) is "that which returns to the First." He is the First; He is the Last; He is the Manifest; He is the Hidden—and all outward abundance returns to His ⟪ar:'وحدانیت'⟫ (oneness) and ⟪ar:'أحدیت'⟫ (absolute uniqueness). As Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 41:53⟫
> ⟪ar:‏سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ حَتَّىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ ۗ أَوَلَمْ يَكْفِ بِرَبِّكَ أَنَّهُۥ عَلَىٰ كُلِّ شَىْءٍۢ شَهِيدٌ ‎⟫
> *We will show them Our Signs in the universe, and in their own selves, until it becomes manifest to them that this (the Qur'an) is the truth. Is it not sufficient in regard to your Lord that He is a Witness over all things?*

In this verse, Allah employs the plural "signs" and "horizons," yet for the Truth itself uses the singular with the definite article—⟪ar:ال⟫—signifying that the multiplicity of all cosmic and spiritual signs converges upon a single Truth that is One.[^cite-3]

An uneasiness and yearning stirs within the human breast, drawing us ever toward the bliss of union with the One. There is an inescapable need to strive perpetually for the felicity of oneness.

### Qur'an and Interpretation

The Qur'an is one, yet each verse contains multiple layers of meaning. ⟪ar:امام جعفر الصادق علیہ السلام⟫ (Imām Jaʿfar al-Ṣādiq, upon him be peace) said to one of his companions: "If I wished, I could expound seventy distinct interpretations for each verse of the Qur'an." ⟪ar:محمد مصطفی صلی اللہ علیہ و آلہ و سلم⟫ (the Prophet Muḥammad, upon whom be blessings and peace) taught Ali the *taʾwīl* (esoteric exegesis) of the Qur'an, and then declared of him: "Ali is with the Qur'an and the Qur'an is with Ali." When Ali spoke of ⟪ar:سورۃ الفاتحۃ⟫ (the Chapter of the Opening) to his uncle al-ʿAbbās, he said: "If I were to unfold its meaning, seventy camels laden with books could not bear it." Ali is the true exegete of the Qur'an.[^cite-4]

Just as the Qur'an is one text bound between two volumes—Muḥammad and Ali—so too do all the intermediate pages refer to the Imams (ʿalayhim al-salām) descended from them, each page a verse reflecting the Divine Reality.

### Reason, Revelation, Spirit

Allah's revelation—the Book of the Qur'an—⟪ar:'صامت'⟫ (is silent; it does not speak in its own voice). It requires an interpreter to expound its meaning: ⟪ar:لا بُدَّ لَہُ مِن تَرجُماَن⟫ (it must have an interpreter). Similarly, to comprehend divine messages ⟪ar:وحی⟫ (revelation), one requires an interpreter—a messenger. That interpreter is the intellect, ⟪ar:عقل⟫, and their connection is evident from the Messenger of Allah's saying: "The messenger of a man is the interpreter of his intellect."[^cite-5] He is, as it were, an emissary dispatched by the intellect itself.

⟪ar:'حق'⟫ (Truth) demands that every utterance of Maulānā Ali reflect the Qur'an. Each word of his moves from the Qur'anic text through its revelation, from revelation through its spirit, and from spirit to the One who reveals it—returning the Qur'anic word through all these stations to its primordial origin. Therefore, the One who revealed this word (the Qur'an) is simultaneously hidden within Ali's discourse—concealed in its meaning—yet manifest through its words. ⟪ar:عقل اول⟫ (The First Intellect) cannot be grasped or described; only through the impressions and traces of creation can its existence and manifestation be acknowledged.

| The Revelation | The Prophet | The Interpretation |
| --- | --- | --- |
| ⟪ar:عقل اول⟫ (The First Intellect) | Muḥammad | Ali |
| The Revelation of the Qur'an | The Words of the Qur'an | The Meaning of the Qur'an |
| Allah | Revelation | Intellect |

Revelation and intellect appear to scholars as two distinct categories:

| Revelation | Intellect |
| --- | --- |
| Convention; tradition | Nature; inherent reality |
| Imitation; conformity | Research; verification |
| Piety; reverence | Inquiry; investigation |

Yet in reality the two are intimate. Each perfects and completes the other. These seemingly separate domains unite to form a single reality—the paramount goal of ⟪ar:توحید⟫ (unification), for ⟪ar:'توحید'⟫ literally means "to make one" or "to unify." Consider an example: if the truth is that Ahmad possesses one goat, this truth emerges only through the negation that Ahmad does not possess two goats—a combination of denial and affirmation.

The union of intellect and revelation, to which the "one" reality points, is ⟪ar:'روح'⟫ (the spirit) that stands between them. The intellect, though vast in its domain, has limits (apart from the soul) and cannot withstand revelation alone. But the spirit—the animating force of intellect—is boundless in its expanse. Only the spirit can receive revelation's messages, become aware of them, and discern their sublimity. It receives these divine messages and conveys them to the intellect; the intellect then processes and integrates them. Were this not so, revelation would devolve into mere rules and regulations imposed upon human will, rather than serving as a creative inspiration for the awakened intellect.

Revelation, being multidimensional, cannot be confined to a single dimension of words. The Messenger of Allah clothed Allah's revelation in words so that spirituality might take on material form, enabling humanity to perceive it through the five senses. Here the connection between revelation and intellect becomes manifest: whereas words confine meaning, the intellect liberates meaning from verbal constraint. Through it, the outer surface of words generates countless streams of inner significance. This is illustrated in the story of Moses: when Moses struck the rock with his staff (the intellect), twelve springs of meaning gushed forth.[^cite-6]

> ⟪quran 2:60⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ وَإِذِ ٱسْتَسْقَىٰ مُوسَىٰ لِقَوْمِهِۦ فَقُلْنَا ٱضْرِب بِّعَصَاكَ ٱلْحَجَرَ ۖ فَٱنفَجَرَتْ مِنْهُ ٱثْنَتَا عَشْرَةَ عَيْنًۭا ۖ قَدْ عَلِمَ كُلُّ أُنَاسٍۢ مَّشْرَبَهُمْ ۖ كُلُوا۟ وَٱشْرَبُوا۟ مِن رِّزْقِ ٱللَّهِ وَلَا تَعْثَوْا۟ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ مُفْسِدِينَ ‎⟫
> *And (remember) when Musa (Moses) asked for water for his people, We said: "Strike the stone with your stick." Then gushed forth therefrom twelve springs. Each (group of) people knew its own place for water. "Eat and drink of that which Allah has provided and do not act corruptly, making mischief on the earth."*

The more refined and subtle the spirit, the more fully it grasps revelation's content and extracts precious pearls from this single shell. The intellect is the inner messenger through which a human may empirically confirm and authenticate the divine messages of revelation. Were this not the case, humanity would be forced to accept revelation's message only through blind conformity.

For this reason, Amir al-Mu'minin told Kamīl ibn Ziyād that one of the reasons Allah sent the prophets was to awaken the hidden treasures of the intellect. The intellect is animated and awakened by revelation. Revelation is, in truth, a voice reaching the spiritual depths of the intellect, through which the seeds of awareness—sown by Allah on the eternal day—are germinated and brought to bloom. The intellect derives its sustenance from nothing but revelation; and the treasures buried in the soil of intellect cannot be uncovered except by revelation. From this perspective emerges an eternal connection between intellect and revelation, whereby one might describe them as analogous, or at least characterize the intellect as a form of revelation.

Maulānā Ali's statement—in which he identifies the reason for sending the prophets as the extraction of the intellect's hidden treasures—proves that the spiritual intellect of any human cannot be ignorant of revelation's message; rather, it recognizes it, because Allah's message accords with the very essence of the intellect. Since both share the same origin, the intellect recognizes the source: it is from ⟪ar:'الہ الحقیقی'⟫ (the True Divine). The prophetic messages awaken the intellect; they cannot be viewed as separate from it. Rather, these messages are the very purpose and perfection of the intellect itself. Thus ⟪ar:'روح'⟫ (the spirit) may receive these divine messages through the intellect and integrate them into itself until the two become one. When this occurs, the heart acquires the capacity to "see" Allah. Allah cannot be perceived with bodily eyes; only the heart perceives Him—what Amir al-Mu'minin calls ⟪ar:'حق الیقین'⟫ (the certainty of truth).

<!-- section 2 (id=3599, raw_sort=2): عقل اور استدلال کا فرق -->

## The Distinction Between Intellect and Reasoning

There is a continuity between the faculty of intellect and the power of reasoning, yet the two are simultaneously distinct and separate. Their continuity lies in this: every thought and idea originates from a meaningful concept, and reasoning produces ideas that are logical and grounded in reality. The faculty of reasoning proceeds through ⟪ar:مفارقۃ⟫ (paradox), ⟪ar:تناقض⟫ (antinomy), ⟪ar:نفی⟫ (negation), and ⟪ar:اثبات⟫ (affirmation), cultivating the hidden treasures of intellect through these instruments. Yet reasoning has a limit—a boundary it cannot transcend. Its domain is restricted to material matters; it cannot enter the realm of spirit. To traverse into spiritual realms requires an external guide: ⟪ar:'وحی⟫ (revelation), which one may understand as the inner messenger that is ⟪ar:'عقل'⟫ (the intellect). Through this companion, intellect ascends into the spiritual domain.

When ⟪ar:'الہ'⟫ (Allah or divinity) Maulānā Ali rejects certain conceptual frameworks, he does so because of the insufficiency and weakness of the discursive faculty. This rejection—seemingly destructive—becomes the foundation for awakening a spiritual or transcendent understanding, evoking a consciousness hidden within the intellect and lying beyond reason's reach. Thus the negation of finite human imagination forms the basis for affirming infinite divinity. It is negation that elevates; it is not negation that diminishes. This paradoxical interplay of negation and affirmation permeates his discourse. In his praise of Allah, he says—as recorded in ⟪ar:نہج البلاغۃ⟫ (the Path of Eloquence):

> Praise be to Allah, whose praise is beyond the reach of those who speak, whose blessings cannot be enumerated, whose diligent servants cannot fulfill His due, whom determination cannot attain, whom diving cannot reach, whose attribute has no bound, no descriptor, no limited duration, and no extended span. He created creatures by His power and spread forth the winds by His mercy, and filled the expanse of His land with stones.

In Amir al-Mu'minin's utterance (and in many others), we perceive this paradox: Allah is worthy of praise, yet He transcends all praise; His blessings exist, yet cannot be counted; other things may be enumerated, yet these cannot. It is obligatory to fulfill Allah's right, yet this right cannot be fulfilled. Such contradictory obligations permeate his discourse.

Divine attributes cannot be ⟪ar:لیس لصفاتہ حد محدود⟫ (bounded or delimited), nor can they be described—yet they exist nonetheless. The Qur'an itself ascribes to Allah such attributes as ⟪ar:'کریم'⟫ (Generous), ⟪ar:'عزیز'⟫ (Mighty), and ⟪ar:'رحیم'⟫ (Merciful). Yet Maulānā Ali declares that none of these attributes can be determined or defined. God is generous—but to what extent? What measure of generosity? Is it like the generosity of one person, another person, or yet another? Or like theirs?

He states: "⟪ar:أخلاص⟫ (Sincerity) emerges from the negation of all attributes pertaining to Allah." On one hand, we must acknowledge Allah's attributes; on the other, we must negate them. The human mind grasps Allah through these attributed words. Yet Ali negates these very attributes, leaving no pathway for conceptual understanding of Allah. If we affirm the attributes through words and then negate them, what is one to do? Yet from this contradiction of affirmation and negation arises a deeper and richer knowledge: the hidden treasures of the intellect awaken, and humanity is compelled to recognize that knowledge of Allah transcends the powers of thinking, reasoning, and discernment—faculties that the soul may feel but the intellect cannot comprehend.

He declares: "My Lord cannot be imprisoned within dimensions, motion, time, and space. He is subtle yet not in subtlety; magnificent yet not in magnitude; great yet not in greatness." Here again, he affirms and negates the attributes of Allah simultaneously. Allah possesses these attributes, yet cannot be confined to them; He cannot be reduced to our imaginings and concepts. These attributes offer the intellect some framework of understanding, though that framework is weak and incomplete. To acknowledge the perfection of these attributes, they must be negated—to overcome the deficiency of conception.

From the interplay of negation and affirmation arises the depth of ⟪ar:'علم'⟫ (knowledge). Yet this depth cannot be established unless it is acknowledged that both negation and affirmation fall short of accurately reflecting this reality. To negate all attributes is to "confess" His infinite Self—the true goal of the universe and the substance of ⟪ar:کلمۃ اخلاص، لا الہ الا اللہ⟫ (the Word of Sincerity: "There is no god but Allah"). For any concept to take root in the human mind, a definition is required; and where definition exists, there are limits and exclusions. But divine attributes, being infinite properties of infinite Essence, are free from these constraints. In a sense, one may substitute every divine attribute into the negation of the Kalimah, reciting: ⟪ar:⟪ar:'لا رحمن الا اللہ'⟫ (There is no Merciful save Allah)⟫, ⟪ar:'لا عظیم الا اللہ'⟫ (There is no Mighty save Allah), ⟪ar:'لا کریم الا اللہ'⟫ (There is no Generous save Allah), and so forth. Thus the apparent negation becomes an affirmation of their identity. All such attributes are not externally affixed to His Essence but are intrinsic to it—distinguished only through ⟪ar:'علم الوجود'⟫ (the knowledge of existence, or metaphysical knowledge).

For this reason, Allah Himself declares:

> ⟪quran 23:91⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مَا ٱتَّخَذَ ٱللَّهُ مِن وَلَدٍۢ وَمَا كَانَ مَعَهُۥ مِنْ إِلَهٍ ۚ إِذًۭا لَّذَهَبَ كُلُّ إِلَهٍ بِمَا خَلَقَ وَلَعَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَىٰ بَعْضٍۢ ۚ سُبْحَنَ ٱللَّهِ عَمَّا يَصِفُونَ ‎⟫
> *No son (or offspring or children) did Allah beget, nor is there any god along with Him; (if there had been many gods), behold, each god would have taken away what he had created, and some would have tried to overcome others! Glorified be Allah above all that they attribute to Him!*[^cite-7]

God's infinity deserves liberation from all imagined constraints—yet the heart is not incapable of knowing Him. It perceives Him through its own discernment. The heart has always been the seat of rational thought and wisdom, and the intellect has ever depended upon it for its purification. ⟪ar:'ذکر اللہ'⟫ (The remembrance of Allah) is, in fact, the source of the intellect's purification; this is why Ali says: "The remembrance of Allah is the noblest form of worship." Yet here too we encounter a paradox: ⟪ar:ذکر⟫ (remembrance) cannot be attained unless the worshipper "loses" himself in it—a state called ⟪ar:'فنا بااللہ'⟫ (annihilation in Allah).

Intellect is a spiritual faculty; the soul is its origin and the source of its life. Without intellect, the soul becomes an unconscious entity; without a true soul, intellect inclines toward lifeless abstractions. Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 32:7-9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِىٓ أَحْسَنَ كُلَّ شَىْءٍ خَلَقَهُۥ ۖ وَبَدَأَ خَلْقَ ٱلْإِنسَنِ مِن طِينٍۢ ‎ ‏ثُمَّ جَعَلَ نَسْلَهُۥ مِن سُلَلَةٍۢ مِّن مَّآءٍۢ مَّهِينٍۢ ‎ ‏ثُمَّ سَوَّىٰهُ وَنَفَخَ فِيهِ مِن رُّوحِهِۦ ۖ وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ ٱلسَّمْعَ وَٱلْأَبْصَرَ وَٱلْأَفْـِٔدَةَ ۚ قَلِيلًۭا مَّا تَشْكُرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Who made everything He has created good, and He began the creation of man from clay. Then He made his offspring from semen of worthless water (male and female sexual discharge). Then He fashioned him in due proportion, and breathed into him the soul (created by Allah for that person), and He gave you hearing (ears), sight (eyes) and hearts. Little is the thanks you give!*

The ⟪ar:'نفخ الروح'⟫ (insufflation of the spirit) creates life and consciousness. If the soul does not receive its due, such existence becomes a form of death. Through this Divine Spirit, static things become animated; unconscious objects awaken to awareness. By this Spirit, a person acquires knowledge not only of others but also of himself. From the union of this "existence" and "knowledge," every spiritual concept is established. When this soul attaches to the body, life emerges—and therefore knowledge revives it, as Allah says:

> ⟪quran 8:24⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱسْتَجِيبُوا۟ لِلَّهِ وَلِلرَّسُولِ إِذَا دَعَاكُمْ لِمَا يُحْيِيكُمْ ۖ وَٱعْلَمُوٓا۟ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يَحُولُ بَيْنَ ٱلْمَرْءِ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَأَنَّهُۥٓ إِلَيْهِ تُحْشَرُونَ ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Answer Allah (by obeying Him) and (His) Messenger when he (PBUH) calls you to that which will give you life, and know that Allah comes in between a person and his heart (i.e. He prevents an evil person to decide anything). And verily to Him you shall (all) be gathered.*

Ali has already affirmed that the divine invitation in which humanity finds life is ⟪ar:'وحی'⟫ (revelation)—the very force that awakens and animates the hidden treasures of intellect. The intellect, being the expression of the soul, is not merely a mental faculty; it is grounded in *life* itself. Maulānā Ali teaches that ⟪ar:'عاقل'⟫ (a wise person) is one whose knowledge is not only correct but whose actions are also correct, and whose striving is always directed toward the Absolute Truth. Another definition: ⟪ar:'عاقل'⟫ (the wise) keep things in their proper place, which proves that only the wise can be just—for only those who perceive things according to their true reality can place them in their rightful station. Correct thinking, impeccable virtue, and authentic being are attributes of the intellect.

<!-- section 3 (id=3578, raw_sort=3): علی کا کمیل ابن زیاد کو خطاب -->

## The Discourse of Ali to Kamīl ibn Ziyād

Kamīl ibn Ziyād an-Nakhāʿī has transmitted that Amir al-Mu'minin ʿAlī ibn Abī Ṭālib (upon him be peace) took hold of his hand and led him into the graveyard. When they had passed through it and left the city behind, Ali heaved a deep sigh and spoke:

⟪ar-quote:قال كُمَيْل بن زياد- أخذ بيدي أميرالمؤمنين علي بن أبي طالب عليه السلام ، فأخرجني إلى الجبّان فلمّا أصحر تنفّس الصّعَدَاء ثمّ قال⟫

"O Kamīl, hearts are vessels. The finest of them are those that preserve their contents. So guard well what I say to you."

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْل بْن زِيَادٍ، إِنَّ هذهِ الْقُلُوبَ أَوْعِيَةٌ فَخَيْرُهَا أَوْعَاهَا فَاحْفَظْ عَنِّي مَا أَقُولُ لَكَ⟫

Humanity falls into three categories. First is the scholar-servant of Allah, devoted to the Divine. Second is the seeker of knowledge who walks the path of deliverance. And lastly is the rabble—base creatures who follow every caller and sway with every wind. They neither illumine themselves with the light of knowledge nor take refuge in any firm support.

⟪ar-quote:النَّاسُ ثَلاَثَةٌ- فَعَالِمٌ رَبَّانِيٌّ وَمُتَعَلِّمٌ عَلَى سَبِيلِ نَجَاةٍ، وَهَمَجٌ رَعَاعٌ أَتْبَاعُ كُلِّ نَاعِقٍ يَمِيلُونَ مَعَ كُلِّ رِيحٍ، لَمْ يَسْتَضِيئُوا بِنُورِ الْعِلْمِ، وَلَمْ يَلْجَؤُوا إِلَى رُكْنٍ وَثِيقٍ⟫

"O Kamīl, knowledge is superior to wealth. Knowledge guards you, whereas you must guard wealth. Wealth diminishes through spending, while knowledge increases through expenditure. The benefit of wealth perishes as wealth itself perishes."

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْلُ، الْعِلْمُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ الْمَالِ- الْعِلْمُ يَحْرُسُكَ وَأَنْتَ تَحْرُسُ المَالَ، وَالْمَالُ تَنْقُصُهُ النَّفَقَةُ، وَالْعِلْمُ يَزْكُوعَلَى الاْنْفَاقِ، وَصَنِيعُ الْمَالِ يَزُولُ بِزَوَالِهِ⟫

"O Kamīl, knowledge is a faith by which one lives. Through it a human acquires obedience in his lifetime and a good name after his death. Knowledge is the ruler; wealth is ruled."

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْلَ بْنَ زِيَادٍ مَعْرِفَةُ الْعِلْمِ دِينٌ يُدَانُ بِهِ . بِهِ يَكْسِبُ الْإِنْسَانُ الطَّاعَةَ فِى حَيَاتِهِ وَ جَمِيلَ الْأُحْدُوثَةِ بَعْدَ وَفَاتِهِ وَ الْعِلْمُ حَاكِمٌ وَ الْمَالُ مَحْكُومٌ عَلَيْهِ⟫

"O Kamīl, the collectors of wealth are dead, though alive; whereas the learned remain living as long as the world endures. Their bodies are absent, yet their example is present in hearts. Behold—here is a vast ocean of knowledge!" And he pointed to his chest. "I have sought for one to bear it, and I have found one—but he proved untrustworthy. He would employ religion as a tool for worldly gain and use Allah's favors to domineer over people, wielding Allah's arguments to rule His servants. Or he would obey the bearers of truth, yet lack discernment in his bosom; at the first shadow of doubt, misgiving would assail his heart."

⟪ar-quote:يَا كُمَيْلُ هَلَكَ خُزَّانُ الْأَمْوَالِ وَ هُمْ أَحْيَاءٌ وَ الْعُلَمَاءُ بَاقُونَ مَا بَقِيَ الدَّهْرُ أَعْيَانُهُمْ مَفْقُودَةٌ وَ أَمْثَالُهُمْ فِى الْقُلُوبِ مَوْجُودَةٌ هَا إِنَّ هَاهُنَا لَعِلْماً جَمّاً وَ أَشَارَ بِيَدِهِ إِلَى صَدْرِهِ لَوْ أَصَبْتُ لَهُ حَمَلَةً بَلَى أَصَبْتُ لَقِناً غَيْرَ مَأْمُونٍ عَلَيْهِ مُسْتَعْمِلًا آلَةَ الدِّينِ لِلدُّنْيَا وَ مُسْتَظْهِراً بِنِعَمِ اللَّهِ عَلَى عِبَادِهِ وَ بِحُجَجِهِ عَلَى أَوْلِيَائِهِ أَوْ مُنْقَاداً لِحَمَلَةِ الْحَقِّ لَا بَصِيرَةَ لَهُ فِى أَحْنَائِهِ يَنْقَدِحُ الشَّكُّ فِى قَلْبِهِ لِأَوَّلِ عَارِضٍ مِنْ شُبْهَةٍ⟫

"Alas, neither this nor that suffices! Either he is consumed by appetites, a tool of passion; or he is besotted with hoarding and accumulation—neither shows any concern for religion. The nearest likeness to such is grazing cattle. Thus knowledge dies when its bearers die."

⟪ar-quote:أَلَا لَا ذَا وَ لَا ذَاكَ أَوْ مَنْهُوماً بِاللَّذَّةِ سَلِسَ الْقِيَادِ لِلشَّهْوَةِ أَوْ مُغْرَماً بِالْجَمْعِ وَ الِادِّخَارِ لَيْسَا مِنْ رُعَاةِ الدِّينِ فِى شَيْ‏ءٍ أَقْرَبُ شَيْ‏ءٍ شَبَهاً بِهِمَا الْأَنْعَامُ السَّائِمَةُ كَذَلِكَ يَمُوتُ الْعِلْمُ بِمَوْتِ حَامِلِيهِ⟫

"O Allah! Yet surely the earth is never bereft of one who upholds Allah's proof—whether openly and renowned, or concealed through fear—lest Allah's proofs and evidences be rendered void. How many such exist, and where are they? By Allah, they are few in number, yet great in esteem before Allah. Through them Allah preserves His proofs and evidences until they entrust them to others like themselves and sow these seeds in the hearts of those who resemble them."

⟪ar-quote:اللَّهُمَّ بَلَىٰ! لاَ تَخْلُو الاْرْضُ مِنْ قَائِمٍ لله بِحُجَّةٍ، إِمَّا ظَاهِراً مَشْهُوراً، أوْ خَائِفاً مَغْمُوراً لِئَلاَّ تَبْطُلَ حُجَجُ اللهِ وَبَيِّنَاتُهُ. وَكَمْ ذَا وَأَيْنَ أُولئِكَ؟ أُولئِكَ ـ وَاللَّهِ ـ الاْقَلُّونَ عَدَداً، وَالاْعْظَمُونَ قَدْراً، يَحْفَظُ اللهُ بِهِمْ حُجَجَهُ وَبَيِّنَاتِهِ، حَتَّىٰ يُودِعُوهَا نُظَرَاءَهُمْ، وَيَزْرَعُوهَا فِي قُلُوبِ أَشْبَاهِهِمْ⟫

"Knowledge has borne them onward into the realities of true discernment. They have embraced the spirit of certainty. They ease what the comfortable find difficult; they find beauty in what the ignorant find repellent. They inhabit this world with bodies, yet their spirits are attached to the Higher Realm. They are Allah's vicegerents upon His earth and callers to His religion. Oh, how I long to see them! Depart now, O Kamīl, wherever you wish!"

⟪ar-quote:هَجَمَ بِهِمُ الْعِلْمُ عَلَىٰ حَقِيقَةِ الْبَصِيرَةِ، وَبَاشَرُوا رُوحَ الْيَقِينِ، وَاسْتَلاَنُوامَا اسْتَوْعَرَهُ الْمُتْرَفُونَ وَأَنِسُوا بِمَا اسْتَوْحَشَ مِنْهُ الْجَاهِلُونَ، وَصَحِبُوا الدُّنْيَا بِأَبْدَانٍ أَرْوَاحُهَا مُعَلَّقَةٌ بِالْـمَحَلِّ الاْعْلَىٰ، أُولئِكَ خُلَفَاءُ اللهِ فِي أَرْضِهِ، وَالدُّعَاةُ إِلَىٰ دِينِهِ، آهِ آهِ شَوْقاً إِلَىٰ رُؤْيَتِهِمْ! انْصَرِفْ إذَا شِئْتَ!⟫

<!-- section 4 (id=3579, raw_sort=4): علم اور بصیرت -->

## Knowledge and Spiritual Discernment

In this discourse, Ali describes the blessed servants of Allah—the Imams—as the very sustenance of Allah's religion. By "Divine Religion" is meant that faith which has descended from the Almighty, embodying the essence of belief in its completeness and immutability. As he declared, "Religion is preserved through the knowledge of true scholars." Without such learned Imams, all traces of religion would vanish. He then proclaimed: ⟪ar-quote:هَجَمَ بِهِمُ الْعِلْمُ عَلَىٰ حَقِيقَةِ الْبَصِيرَةِ⟫ (Knowledge has charged through them into the realities of insight).[^cite-8]

Although knowledge rests eternally hidden within the essence of the intellect, it must be awakened. His use of the word "charged" (⟪ar:'ھَجَمَ'⟫, from ⟪ar:ھجم⟫) signifies that this knowledge lies concealed in meanings buried within the depths of words—layers of deeper significance subordinate to surface meaning. This utterance alludes to varying degrees and stations of knowledge. When he pointed to his chest and said: ⟪ar-quote:هَاهُنَا لَعِلْماً جَمّاً⟫ (Here is a vast ocean of knowledge), the external reference is to the chest; yet to reach what the chest contains—the heart—one must penetrate its inner depths. Words may point to hidden truths, but they cannot encompass them.

In Arabic, the word ⟪ar:'ھَجَمَ'⟫ means to charge or attack. When an army charges, it aims for the center—the heart of the opposing force. Similarly, ⟪ar:ھجم⟫ invites us to investigate: to attack the surface of words and penetrate to the depths of reality concealed within them. Once the depths of insight are disclosed, contemplation's gates open before the intellect, and one knows the truth of knowledge itself. As the Lord says: "He who has developed understanding has attained the essence of knowledge." This demands effort—as is affirmed: "Knowledge is gained through sustained study." The aim is that a person should integrate this external knowledge into his own essence through the intellect, rendering the two as one. The faculty of ⟪ar:'روح'⟫ (the spirit) is what accomplishes this ⟪ar:'توحید'⟫ (unification) of knowledge and self.

### The Struggle Against the Self

Yet this is possible only when the self is freed from egocentricity ⟪ar:أنانیت⟫. Maulānā Ali teaches that the wise are those engaged in perpetual struggle against the baser inclinations, lusts, and desires of the self—for all of these assail the faculty of knowledge. The soul's evils are like clouds that, when they veil the sky of intellect, dim the vision and obscure reality. The Qur'an characterizes these evils as "rust":

> ⟪quran 83:14⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كَلَّا ۖ بَلْۜ رَانَ عَلَىٰ قُلُوبِهِم مَّا كَانُوا۟ يَكْسِبُونَ ‎⟫
> *Nay! But on their hearts is the Ran (covering of sins and evil deeds) which they used to earn.*[^cite-9]

Though these evils are morally reprehensible, from a spiritual perspective they stand as the antithesis of God's realities. To follow them is to obliterate sight and blind the heart's eye—the eye through which Allah is perceived. A wise person therefore wages constant war against desire and cultivates virtue. The root of all vice is ignorance; one must wage what the Prophet called the ⟪ar:'جہاد اکبر'⟫ (Greater Jihad) against oneself to overcome it. Regarding this ⟪ar:جہاد النفس⟫ (struggle against the self), Maulānā Ali teaches:

| The wise person fights his self through knowledge.
| The mightiest is he who conquers his own self.
| Those who fight against their souls in Allah's cause have rank with Allah as those martyred.
| The ultimate battle is man's war with his own self.
| He who knows his self contends with it.
| No jihad is greater than the jihad of the self. |

This war, though directed at the self, is in reality for the self's own good. Ali declares: ⟪ar:العقل⟫ (The intellect) is the commander of the righteous army, while ⟪ar:الھوی⟫ (desire) is the commander of Satan's army. The self is caught between the two, torn ⟪ar:متجاذبہ بینھُما⟫ (pulled in both directions), and whoever overcomes it joins his ranks. This demonstrates that complete conquest of the self is necessary to be enlisted in the Merciful's army. The goal is not the annihilation of the self, but the elimination of what is ⟪ar:'ھوی'⟫ (desire and base inclination) within it. The Qur'an affirms that the Messenger did not speak from ⟪ar:ھوی⟫:

> ⟪quran 53:3-4⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمَا يَنطِقُ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰٓ ‎ ‏إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا وَحْىٌۭ يُوحَىٰ ‎⟫
> *Nor does he speak of (his own) desire. It is only an Inspiration that is inspired.*[^cite-10]

The intellect serves as interpreter of the Merciful's army, which battles against Satan's army. The term ⟪ar:الھوی⟫ appears in another Qur'anic context:

> ⟪quran 25:43⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ أَفَأَنتَ تَكُونُ عَلَيْهِ وَكِيلًا ‎⟫
> *Have you (O Muhammad PBUH) seen him who has taken as his ilah (god) his own desire? Would you then be a Wakîl (a disposer of his affairs or a watcher) over him?*[^cite-11]

> ⟪quran 45:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ وَأَضَلَّهُ ٱللَّهُ عَلَىٰ عِلْمٍۢ وَخَتَمَ عَلَىٰ سَمْعِهِۦ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَجَعَلَ عَلَىٰ بَصَرِهِۦ غِشَوَةًۭ فَمَن يَهْدِيهِ مِنۢ بَعْدِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أَفَلَا تَذَكَّرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Have you seen him who takes his own lust (vain desires) as his ilah (god), and Allah knowing (him as such), left him astray, and sealed his hearing and his heart, and put a cover on his sight. Who then will guide him after Allah? Will you not then remember?*[^cite-12]

The Prophet declared that ⟪ar:'شرک خفی'⟫ (subtle idolatry), concealed within believers, "creeps among you like the ant's footstep." To shatter the idols of the self and its ⟪ar:أنانیت⟫ (egocentrism), an external force is required—one not derived from the self itself. These are the "divine sciences" that flow from intellect and revelation. Allah states:

> ⟪quran 79:40-41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِۦ وَنَهَىٰ ٱلنَّفْسَ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰ ‎ ‏فَإِنَّ ٱلْجَنَّةَ هِىَ ٱلْمَأْوَىٰ ‎⟫
> *But as for him who feared standing before his Lord, and restrained himself from impure evil desires, and lusts. Verily, Paradise will be his abode.*[^cite-13]

The soul's fundamental energy cannot be destroyed; it must be redirected—from the myriad satanic impulses toward the Beneficent. Tawhīd (⟪ar:توحید⟫) means "to make one" or "to unify." Allah is not only ⟪ar:'أحد'⟫ (Uniquely One) but also the Creator. In this sense, monotheism is both an acknowledgment of Allah's ⟪ar:أحدیت⟫ (absolute oneness) and a declaration of one's own ⟪ar:أحد⟫, so that it may be properly reflected in the created realm. To know God is to be united with Him. One meaning of intellect is "binding" or "containing," for it encompasses and contains meaning. In contrast stands the "heart," which is the locus of intellect and broadcasts spiritual realities—the intellect grasps, the heart radiates. The intellect unites the soul's disparate elements into one whole. This is why the Creator of the universe declares:

"He who knows Allah becomes unified with Him; he who knows his own self separates from it; he who knows people distances himself from them; he who knows the world renounces it."

### Sincere Devotion

In another place, Maulānā Ali names this complete alignment of the self with Divine reality ⟪ar:أخلاص⟫ (sincerity or purification). The term ⟪ar:خَلُصَ⟫ denotes complete purification, descent into essence, or purity unadulterated. Thus he says: "Make your knowledge and deeds, love and hatred, taking and renouncing, speech and silence pure for Allah's sake." The meaning of sincerity is to purify oneself for Allah in such fashion that no blemish remains—where "blemish" means everything that is ⟪ar:'غیر اللہ'⟫ (other than Allah). That is, sincerity is the purification of devotion, action, intention, and passion from everything other than Allah. The most grievous of these blemishes is ⟪ar:أنانیت⟫ (egocentrism). Sincerity demands that every action, thought, and moment of existence be selfless and for Allah's sake. Ali's use of the phrase "final battle" underscores this very point. Whoever develops such sincerity becomes a ⟪ar:شہید⟫ (witness and martyr) in Allah's sight—having sacrificed his self for Allah's sake, living by the light of intellect and sustained by revelation, as He affirmed:

> ⟪quran 3:169⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَحْسَبَنَّ ٱلَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا۟ فِى سَبِيلِ ٱللَّهِ أَمْوَتًۢا ۚ بَلْ أَحْيَآءٌ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ ‎⟫
> *Think not of those who are killed in the Way of Allah as dead. Nay, they are alive, with their Lord, and they have provision.*[^cite-14]

The witness is also one who testifies—through the sacrifice of his soul—that he stands with Allah and against all that is other than Allah. Such a person's focus is not his own self but Allah alone as the center of all reality. Thus sincerity is existence for Allah's sake and fullness in Allah, as He declares:

> ⟪quran 6:162⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلْ إِنَّ صَلَاتِى وَنُسُكِى وَمَحْيَاىَ وَمَمَاتِى لِلَّهِ رَبِّ ٱلْعَلَمِينَ ‎⟫
> *Say (O Muhammad PBUH): "Verily, my Salat (prayer), my sacrifice, my living, and my dying are for Allah, the Lord of the 'Alamîn (mankind, jinns and all that exists).*[^cite-15]

### Devotion and Prayer

Prayer is the very substance of sincere devotion. The human soul's nourishment is worship; there is no better sustenance for it than prayer. This is why Allah mentions prayer first in this verse and in countless others. Should one neglect prayer, he deprives his soul of its sustenance and fails to render it its due. Whoever cannot fulfill his own obligations will never fulfill the obligations toward others. He who sets things right between himself and Allah will find Allah setting things right between him and His servants. Consider this Qur'anic verse:

> ⟪quran 15:99⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱعْبُدْ رَبَّكَ حَتَّىٰ يَأْتِيَكَ ٱلْيَقِينُ ‎⟫
> *And worship your Lord until there comes unto you the certainty (i.e. death).*[^cite-16]

If the intellect's hidden treasures are to awaken, one must pursue knowledge with steadfast dedication and utmost sincerity. Such dedication demands a focus upon divine realities and a profound form of worship—a worship in which no barrier stands between seeker and the Sought. This is worship wherein the servant forgets all, even himself; otherwise mechanical worship bears no fruit. Maulānā Ali teaches that the example of one who prays without sincere exertion is like one who shoots an arrow without a bow. Similarly, knowledge depends upon action; without balanced action it dissipates. The heart cannot digest knowledge acquired without earnestness; therefore it lacks vision and cannot perceive Allah.

The Master of the Universe teaches: "Seek knowledge, and life will seek you." Initially, one stands ignorant of life's realities. Through knowledge, consciousness awakens. Yet when this is pursued with sincerity over time—when knowledge is continuously translated into action—a threshold arrives where one no longer integrates knowledge into oneself; rather, authentic life absorbs and encompasses the seeker. What began as disciplined effort and sincere striving becomes the rhythm of existence, pursued now unconsciously with the same dedication. Habit transforms into nature itself.

Returning to the Master's teaching that knowledge surges through them into the realities of insight: ⟪ar:'عالم'⟫ (the one who knows) does not remain submerged in those insights. Rather, he ⟪ar:'علم'⟫ (receives the knowledge), and the world itself becomes his instrument, for he has integrated himself into that knowledge.


<!-- section 5 (id=3580, raw_sort=5): یقین کی روح -->

## The Spirit of Certainty

Then you say, "They rejoice because they are attached to the Spirit of Faith." Human beings mean by 'close relationship' or 'physical relationship' with something, and hence the word ⟪ar:'مباشرت'⟫ (direct contact; intimate association) in its derivation. It also carries another meaning: 'extreme happiness.' When a person touches the spirit of faith—that is, attains an immediate experiential knowledge of the Divine—the joy he receives cannot be expressed in words. That happiness transcends any other blessing of Paradise, for which Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 9:72⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَعَدَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَٱلْمُؤْمِنَتِ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ خَلِدِينَ فِيهَا وَمَسَكِنَ طَيِّبَةًۭ فِى جَنَّتِ عَدْنٍۢ ۚ وَرِضْوَنٌۭ مِّنَ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۚ ذَلِكَ هُوَ ٱلْفَوْزُ ٱلْعَظِيمُ ‎⟫
> *Allah has promised to the believers—men and women—Gardens beneath which rivers flow, wherein they shall dwell forever, and fair dwellings in Gardens of Eden. Yet greater still is Allah's good pleasure. That is the supreme triumph.*

Maulana Ali teaches that it is a blessing for the scholar to acquire knowledge and contemplate it. Allah Himself is One, and He has created every being uniquely. Each human possesses an irreplaceable identity that no other shares; he stands alone in this circle, his essence indivisible. Therefore, true knowledge of man is knowledge of his own self—a knowledge he cannot fully grasp.[^cite-17] This is why the Messenger of Allah (upon him be peace) declared: "Whoever knows his own soul, he knows his Lord."[^cite-18] In the early stages of knowledge-acquisition, a person's happiness resembles that of one returning from the exile of ignorance to the tranquility of home. The wisest is the most alive, and the most alive is nearest to Allah; life itself becomes joy. This happiness differs entirely from pleasures obtained through worldly means. Maulana Ali teaches that the true scholar ⟪ar:'فقیہ'⟫ (jurist; learned one) is he who does not despair of Allah's mercy. He remains ever immersed in the light of Divine mercy, and thus never experiences disappointment. He carries unshakeable confidence that whatever Allah ordains contains within it the fullness of His mercy. Allah says:

> ⟪quran 15:56⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قَالَ وَمَن يَقْنَطُ مِن رَّحْمَةِ رَبِّهِۦٓ إِلَّا ٱلضَّآلُّونَ ‎⟫
> *Said [Abraham]: "And who despairs of the mercy of his Lord except those who have gone astray?"*

> ⟪quran 6:54⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذَا جَآءَكَ ٱلَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِـَٔايَتِنَا فَقُلْ سَلَمٌ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ كَتَبَ رَبُّكُمْ عَلَىٰ نَفْسِهِ ٱلرَّحْمَةَ ۖ أَنَّهُۥ مَنْ عَمِلَ مِنكُمْ سُوٓءًۢا بِجَهَلَةٍۢ ثُمَّ تَابَ مِنۢ بَعْدِهِۦ وَأَصْلَحَ فَأَنَّهُۥ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *And when those who believe in Our signs come to you, say: "Peace be upon you. Your Lord has prescribed mercy upon Himself, so that if any of you commits evil in ignorance, then repents thereafter and makes amends, surely He is All-Forgiving, All-Merciful."*

The joy of Allah's mercy is, in fact, the definition of beauty ⟪ar:'أحسان'⟫ (excellence; beautiful conduct). This beauty differs fundamentally from aesthetic pleasure. It is true beauty—the imagination arising from intellect itself. The Arabic word for excellence carries also the meaning ⟪ar:حُسن⟫ (beauty), denoting those concepts that beautify the soul. Maulana Ali has taught that the excellence of the intellect lies in the capacity ⟪ar:ینظر جمال الظاہر والباطن⟫ to perceive beauty in all things, both outward and inward. The beauty of external forms and actions is completed by their inner beauty. Similarly, the beauty of deeds flows from the beauty or virtue of the soul. This is why the Prophet ⟪ar:محمد مصطفی صلی اللہ علیہ و آلہ و سلم⟫ (Muhammad the Chosen, upon him be peace and the peace of his family) taught: "Allah is beautiful and loves beautiful things."[^cite-19]

By instilling beautiful morals within oneself, a person becomes capable of loving Allah, for Allah loves those possessed of beauty. Because of these noble qualities, he became the most beloved servant of Allah, and he invited his Community to adopt the same sublime manners, saying:

> ⟪quran 3:31⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلْ إِن كُنتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ ٱللَّهَ فَٱتَّبِعُونِى يُحْبِبْكُمُ ٱللَّهُ وَيَغْفِرْ لَكُمْ ذُنُوبَكُمْ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *Say: "If you love Allah, then follow me, and Allah will love you and forgive you your sins. And Allah is All-Forgiving, All-Merciful."*

The Creator of the Universe explained this thus: "The foundation of intellect is love." To plant the seeds of love within the self and then express this love through action outwardly—so that it becomes the radiance of the exterior and the attraction of the interior.[^cite-20] Following the Messenger of Allah is the inculcation of his morals within oneself, for he alone attained their perfection. It is understood that the intellect's connection with Truth ⟪ar:'الحق'⟫ (Ultimate Reality) is established through the noblest morals—gentleness, contentment, gratitude, generosity, modesty, wisdom, forbearance—which are beautiful in themselves and also kindle love in both outer and inner dimensions. The true intellect embodies all these morals; without them, intellect cannot reach completion. Through these morals, one creates depth in spontaneous action and brings forth the hidden treasures of the intellect. Molding all these morals into one's soul and uniting them is, in a sense, an act of *tawhīd* ⟪ar:توحید⟫ (affirmation of Divine unity). Although truth touches the soul, morality must become the leaven for the intellect—so that it spreads through action and reaches perfection through the faculties of ⟪ar:بالفعل⟫ (actuality; in act) and ⟪ar:بالقوۃ⟫ (potentiality; in potency). Thus all immorality is not merely evil but a cause of intellectual diminishment. The heart grows sick, and the eye grows blind—unable any longer to perceive reality. As the Qur'an states:

> ⟪quran 2:10⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فِى قُلُوبِهِم مَّرَضٌۭ فَزَادَهُمُ ٱللَّهُ مَرَضًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌ أَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا كَانُوا۟ يَكْذِبُونَ ‎⟫
> *In their hearts is a disease, and Allah has increased their disease. And there awaits them a painful punishment for the lies they used to tell.*

> ⟪quran 22:46⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَلَمْ يَسِيرُوا۟ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ فَتَكُونَ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌۭ يَعْقِلُونَ بِهَآ أَوْ آذَانٌۭ يَسْمَعُونَ بِهَا ۖ فَإِنَّهَا لَا تَعْمَى ٱلْأَبْصَرُ وَلَكِن تَعْمَى ٱلْقُلُوبُ ٱلَّتِى فِى ٱلصُّدُورِ ‎⟫
> *Have they not journeyed through the earth, so that they might have hearts to understand with, or ears to hear with? It is not the eyes that grow blind, but it is the hearts within the breasts that grow blind.*

Maulana Ali teaches that he who masters his desires has prospered. Through this mastery, one feels the happiness born of certainty. And the spirit of this certainty arises from the union of sincere intention with the observance of Sacred Law. Without sincerity in acts of worship, there is only hypocrisy—which is *shirk*, a denial of unity. He said: "Know that even the slightest hypocrisy is *shirk*."[^cite-21] Allah clarifies this in the chapter that follows:

> ⟪quran 107:1-7⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَرَءَيْتَ ٱلَّذِى يُكَذِّبُ بِٱلدِّينِ ‎ ‏فَذَلِكَ ٱلَّذِى يَدُعُّ ٱلْيَتِيمَ ‎ ‏وَلَا يَحُضُّ عَلَىٰ طَعَامِ ٱلْمِسْكِينِ ‎ ‏فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْمُصَلِّينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَن صَلَاتِهِمْ سَاهُونَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ يُرَآءُونَ ‎ ‏وَيَمْنَعُونَ ٱلْمَاعُونَ ‎⟫
> *Have you seen him who denies the Recompense? That is he who repulses the orphan harshly, and urges not the feeding of the needy. Woe unto those performers of prayer who are heedless of their prayers, those who do good deeds only to be seen, and refuse kindness.*

This chapter shows that outward acts of worship hold no value unless joined with sincerity and a moral life. Without this inner depth, religion becomes hollow. An action infused with pure intention is a true action; all other outward deeds are mere dust, rising not in Allah's sight.

> ⟪quran 22:37⟫
> ⟪ar:‏لَن يَنَالَ ٱللَّهَ لُحُومُهَا وَلَا دِمَآؤُهَا وَلَكِن يَنَالُهُ ٱلتَّقْوَىٰ مِنكُمْ ۚ كَذَلِكَ سَخَّرَهَا لَكُمْ لِتُكَبِّرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ عَلَىٰ مَا هَدَىٰكُمْ ۗ وَبَشِّرِ ٱلْمُحْسِنِينَ ‎⟫
> *Their flesh reaches not Allah, nor their blood, but what reaches Him is your God-consciousness. Thus have We made them subject to you, that you may magnify Allah for having guided you. And give glad tidings to those who do good.*

Maulana Ali teaches: "He who lacks intellect has no religion." And: "The sleep of certainty is sweeter than the wakefulness of doubt." Such persons remain spiritually awake even in sleep. Thus the Messenger of Allah (upon him be peace) said: "My eyes sleep, but my heart remains awake."[^cite-22] The wise understand that although outward acts of worship are necessary in themselves, the blessings of Allah cannot be obtained through them alone. They require awareness—consciousness of what one does and why. This consciousness, united with moral beauty and inner refinement, attracts Allah's acceptance. Maulana Ali declared: "The finest knowledge for you is that which makes your deeds acceptable to Allah."

*Verses referenced in this section (curated from KASHKOLE):*

> ⟪quran 2:25⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَبَشِّرِ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ أَنَّ لَهُمْ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ ۖ كُلَّمَا رُزِقُوا۟ مِنْهَا مِن ثَمَرَةٍۢ رِّزْقًۭا ۙ قَالُوا۟ هَذَا ٱلَّذِى رُزِقْنَا مِن قَبْلُ ۖ وَأُتُوا۟ بِهِۦ مُتَشَبِهًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ فِيهَآ أَزْوَجٌۭ مُّطَهَّرَةٌۭ ۖ وَهُمْ فِيهَا خَلِدُونَ ‎⟫
> *And give glad tidings to those who believe and do righteous deeds, that for them are Gardens beneath which rivers flow; whenever they are provided with a fruit therefrom, they will say, "This is what we were provided with before," and they will be given fruits in resemblance. Therein they shall have purified spouses, and therein they shall abide eternally.*

> ⟪quran 38:46⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَخْلَصْنَهُم بِخَالِصَةٍۢ ذِكْرَى ٱلدَّارِ ‎⟫
> *Assuredly We chose them by granting them a singular blessing: the remembrance of the Hereafter.*

> ⟪quran 55:60⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هَلْ جَزَآءُ ٱلْإِحْسَنِ إِلَّا ٱلْإِحْسَنُ ‎⟫
> *Is there any recompense for excellence save excellence?*

> ⟪quran 87:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْآخِرَةُ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَبْقَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *Yet the Hereafter is better and more enduring.*

> ⟪quran 89:27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎⟫
> *O soul at peace and contentment!*

<!-- section 6 (id=3600, raw_sort=6): دنیا میں رہتے ہوئے آخرت کی زندگی -->

## Living the Life of the Hereafter While in This World

He then says: They are bound to this world through their bodies, yet their souls are joined to the Hereafter. This statement finds its parallel in another utterance of the Commander of the Faithful: he belonged to a people whose spiritual rank was such that their hearts dwelt in Paradise while their bodies labored in this world. Your assertion that hearts are 'settled' in heaven—that although they dwell in this world, they have reached the Hereafter spiritually, conceptually, and truly—confirms the saying of the Messenger of Allah (upon him be peace): "Allah keeps His servants in the state they desire."[^cite-23] Those who live oriented toward the upper realm ground themselves in the Hereafter. By contrast, the worldly person's every thought, imagination, and reflection remains imprisoned in this lower sphere. Each action bears the imprint of this inferior realm. Yet the wise structure every deed upon the reward awaiting in the Hereafter—understanding the profound truth that every act is dust except that which springs from sincerity and which Allah accepts.

Maulana Ali frequently speaks of Paradise's blessings and Hell's torments in his sermons. Does this suggest he has cast a mercenary hue over Allah's commands? Not at all. To know of Paradise and Hell differs vastly from understanding them. His aim is to kindle in the Community a consciousness through which morals may flourish. A merchant who trades seeks to gain; once the profit is secured, the object becomes useless. But will the attributes of piety, noble character, and abstinence from sin become worthless once Paradise is attained? Never. Rather, these very qualities shall constitute the atmosphere of Paradise itself. His mention of Paradise serves to inspire persons to prepare themselves in this world for that realm—to fashion themselves into fitting dwellers of it. In one sermon, he describes Paradise thus:

> If you turn your heart to the descriptions of Paradise, your soul will grow disgusted with the world's marvels, desires, pleasures, and charming vistas. She will be lost in contemplation of Paradise—of swaying streams on canal banks, of roots planted in musk-scented dunes, of branches hanging with glittering pearls.

The highest degree of certainty ⟪ar:'روحانیت'⟫ (spirituality; spiritual reality) transcends both desire for Paradise and fear of Hell. Yet when this spirituality is attained, the soul becomes celestial even while dwelling in mortality. And the state of the soul then becomes such that it finds satisfaction only in the overwhelming presence of its Lord, desiring nothing else. He names this condition with the Qur'anic term ⟪ar:'نفس المطمئنۃ'⟫ (the soul at peace):

> ⟪quran 89:27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎⟫
> *O soul at peace and contentment!*

The contentment of this soul derives from complete faith. This Qur'anic verse resonates throughout Maulana Ali's discourses:

> ⟪quran 87:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْآخِرَةُ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَبْقَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *Yet the Hereafter is better and more enduring.*

The Hereafter is not merely a 'time' when revelations are fulfilled and glad tidings materialize. It is a 'dwelling place' where all the highest attributes—earthly and divine—shall manifest, whose faintest reflection can be glimpsed in this world. By this measure, even the mention and conception of Paradise purifies the intellect and turns it from worldly desires and pleasures, as Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 38:46⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَخْلَصْنَهُم بِخَالِصَةٍۢ ذِكْرَى ٱلدَّارِ ‎⟫
> *Assuredly We chose them by granting them a singular blessing: the remembrance of the Hereafter.*

In other words, pure knowledge of the Hereafter creates the concept of becoming Paradise in this world—permitting one to cultivate the deeds and morals that are originally of the Hereafter, and thereby to attain happiness in both worlds. It has thus been proven that such moral qualities arise only in one whose eyes have been cleared of the veil that shrouds this world—who can see and feel the life of the Hereafter while inhabiting this mortal realm. That is, good deeds are not performed so that reward awaits in the Hereafter; rather, goodness itself constitutes part of that reward. Allah says:

> ⟪quran 55:60⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هَلْ جَزَآءُ ٱلْإِحْسَنِ إِلَّا ٱلْإِحْسَنُ ‎⟫
> *Is there any recompense for excellence save excellence?*

Maulana Ali teaches: "The fruit of any good deed resembles its root"—meaning that the end of any action lies in its beginning, in the intention. At this juncture, another Qur'anic verse becomes deeply relevant:

> ⟪quran 2:25⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَبَشِّرِ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ أَنَّ لَهُمْ جَنَّتٍۢ تَجْرِى مِن تَحْتِهَا ٱلْأَنْهَرُ ۖ كُلَّمَا رُزِقُوا۟ مِنْهَا مِن ثَمَرَةٍۢ رِّزْقًۭا ۙ قَالُوا۟ هَذَا ٱلَّذِى رُزِقْنَا مِن قَبْلُ ۖ وَأُتُوا۟ بِهِۦ مُتَشَبِهًۭا ۖ وَلَهُمْ فِيهَآ أَزْوَجٌۭ مُّطَهَّرَةٌۭ ۖ وَهُمْ فِيهَا خَلِدُونَ ‎⟫
> *And give glad tidings to those who believe and do righteous deeds, that for them are Gardens beneath which rivers flow; whenever they are provided with a fruit therefrom, they will say, "This is what we were provided with before," and they will be given fruits in resemblance. Therein they shall have purified spouses, and therein they shall abide eternally.*

The fruits of the Hereafter are tasted in this world as every kind of goodness, beauty, truth, and the joys that flow from them. All these flavors are of the real sustenance of the Hereafter, to be obtained in full in Paradise. In the realm of morality, good deeds and the consciousness of their necessity (benevolence) are essential not only for salvation but also for flourishing in this world. They liberate one outwardly from the bondage of sins and inwardly from the bondage of ego. This liberation has been the focus and purpose of all his teachings.

<!-- section 7 (id=3581, raw_sort=7): وہ چیز جو آسان بھی ہے اور مشکل بھی -->

## That Which Is Both Easy and Difficult

He said: "Those things are easy for them and difficult for the extravagant. They love that from which the ignorant feel estranged." This teaching describes an effect that rests perpetually on the hearts of Allah's saints. They continuously remember death and their meeting with Allah, and by His grace they renounce the world. What appears strange and alienating to the ignorant are the apparent hardships, trials, and deprivations of this life. The Qur'an speaks of them thus:

> ⟪quran 2:155-157⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَنَبْلُوَنَّكُم بِشَىْءٍۢ مِّنَ ٱلْخَوْفِ وَٱلْجُوعِ وَنَقْصٍۢ مِّنَ ٱلْأَمْوَلِ وَٱلْأَنفُسِ وَٱلثَّمَرَتِ ۗ وَبَشِّرِ ٱلصَّبِرِينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ إِذَآ أَصَبَتْهُم مُّصِيبَةٌۭ قَالُوٓا۟ إِنَّا لِلَّهِ وَإِنَّآ إِلَيْهِ رَجِعُونَ ‎ ‏أُو۟لَٓئِكَ عَلَيْهِمْ صَلَوَتٌۭ مِّن رَّبِّهِمْ وَرَحْمَةٌۭ ۖ وَأُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْمُهْتَدُونَ ‎⟫
> *And surely We shall test you with something of fear and hunger, and loss of wealth and lives and fruits; but give glad tidings to those who are patient. Who, when afflicted with calamity, say: "Surely we belong to Allah, and surely to Him we shall return." Upon such people are blessings from their Lord and mercy, and it is they who are rightly guided.*

These guided ones ⟪ar:مھتدون⟫ (the rightly guided) are patient amid adversity; they perceive and taste the blessings that patience yields, understanding this truth within their hearts:

> ⟪quran 103:1-3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلْعَصْرِ ‎ ‏إِنَّ ٱلْإِنسَنَ لَفِى خُسْرٍ ‎ ‏إِلَّا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ وَتَوَاصَوْا۟ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَتَوَاصَوْا۟ بِٱلصَّبْرِ ‎⟫
> *By time! Surely man is in loss, save those who have believed and done righteous deeds, and enjoined truth upon one another, and enjoined patience upon one another.*

These are believers steadfast in trial, conscious of their origin and their end, secure in Allah's word: "To Him we shall return." Because of this knowledge, worldly hardships become easy for them. The extravagant, by contrast, tastes only the bitterness and pain of suffering. The ease concealed within trial eludes his ignorance but stands obvious to the wise:

> ⟪quran 94:5-6⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَإِنَّ مَعَ ٱلْعُسْرِ يُسْرًا ‎ ‏إِنَّ مَعَ ٱلْعُسْرِ يُسْرًۭا ‎⟫
> *Surely with every hardship comes ease. Surely with every hardship comes ease.*

These wise ones not only perceive the fruit of ease that follows difficulty with their insight, but they taste it directly. They embrace suffering and trials as companions, while the ignorant feel estranged from them. Thus he declared: "Death is as dear to me as a mother's breast to an infant."[^cite-24] Yet he speaks of loving death while yet alive, as though he sees the reality of death and the blessings that follow it with his own eyes. He also said: "I am death's death!"[^cite-25] For in this life itself, life becomes a kind of death—a constraint and compulsion. Allah says:

> ⟪quran 29:64⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمَا هَذِهِ ٱلْحَيَوٰةُ ٱلدُّنْيَآ إِلَّا لَهْوٌۭ وَلَعِبٌۭ ۚ وَإِنَّ ٱلدَّارَ ٱلْآخِرَةَ لَهِىَ ٱلْحَيَوَانُ ۚ لَوْ كَانُوا۟ يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *And this worldly life is merely sport and pastime. Yet the Hereafter—that is the true life, if only they knew.*

### Asceticism

It must be noted here that the intent behind these sayings is not a rejection of the physical world itself, but a renunciation of 'worldliness'—the attachment ⟪ar:'أنا'⟫ (the ego; the 'I') connected to the world. He designates this state as ⟪ar:'زہد'⟫ (asceticism; detachment), and in the ⟪ar:نہج البلاغۃ⟫ (Path of Eloquence—the collected sermons of Amir al-Mu'minin) he describes it:

> This world is a place to which destruction has been ordained, and whose people are appointed for ruin. It is sweet and enticing; whoever sets out in pursuit of it, it comes running to him; whoever looks upon it settles it in his heart. Therefore, gather the finest provisions from it and leave. Do not ask for anything save what is most vital.

Elsewhere he states that true asceticism is ⟪ar:'تقوی'⟫ (God-consciousness; piety). For the next life, provisions are obtained in measure with one's detachment from the mortal things of this world.

> ⟪quran 17:18⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مَّن كَانَ يُرِيدُ ٱلْعَاجِلَةَ عَجَّلْنَا لَهُۥ فِيهَا مَا نَشَآءُ لِمَن نُّرِيدُ ثُمَّ جَعَلْنَا لَهُۥ جَهَنَّمَ يَصْلَىٰهَا مَذْمُومًۭا مَّدْحُورًۭا ‎⟫
> *Whoever desires the swift bounty of this world, We hasten for him therein what We will, for whom We wish. Then We have appointed Hell for him—he shall enter it, despised and rejected.*

The words of Maulana Ali fully express this contempt for worldliness:

> By Allah! In my sight, this world of yours is as vile as a pig's chewed bone held in the hand of a leper.
> The world is like a serpent—smooth to the touch, yet filled with deadly venom.
> To me, this world is like the substance that flows from a goat's nose.[^cite-26]

The greatness of Allah renders the world contemptible and base. When viewed in the light of the Absolute Real, all the world's pleasures appear fleeting and trivial. The smallness of His servants before His magnitude becomes evident. Maulana Ali praised a believer thus: "His contempt for the world's trivialities made him great in my eyes."[^cite-27] The world was not deemed worthless because it is useless, but because of Allah's magnificence, the Hereafter, and the absolute realities these servants beheld—and by virtue of that vision, the world became small in their eyes. For:

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other god alongside Allah. There is no god save He. All things shall perish save His Face. His is the command, and unto Him you shall be returned.*

The value of this world lies in this: that it contains creatures of Allah who glorify Him morning and evening, acknowledging His greatness:

> ⟪quran 17:44⟫
> ⟪ar:‏تُسَبِّحُ لَهُ ٱلسَّمَوَتُ ٱلسَّبْعُ وَٱلْأَرْضُ وَمَن فِيهِنَّ ۚ وَإِن مِّن شَىْءٍ إِلَّا يُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِهِۦ وَلَكِن لَّا تَفْقَهُونَ تَسْبِيحَهُمْ ۗ إِنَّهُۥ كَانَ حَلِيمًا غَفُورًۭا ‎⟫
> *The seven heavens and the earth and all that is therein glorify Him. There is not a thing but glorifies Him with His praise, yet you understand not their glorification. Surely He is All-Forbearing, All-Forgiving.*

> ⟪quran 24:41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ مَن فِى ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱلطَّيْرُ صَٓفَّتٍۢ ۖ كُلٌّۭ قَدْ عَلِمَ صَلَاتَهُۥ وَتَسْبِيحَهُۥ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ عَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا يَفْعَلُونَ ‎⟫
> *Do you not see that all those in the heavens and the earth glorify Allah, and the birds with outstretched wings? Each knows its prayer and its glorification, and Allah knows all that they do.*

Here emerges a subtle paradox: the world is in one sense a 'vile place,' yet in another a 'noble place' in which all the deeds for the Hereafter may be prepared. In his sermons, he praises Allah for the creation and artistry of nature—for peacocks, birds, even ants, dragons, and elephants. In another sermon, he uses the blessings of this world to illuminate those of the Hereafter: when the eye beholds Paradise's vistas, even the fairest scenes and most exquisite pleasures of this world become despicable to the soul. Because of this, all worldly hardships become easy for the believer—even a source of joy. The ascetics ⟪ar:زاہدین،⟫ furnished with these spiritual resources born of faith, endure every trial. They possess a knowledge that grants them such unwavering conviction that they declare: "Even if the veil were lifted, my certainty would not increase."[^cite-28]

In describing his sincerity, he said: "I bear witness that there is no god save Allah! The sincerity of my testimony has been tested, and its essence is woven with conviction." The Arabic word ⟪ar:'مصاص'⟫ (essence; the finest part) denotes that subtle element within any object that contains its quintessence. Just as the origin of any fruit is its juice—which one draws or sucks forth—so the sincerity of his testimony is ⟪ar:مُعتقدٌ مصاصُہُ⟫ the spiritual essence of the soul, not a notion arising from mere words or their outward meaning. The words themselves are merely echoes of the spiritual substance established within the heart.

He returns to the saying: "Those things are easy for them and difficult for the extravagant. They love that from which the ignorant feel estranged." In one sense it is 'trial,' in another it is 'death' itself. For the ignorant, death is a dreadful dissolution—separation from the body. For him, it marks life's end rather than its beginning. It is estrangement from the very thing that has been his focus and center throughout life. For the wise, by contrast, death means release from suffering and encounter with Allah; it is the completion of *tawhīd*—the merger into His transcendent realm, becoming 'one' ⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫ with Him. Only one who immerses himself in this ocean can taste its sweetness. The fire of this immersion burns all components to ash. Those enslaved to ego remain entangled in the external and internal aspects of their parts. But the wise one's attention is ever fixed on remembrance of the Absolute; the joy flowing from it displaces his ego and shatters all his illusions.

<!-- section 8 (id=3583, raw_sort=8): عدل کا فلسفہ -->

## The Philosophy of Justice

The finest exemplification of ⟪ar:أمیر المومنین⟫ (the Commander of the Faithful) K.K.'s philosophy of ⟪ar:'عدل'⟫ (justice; putting things in their rightful place) is found in the letter he composed to ⟪ar:'مالک اشتر بن الحارث النخئی'⟫ (Malik al-Ashtar ibn al-Harith al-Nakha'i), his commander and governor, when appointing him to the governorship of Egypt. In his view, the inclination of moral law toward justice extends beyond the external realm into the spiritual dimension. The principles of justice he outlined transcend the constraints of mere process. In his utterances, thought and action appear as complementary forces, manifesting ⟪ar:'توحید'⟫ (the affirmation of Divine unity). The lives of the Prophet (upon him be peace) and Ali (upon him be peace) exemplify these principles in living form.

Two facets emerge: first, ⟪ar:امیر المونین⟫ he himself was the perfect embodiment of justice; second, his justice rested upon profound spiritual foundations, revealing how a life devoted to love of Allah naturally flows into righteous living. A life that mirrors oneself in ⟪ar:'الحق'⟫ (Ultimate Reality) itself! Were we to examine ethics broadly, we would find that the integration of morality's dimensions and aspects creates a depth that molds both into a fundamental principle. The common questions of right and wrong then transform into the singular question: "What is Reality?"

Ali's spiritual understanding of *tawhīd* encompasses not merely that Allah has no equal, but that no power stands against Him. For this reason, every good deed ⟪ar:حَسَنَ⟫ (beautiful; fine) that stands as Allah's path is not the opposite of moral evil. It possesses its own individual, singular existence. In contrast to it, if anything exists, it is only ⟪ar:'عدم'⟫ (non-being; negation). Thus if good ⟪ar:الحق⟫ constitutes the positive aspect, evil becomes the 'potentiality' or 'intention' to negate goodness. In other words, if goodness is an attribute of the Creator, then evil is an attribute of the creation He has fashioned. Allah states:

> ⟪quran 113:2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مِن شَرِّ مَا خَلَقَ ‎⟫
> *From the evil of what He has created.*

This verse is often rendered erroneously as "the evil that Allah created"—a reading that is both theologically and linguistically unsound. Allah's statement makes clear that the 'evil' arose from the 'creation' He fashioned. That is: Allah created free creatures endowed with good qualities. Evil emerges when they negate these attributes through their own choice. Thus it cannot be said that God created evil; He created only those conditions permitting His creatures to choose, though they might have chosen Truth. This proves that evil is in fact nothing more than a negation of good—it possesses no independent existence. The verse may also be understood as seeking refuge in ⟪ar:‏مِن شَرِّ مَا خَلَقَ،⟫ Truth from falsehood. Evil appears only as the negation of Truth—what the eye of the heart perceives as 'illusion.' And just as reason can shatter every illusion, so Truth and goodness possess the power to overcome any evil. The more a soul stands before its Lord in uprightness, the more it shall overcome evil through the firmness of its will. This maturity moves from intellect to heart, convincing it that good is more 'true' than evil—a conviction strengthened by its knowledge that ⟪ar:'الحق'⟫ (truth; reality) is all-encompassing. Since evil does not exist—it being merely an object that has deviated from its position—there is a need to overcome it and restore it to Truth. Thus in the eyes of Amir al-Mu'minin, fulfilling obligations and securing rights for all (toward Allah, toward oneself, toward creation) constitutes the definition of justice. He points to this saying: "Justice is the placement of things in their proper stations."[^cite-29] The greater a person's actions remain in their rightful place, the more just he becomes. This essence of justice dwells in a person in measure with his relation to ⟪ar:'الحق'⟫ Reality. First, a person must *become* good; only then can he *do* good. And to be good is to become 'one'—⟪ar:توحید⟫ united in ⟪ar:الحق⟫ Reality—for He alone is One.

The letter to ⟪ar:مالک اشتر⟫ reveals that justice is not the name of any single attribute among all virtues, but rather the name of their sum and harmony—especially the three cardinal virtues of temperance, courage, and wisdom. When these three virtues occupy their proper stations, the soul itself may be called just.

Ethics and spirituality intertwine, as evidenced by a transmitted account: once, while the Messenger of Allah (upon him be peace and the peace of his family) sat with his companions, Gabriel (upon him be peace) came to him in human form and asked: ⟪ar:یا محمد (ﷺ)!⟫ "Tell me about ⟪ar:'اسلام'⟫ Islam." He replied: "It is to testify that there is no god save Allah and that Muhammad is His Messenger, and to establish prayer, give *zakat*, fast in Ramadan, and make pilgrimage to Allah's House." Gabriel said: "You have spoken truly!" Then he asked: "Tell me about ⟪ar:'ایمان'⟫ faith." He answered: "It is to believe in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, and the Day of Resurrection, and to believe in destiny—both its good and evil." Gabriel said: "You have spoken truly!" Then: "Tell me about ⟪ar:'أحسان'⟫ excellence."[^cite-30] He said: "It is to worship Allah as though you see Him; if you see Him not, yet know that He sees you."

The constant presence of Allah and the consciousness of standing in His sight runs through all these noble stations. The Prophet (upon him be peace) taught: "Worship Allah as though you see Him." The concept of *ihsan* (excellence) is thus rooted in Islam itself. Ali says in his sermons: "Know that every deed you perform depends upon your *niyyah* (intention)—upon how you regard goodness."[^cite-31] Yet he also declares: "Beware: pretense, arrogance, and self-magnification are Satan's finest snares, through which he destroys others."[^cite-32] The fundamental purpose of worship is the annihilation of one's self-will, egoism, and ⟪ar:أنانیت⟫ (selfhood; egotism) in the presence of Allah. Your first utterance calls for justice, which places all things—⟪ar:أنائیت⟫ including the ego—in their rightful stations. Your second utterance reveals the root of all injustice: ⟪ar:کبر⟫ (arrogance; pride), ⟪ar:حرس⟫ (envy; grudge), and what are called ⟪ar:'أمہات معاصی'⟫ (the mother-sins; the cardinal vices) and ⟪ar:حسد⟫ (jealousy; malice).


<!-- section 9 (id=3582, raw_sort=9): مالک اشتر کے نام خط -->

## Letter to Malik al-Ashtar

This is what Allah's servant ⟪ar:'Ali'⟫, Amir al-Mu'minin, has ordered Malik ibn al-Harith al-Ashtar in his instrument of appointment when he made him Governor of Egypt—for the collection of its revenues, the waging of jihad against its enemies, the restoration of its people, and the prosperity of its lands.

⟪ar-quote:هذَا مَا أَمَرَ بِهِ عَبْدُ اللهِ عَلِيٌ أَميِرُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ، مَالِكَ بْنَ الْحَارِثِ الاْشْتَرَ فِي عَهْدِهِ إِلَيْهِ، حِينَ وَلاَّهُ مِصْرَ- جِبْوةَ خَرَاجِهَا، وَجِهَادَ عَدُوِّهَا، وَاسْتِصْلاَحَ أَهْلِهَا، وَعِمَارَةَ بِلاَدِهَا⟫

He has ordered him to fear Allah—to prefer obedience to Him and to follow what He has commanded in His Book out of both obligatory duties and exemplary practices, for without adherence to them no one can prosper, nor can anyone descend into wretchedness save through their rejection and neglect. He commands further that Malik aid Allah the Glorified with his heart, hand, and tongue, for verily Allah takes upon Himself to aid those who aid Him and to grant glory to those who grant Him glory.[^cite-33] He also orders Malik to break his heart away from passions and to restrain it when desires surge forth, because the soul incites toward evil unless Allah grants it mercy.[^cite-34]

⟪ar-quote:أَمَرَهُ بِتَقْوَى اللهِ، وَإِيثَارِ طَاعَتِهِ، وَاتِّبَاعِ مَا أَمَرَ بِهِ فِي كِتَابِهِ- مِنْ فَرَائِضِهِ وَسُنَنِهِ، الَّتِي لاَ يَسْعَدُ أَحَدٌ إِلاَّ بِاتِّبَاعِهَا، وَلاَ يَشْقَى إِلاَّ مَعَ جُحُودِهَا وَإِضَاعَتِهَا، وَأَنْ يَنْصُرَ اللهَ سُبْحَانَهُ بَيَدِهِ وَقَلْبِهِ وَلِسَانِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ، جَلّ اسْمُهُ، قَدْ تَكَفَّلَ بِنَصْرِ مَنْ نَصَرَهُ، وَإِعَزَازِ مَنْ أَعَزَّهُ. وَأَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَكْسِرَ نَفْسَهُ عِنْدَ الشَّهَوَاتِ، وَيَزَعَهَا عِنْدَ الْجَمَحَاتِ، فَإِنَّ النَّفْسَ أَمَّارَةٌ بِالسُّوءِ، إِلاَّ مَا رَحِمَ اللهُ⟫

## The Qualifications of a Governor and His Responsibilities

Know, O Malik, that I have directed you to a land where governments have held sway before you—some marked by justice, others by oppression. Now the people will observe your conduct as you once observed the conduct of those rulers before you, and they will speak of you as you have spoken of them. Verily, the righteous are recognized through the repute that Allah establishes for them upon the tongues of His servants.[^cite-35] Therefore, let your most precious treasure be the treasury of righteous deeds. Master your desires and guard your soul from what is unlawful for you, for self-restraint means holding the heart at the midpoint between what it craves and what it abhors.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ اعْلَمْ يَا مَالكُ، أَنِّي قدْ وَجَّهْتُكَ إِلَى بِلاَد قَدْ جَرَتْ عَلَيْهَا دُوَلٌ قَبْلَكَ، مِنْ عَدْل وَجَوْر، وَأَنَّ النَّاسَ يَنْظُرُونَ مِنْ أُمُورِكَ فِى مِثْلِ مَا كُنْتَ تَنْظُرُ فِيهِ مِنْ أُمُورِ الْوُلاَةِ قَبْلَكَ، وَيَقُولُونَ فِيكَ مَا كُنْتَ تَقُولُ فِيهِمْ،إِنَّمَا يُسْتَدَلُّ عَلَى الصَّالِحِينَ بِمَا يُجْرِي اللهُ لَهُمْ عَلَى أَلْسُنِ عِبَادِهِ. فَلْيَكُنْ أَحَبَّ الذَّخَائِرِ إِلَيْكَ ذَخِيرَةُ الْعَمَلِ الصَّالِحِ، فَامْلِكْ هَوَاكَ، وَشُحَّ بِنَفْسِكَ عَمَّا لاَ يَحِلُّ لَكَ، فَإِنَّ الشُّحَّ بِالنَّفْسِ الاْنْصَافُ مِنْهَا فَيَما أَحْبَبْتَ وَكَرِهْتَ⟫

Cultivate mercy in your heart toward those under your care and affection and gentleness toward them. Do not stand over them like a ravenous beast, seeking merely to devour them. They are of two kinds: either brothers to you in faith or like you in creation. They slip and stumble; infirmity befalls them. Some act wrongly intentionally, others through negligence. Grant them your pardon and forbearance as you would wish Allah to grant you His pardon and forbearance. For you stand above them, your responsible Commander stands above you, and Allah stands above him who appointed you. He has entrusted you with their governance and tested you through them.[^cite-36]

⟪ar-quote:وَأَشْعِرْ قَلْبَكَ الرَّحْمَةَ لِلرَّعِيَّةِ، وَالْـمَحَبَّةَ لَهُمْ، وَاللُّطْفَ بِهِمْ، وَلاَ تَكُونَنَّ عَلَيْهِمْ سَبُعاً ضَارِياً تَغْتَنِمُ أَكْلَهُمْ، فَإِنَّهُمْ صِنْفَانِ- إِمَّا أَخٌ لَكَ فِي الدِّينِ، وَإمّا نَظِيرٌ لَكَ فِي الْخَلْقِ، يَفْرُطُ مِنْهُمُ الزَّلَلُ، وَتَعْرِضُ لَهُمُ الْعِلَلُ،يُؤْتَى عَلَى أَيْدِيهِمْ فِي الَعَمْدِ وَالْخَطَاَ، فَأَعْطِهِمْ مِنْ عَفْوِكَ وَصَفْحِكَ مِثْلَ الَّذِي تُحِبُّ أَنْ يُعْطِيَكَ اللهُ مِنْ عَفْوِهِ وَصَفْحِهِ، فَإِنَّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ، وَ وَالِي الاْمْرِ عَلَيْكَ فَوْقَكَ، وَاللهُ فَوْقَ مَنْ وَلاَّكَ! وَقَدِ اسْتَكْفَاكَ أَمْرَهُمْ، وَابْتَلاَكَ بِهِمْ⟫

Do not contend against Allah, for you have no strength against His might, and you cannot dispense with His pardon and mercy. Do not repent of clemency, nor glory in punishment hastily. Do not rush to consequences when you can find an alternative. Never declare, "I have been invested with authority, and my command must be obeyed"—for such words breed corruption in the heart, undermine religion, and lead toward ruin. Should your station breed pride or vanity, then contemplate the greatness of Allah's dominion above you and His power, over which you have no mastery even concerning your own self. This reflection will humble your ambition, cure your arrogance, and restore the wisdom that has abandoned you.[^cite-37]

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تَنْصِبَنَّ نَفْسَكَ لِحَرْبِ اللهِ، فَإِنَّهْ لاَيَدَيْ لَكَ بِنِقْمَتِهِ، وَلاَ غِنَى بِكَ عَنْ عَفْوِهِ وَرَحْمَتِهِ. وَلاَ تَنْدَمَنَّ عَلَى عَفْو، وَلاَ تَبْجَحَنَّ بِعُقُوبَة، وَلاَ تُسْرِعَنَّ إِلَى بَادِرَة وَجَدْتَ مِنْهَا مَنْدُوحَةً، وَلاَ تَقُولَنَّ- إِنِّي مُؤَمَّرٌ آمُرُ فَأُطَاعُ، فَإِنَّ ذلِكَ إِدْغَالٌ فِي الْقَلْبِ، وَمَنْهَكَةٌ لِلدِّينِ، وَتَقَرُّبٌ مِنَ الْغِيَرِ. وَإِذَا أَحْدَثَ لَكَ مَا أَنْتَ فِيهِ مِنْ سُلْطَانِكَ أُبَّهَةً أَوْ مَخِيلَةً، فَانْظُرْ إِلَى عِظَمِ مُلْكِ اللهِ فَوْقَكَ، وَقُدْرَتِهِ مَنْكَ عَلَى مَا لاَ تَقْدرِ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ نَفْسِكَ، فَإِنَّ ذلِكَ يُطَامِنُ إِلَيْكَ مِنْ طِمَاحِكَ، وَيَكُفُّ عَنْكَ مِنْ غَرْبِكَ،يَفِيءُ إِلَيْكَ بِمَا عَزَبَ عَنْكَ مِنْ عَقْلِكَ⟫

Beware of likening yourself to Allah in His majesty or of emulating Him in His sovereignty, for Allah humbles every tyrant and disgraces all the haughty.

⟪ar-quote:إِيَّاكَ وَمُسَامَاةَ اللهِ فِي عَظَمَتِهِ، وَالتَّشَبُّهَ بِهِ فِي جَبَرُوتِهِ، فَإِنَّ اللهَ يُذِلُّ كُلَّ جَبَّار، وَيُهِينُ كُلَّ مُخْتَال⟫

Render justice to Allah and render justice to the people against yourself, against your kin, and against those among your subjects for whom you harbor affection. For if you fail to do so, you become an oppressor. And whoever oppresses the servants of Allah becomes Allah's adversary—placed in opposition to His creatures. When Allah becomes one's adversary, His proof against him is crushed, and he remains at war with Allah until he desists and repents. Nothing hastens the reversal of Allah's favor or the acceleration of His punishment more than persistence in oppression, for Allah hears the prayer of the wronged and lies in wait for the oppressors.[^cite-38]

⟪ar-quote:أَنْصِفِ اللهَ وَأَنْصِفِ النَّاسَ مِنْ نَفْسِكَ، وَمِنْ خَاصَّةِ أَهْلِكَ، وَمَنْ لَكَ فِيهِ هَوىً مِنْ رَعِيَّتِكَ، فَإِنَّكَ إِلاَّ تَفْعَلْ تَظْلِمْ، وَمَنْ ظَلَمَ عِبَادَ اللهِ كَانَ اللهُ خَصْمَهُ دُونَ عِبَادِهِ، وَمَنْ خَاصَمَهُ اللهُ أَدْحَضَ حُجَّتَهُ، وَكَانَ لله حَرْباً حَتَّى يَنْزعَ وَيَتُوبَ. وَلَيْسَ شَيْءٌ أَدْعَى إِلَى تَغْيِيرِ نِعْمَةِ اللهِ وَتَعْجِيلِ نِقْمَتِهِ مِنْ إِقَامَة عَلَى ظُلْم، فَإِنَّ اللهَ سَميِعٌ دَعْوَةَ الْمَظْلُومِينَ، وَهُوَ لِلظَّالِمِينَ بِالْمِرْصَادِ⟫

Let the course you favor be that which is most equitable in truth, most comprehensive in justice, and most unifying in winning the approval of your subjects. For the displeasure of the common people overwhelms the pleasure of the elite, whereas the displeasure of the elite can be borne when the common people are content. None among your subjects bears a heavier burden upon the ruler in times of prosperity, offers less assistance in times of hardship, is more averse to just treatment, more importunate in requests, less grateful upon receiving, slower to excuse upon refusal, and more fragile in enduring life's afflictions than the elite. The common people form the pillar of the faith, the cohesion of the Muslims, and the defense against enemies. Your inclination and concern must therefore be toward them.[^cite-39]
