⟪ar-quote:كُنْ أَحَبَّ الاْمُورِ إِلَيْكَ أَوْسَطُهَا فِي الْحَقِّ، وَأَعَمُّهَا فِي الْعَدْلِ، وَأَجْمَعُهَا لِرِضَى الرَّعِيَّةِ، فَإِنَّ سُخْطَ الْعَامَّةِ يُجْحِفُ بِرِضَى الْخَاصَّةِ، وَإِنَّ سُخْطَ الْخَاصَّةِ يُغْتَفَرُ مَعَ رِضَى الْعَامَّةِ. وَلَيْسَ أَحَدٌ مِنَ الرَّعِيَّةِ، أَثْقَلَ عَلَى الْوَالِي مَؤُونَةً فِي الرَّخَاءِ، وَأَقَلَّ مَعُونَةً لَهُ فِي الْبَلاَءِ، وَأَكْرَهَ لِلاْنْصَافِ، وَأَسْأَلَ بِالاْلْحَافِ، وَأَقَلَّ شُكْراً عِنْدَ الاْعْطَاءِ، وَأَبْطَأَ عُذْراً عِنْدَ الْمَنْعِ، وَأَضْعَفَ صَبْراً عِنْدَ مُلِمَّاتِ الدَّهْرِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْخَاصَّةِ، وَإِنَّمَا عَمُودُ الدِّينِ، وَجِمَاعُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ، وَالْعُدَّةُ لِلاْعْدَاءِ، الْعَامَّةُ مِنَ الاْمَّةِ، فَلْيَكُنْ صِغْوُكَ لَهُمْ، وَمَيْلُكَ مَعَهُمْ⟫

Among your subjects, those most distant from you and most odious should be those most inquisitive of others' faults. For all people have defects, and the ruler is most fit to conceal them. Do not expose what remains hidden from you, for your duty is to remedy what appears before you, while Allah judges what is concealed. Cover the faults as best you can, so that Allah may cover from your subjects what you would wish concealed. Loose every bond of hatred among the people and sever yourself from every cause of enmity. Feign ignorance of what is ambiguous to you. Do not hasten to credit a backbiter, for the backbiter is a deceiver even though he wears the garb of the well-wisher.[^cite-40]

⟪ar-quote:وَلْيَكُنْ أَبْعَدَ رَعِيَّتِكَ مِنْكَ، وَأشْنَأَهُمْ عِنْدَكَ، أَطْلَبُهُمْ لِمَعَائِبِ النَّاسِ، فإنَّ في النَّاسِ عُيُوباً، الْوَالِي أَحَقُّ مَنْ سَتَرَهَا، فَلاَ تَكْشِفَنَّ عَمَّا غَابَ عَنْكَ مِنْهَا، فَإنَّمَا عَلَيْكَ تَطْهِيرُ مَا ظَهَرَ لَكَ، وَاللهُ يَحْكُمُ عَلَى مَا غَابَ عَنْكَ، فَاسْتُرِ الْعَوْرَةَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتَ يَسْتُرِ اللهُ مِنْكَ ما تُحِبُّ سَتْرَهُ مِنْ رَعِيَّتِكَ. أَطْلِقْ عَنِ النَّاسِ عُقْدَةَ كُلِّ حِقْد، وَاقْطَعْ عَنْكَ سَبَبَ كُلِّ وِتْر، وَتَغَابَ عَنْ كلِّ مَا لاَ يَضِحُ لَكَ، وَلاَ تَعْجَلَنَّ إِلَى تَصْدِيقِ سَاع، فَإِنَّ السَّاعِيَ غَاشٌ،⟫

Do not admit into your counsel a miser who would turn you from liberality and warn you of poverty, nor a coward who would weaken you in your affairs, nor a greedy person who would embellish for you the accumulation of wealth through wrongdoing. For miserliness, cowardice, and avarice are disparate qualities united only by a corrupted estimate of Allah.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تُدْخِلَنَّ فِي مَشُورَتِكَ بَخِيلاً يَعْدِلُ بِكَ عَنِ الْفَضْلِ، وَيَعِدُكَ الْفَقْرَ، وَلاَ جَبَاناً يُضعِّفُكَ عَنِ الاْمُورِ، وَلاَ حَرِيصاً يُزَيِّنُ لَكَ الشَّرَهَ بِالْجَوْرِ، فَإِنَّ الْبُخْلَ وَالْجُبْنَ وَالْحِرْصَ غَرَائِزُ شَتَّى يَجْمَعُهَا سُوءُ الظَّنِّ بِاللهِ⟫

The worst of your counselors are those who were counselors to the wicked before you and who shared in their sins. Such men should not be your intimates, for they are abettors of transgressors and brothers of the oppressors. Rather, seek their worthy successors—those possessed of similar judgment and acumen yet free from their vice and transgression, who never aided an oppressor in his wrong nor a sinner in his sin. These require less of you and render you greater service; they are more considerate of your interests and less inclined toward others. Make them your close companions in private and in public.[^cite-41]

⟪ar-quote:شَرُّ وُزَرَائِكَ مَنْ كَانَ لِلاْشْرَارِ قَبْلَكَ وَزِيراً، وَمَنْ شَرِكَهُمْ فِي الاْثَامِ، فَلاَ يَكُونَنَّ لَكَ بِطَانَةً، فَإِنَّهُمْ أَعْوَانُ الاْثَمَةِ، وَإِخْوَانُ الظَّلَمَةِ، وَأَنْتَ وَاجِدٌ مِنْهُمْ خَيْرَ الْخَلَفِ مِمَّنْ لَهُ مِثْلُ آرَائِهِمْ وَنَفَاذِهِمْ، وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ مِثْلُ آصَارِهِمْ وَأَوْزَارِهِمْ وَ آثَامِهِمْ، مِمَّنْ لَمْ يُعَاوِنْ ظَالِماً عَلَى ظُلْمِهِ، وَلاَ آثِماً عَلَى إِثْمِهِ، أُولئِكَ أَخَفُّ عَلَيْكَ مَؤُونَةً، وَأَحْسَنُ لَكَ مَعُونَةً، وَأَحْنَى عَلَيْكَ عَطْفاً، وَأَقَلُّ لِغَيْرِكَ إِلْفاً، فَاتَّخِذْ أُولئِكَ خَاصَّةً لِخَلَوَاتِكَ وَحَفَلاَتِكَ⟫

Among these, most worthy of your regard are those who speak hard truths before you and least support your actions that Allah disapproves in His friends, regardless of your inclination toward them. Attach yourself to the God-fearing and truthful; then train them not to flatter you or to please you with false praise for deeds you have not performed, for excess of flattery breeds arrogance and draws you close to haughtiness.[^cite-42]

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ لْيَكُنْ آثَرُهُمْ عِنْدَكَ أَقْوَلَهُمْ بِمُرِّ الْحَقِّ لَكَ، وأَقَلَّهُمْ مُسَاعَدَةً فِيَما يَكُونُ مِنْكَ مِمَّا كَرِهَ اللهُ لاِوْلِيَائِهِ، وَاقِعاً ذلِكَ مِنْ هَوَاكَ حَيْثُ وَقَعَ. وَالْصَقْ بِأَهْلِ الْوَرَعِ وَالصِّدْقِ، ثُمَّ رُضْهُمْ عَلَى أَلاَّ يُطْرُوكَ وَلاَ يُبَجِّحُوكَ بِبَاطِل لَمْ تَفْعَلْهُ، فَإِنَّ كَثْرَةَ الاْطْرَاءِ تُحْدِثُ الزَّهْوَ، وَتُدْنِي مِنَ الْعِزَّةِ⟫

Let not the doer of good and the doer of wrong occupy equal standing before you, for this discourages the virtuous from virtue and encourages the wicked in wickedness. Fix each in the rank that their deeds assign them. Know that nothing more surely secures the favor of a ruler's subjects than his kindness to them, the easing of their burdens, and his refusal to impose unbearable trials upon them. Cultivate such conduct so that your subjects hold you in good regard; indeed, such esteem relieves you of great fatigue. The one most entitled to your favorable opinion is he to whom you have shown kindness, and the one most entitled to your ill opinion is he toward whom you have shown severity.[^cite-43]

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ يَكُونَنَّ الْـمُحْسِنُ وَالْمُسِيءُ عِنْدَكَ بِمَنْزِلَة سَوَاء، فَإِنَّ فِي ذلِكَ تَزْهِيداً لاِهْلِ الاْحْسَانِ فِي الاْحْسَانِ،تَدْرِيباً لاِهْلِ الاْسَاءَةِ عَلَى الاْسَاءَةِ، وَأَلْزِمْ كُلاًّ مِنْهُمْ مَا أَلْزَمَ نَفْسَهُ. وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ شَيْءٌ بِأَدْعَى إِلَى حُسْنِ ظَنِّ وَال بِرَعِيَّتِهِ مِنْ إحْسَانِهِ إِلَيْهِمْ، وَتَخْفِيفِهِ الْمُؤُونَاتِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَتَرْكِ اسْتِكْرَاهِهِ إِيَّاهُمْ عَلَى مَا لَيْسَ لهُ قِبَلَهُمْ، فَلْيَكُنْ مِنْكَ فِي ذلِكَ أَمْرٌ يَجَتَمِعُ لَكَ بِهِ حُسْنُ الظَّنِّ بِرَعِيَّتِكَ، فَإِنَّ حُسْنَ الظَّنِّ يَقْطَعُ عَنْكَ نَصَباً طَوِيلاً، وَإِنَّ أَحَقَّ مَنْ حَسُنَ ظَنُّكَ بِهِ لَمَنْ حَسُنَ بَلاَؤُكَ عِنْدَهُ، وَإِنَّ أَحَقَّ مَنْ سَاءَ ظَنُّكَ بِهِ لَمَنْ سَاءَ بَلاَؤُكَ عِنْدَهُ⟫

Do not overturn righteous precedents which have been established by the foregoing generations of this community—through which concord was achieved and the people prospered. Innovate no ruling that injures these established traditions, for the reward accrues to those who first established them, while the burden of undoing them falls upon you. Increase your study with the learned and your deliberation with the wise, so as to strengthen governance in your lands and ensure continuity of what your predecessors have established.[^cite-44]

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تَنْقُضْ سُنَّةً صَالِحَةً عَمِلَ بِهَا صُدُورُ هذِهِ الاْمَّةِ، وَاجْتَمَعتْ بِهَا الاْلْفَةُ، وَصَلَحَتْ عَلَيْهَا الرَّعِيَّةُ،لاَ تُحْدِثَنَّ سُنَّةً تَضُرُّ بِشَيء مِنْ مَاضِي تِلْكَ السُّنَنِ، فَيَكُونَ الاْجْرُ بِمَنْ سَنَّهَا، وَالْوِزْرُ عَلَيْكَ بِمَا نَقَضْتَ مِنْهَا. وَأَكْثِرْ مُدَارَسَةَ الَعُلَمَاءِ، وَمُنَافَثَةَ الْحُكَمَاءِ، فِي تَثْبِيتِ مَا صَلَحَ عَلَيْهِ أَمْرُ بِلاَدِكَ،⟫

Understand that the people form classes that cannot subsist without one another, nor is any class independent. Among them are Allah's soldiers, then the secretaries of the elite and the masses, then judges of justice, then administrators of fairness and mercy, then the payers of jizya and kharāj (poll tax and land tax) from the protected peoples and Muslims, then merchants and artisans, and finally the lowest class of the needy and destitute. Allah has fixed the share of each and established His ordinances regarding the bounds and duties of each in His Book and in the Sunna of His Prophet, a covenant preserved with us.[^cite-45]

⟪ar-quote:وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الرَّعِيَّةَ طَبَقَاتٌ لاَ يَصْلُحُ بَعْضُهَا إلاَّ بِبَعْض، وَلاَ غِنَى بِبَعْضِهَا عَنْ بَعْض- فَمِنْهَا جُنُودُ اللهِ،مِنْهَا كُتَّابُ الْعَامَّةِ وَالْخَاصَّةِ، وَمِنْهَا قُضَاةُ الْعَدْلِ، وَمِنهَا عُمَّالُ الاْنْصَافِ وَالرِّفْقِ، وَمِنْهَا أَهْلُ الْجِزْيَةِ وَالْخَراجِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الذِّمَّةِ وَمُسْلِمَةِ النَّاسِ، وَمِنْهَا التُّجَّارُ وَأَهْلُ الصِّنَاعَاتِ، وَمِنهَا الطَّبَقَةُ السُّفْلَى مِنْ ذَوِي الْحَاجَةِ وَالْمَسْكَنَةِ، وَكُلٌّ قَدْ سَمَّى اللهُ سَهْمَهُ، وَوَضَعَ عَلَى حَدِّهِ وَفَرِيضَتِهِ فِي كِتَابِهِ أَوْ سُنَّةِ نَبِيِّهِ (صلى الله عليه وآله)عَهْداً مِنْهُ عِنْدَنَا مَحْفُوظاً⟫

The army forms, by Allah's will, the fortress of the subjects, the ornament of the ruler, the glory of the faith, and the means of security. The subjects cannot survive without them, yet the army cannot endure save through the revenues that Allah has ordained for them. Through these they gain strength to fight enemies, attain prosperity, and meet their needs. Neither of these two classes can exist without the third: the judges, administrators, and secretaries who seal contracts, gather revenues, and are depended upon in both particular and general matters.

⟪ar-quote:فَالْجُنُودُ، بِإِذْنِ اللهِ، حُصُونُ الرَّعِيَّةِ، وَزَيْنُ الْوُلاَةِ، وعِزُّ الدِّينِ، وَسُبُلُ الاْمْنِ، وَلَيْسَ تَقُومُ الرَّعِيَّةُ إِلاَّ بِهِمْ. ثُمَّ لاَ قِوَامَ لِلْجُنُودِ إِلاَّ بِمَا يُخْرِجُ اللهُ لَهُمْ مِنَ الْخَرَاجِ الَّذِي يَقْوَوْنَ بِهِ فِي جِهَادِ عَدُوِهِمْ، وَيَعْتَمِدُونَ عَلَيْهِ فِيَما أصْلَحهُمْ، وَيَكُونُ مِنْ وَرَاءِ حَاجَتِهِمْ. ثُمَّ لاَ قِوَامَ لِهذَيْنِ الصِّنْفَيْنِ إِلاَّ بِالصِّنْفِ الثَّالِثِ مِنَ الْقُضَاةِ وَالْعُمَّالِ وَالْكُتَّابِ، لِمَا يُحْكِمُونَ مِنَ الْمَعَاقِدِ، وَيَجْمَعُونَ مِنَ الْمَنَافِعِ، وَيُؤْتَمَنُونَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ خَوَاصِّ الاْمُورِ وَعَوَامِّهَا⟫

All classes together cannot exist save through traders and craftsmen who supply them with necessities, establish markets, and free them from the burden of self-provision. Last comes the lowest class of the needy and destitute, whose support and assistance is a binding obligation, for Allah has made ample provision for each. Every person has a right upon the ruler according to what benefits his condition. The ruler cannot fulfill his obligations to Allah in this matter save through diligence, through seeking Allah's help, through steadying himself upon the right, and through enduring whatever burden befalls him, light or heavy.[^cite-46]

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ قِوَامَ لَهُمْ جَمِيعاً إِلاَّ بِالتُّجَّارِ وَذَوِي الصِّنَاعَاتِ، فِيَما يَجْتَمِعُونَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ مَرَافِقِهِمْ، وَيُقِيمُونَهُ مِنْ أَسْوَاقِهِمْ، وَيَكْفُونَهُمْ مِنَ التَّرَفُّقِ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ ممّا لاَ يَبْلُغُهُ رِفْقُ غَيْرِهِمْ. ثُمَّ الطَّبَقَةُ السُّفْلَى مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَاجَةِ وَالْمَسْكَنَةِ الَّذِينَ يَحِقُّ رِفْدُهُمْ وَمَعُونَتُهُمْ. وَفِي اللهِ لِكُلّ سَعَةٌ، وَلِكُلٍّ عَلَى الْوَالِي حَقٌ بِقَدْرِ مَا يُصْلِحُهُ. وَلَيْسَ يَخْرُجُ الْوَالِي مِنْ حَقِيقَةِ مَا أَلْزَمَهُ اللهُ مِنْ ذلِكَ إِلاَّ بِالاْهْتِمامِ وَالاسْتِعَانَةِ بِاللهِ، وَتَوْطِينِ نَفْسِهِ عَلَى لُزُومِ الْحَقِّ، وَالصَّبْرِ عَلَيْهِ فِيَما خَفَّ عَلَيْهِ أَوْ ثَقُلَ⟫

## The Army

Invest command of your forces in one who is, in your view, most sincere in his devotion to Allah, His Messenger, and your Imam. Seek a commander pure in heart and preeminent in forbearance—one who is slow to anger, disposed to excuse, compassionate toward the weak, and severe with the strong; one upon whom neither violence inflames nor weakness sits paralyzed.

⟪ar-quote:فَوَلِّ مِنْ جُنُودِكَ أَنْصَحَهُمْ فِي نَفْسِكَ لله وَلِرَسُولِهِ وَلاِمَامِكَ، وَأَنْقَاهُمْ جَيْباً، وَأَفْضَلَهُمْ حِلْماً مِمَّنْ يُبْطِىءُ عَنِ الْغَضَبِ، وَيَسْتَرِيحُ إِلَى الْعُذْرِ، وَيَرْأَفُ بِالضُّعَفَاءِ، وَيَنْبُو عَلَى الاْقْوِيَاءِ، وَمِمَّنْ لاَ يُثِيرُهُ الْعُنْفُ، وَلاَ يَقْعُدُ بِهِ الضَّعْفُ⟫

Gather around yourself those of noble lineage and virtuous households, men of sound precedent and then those renowned for courage, valor, generosity, and clemency—for these are the repositories of honor and the wellspring of virtue. Attend to their affairs as parents attend to their children. Do not regard the strengthening of them as arduous, nor count any kindness shown them as insignificant, even if it be small; for such compassion becomes an invitation to their sincere counsel and fosters their good opinion of you. Do not neglect their small needs for the sake of attending to greater ones, for their small favors benefit them, while the great ones they cannot forsake.[^cite-47]

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ الْصَقْ بَذَوِي الْمُرُوءَاتِ وَالاْحْسَابِ، وَأَهْلِ الْبُيُوتَاتِ الصَّالِحَةِ، وَالسَّوَابِقِ الْحَسَنَةِ، ثُمَّ أَهْلِ النَّجْدَةِ وَالشَّجَاعَةِ، وَالسَّخَاءِ وَالسَّماحَةِ، فَإِنَّهُمْ جِمَاعٌ مِنَ الْكَرَمِ، وَشُعَبٌ مِنَ الْعُرْفِ. ثُمَّ تَفَقَّدْ مِنْ أُمُورِهِمْ مَا يَتَفَقَّدُهُ الْوَالِدَانِ مِنْ وَلَدِهِمَا، وَلاَ يَتَفَاقَمَنَّ فِي نَفْسِكَ شَيْءٌ قَوَّيْتَهُمْ بِهِ، وَلاَ تَحْقِرَنَّ لُطْفاً تَعَاهَدْتَهُمْ بِهِ وَإِنْ قَلَّ، فَإِنَّهُ دَاعِيَةٌ لَهُمْ إِلَى بَذْلِ النَّصِيحَةِ لَكَ، وَحُسْنِ الظَّنِّ بِكَ. وَلاَ تَدَعْ تَفَقُّدَ لَطيِفِ أُمُورِهِمُ اتِّكَالاً عَلَى جَسِيمِهَا، فَإِنَّ لِلْيَسِيرِ مِنْ لُطْفِكَ مَوْضِعاً يَنْتَفِعُونَ بِهِ، وَلِلْجَسِيمِ مَوْقِعاً لاَ يَسْتَغْنُونَ عَنْهُ.⟫

Your military commander should hold such standing with you that he distributes support justly, expends from his own wealth for them and for their families left behind, so that their concern converges into one: the struggle against the enemy. Your kindness toward them will turn their hearts to you. The most pleasant sight for rulers is the establishment of justice throughout their lands and the manifestation of their subjects' affection, yet affection manifests only when hearts are purified. True counsel reveals itself only through their protection of their commanders and through the lightness they feel in their governors' tenure, never watching for its end. Therefore, expand their hopes, continue praising their virtues, and recount the deeds of those who have shown excellence. For recounting noble deeds stirs the brave and rouses the sluggard, if Allah wills.[^cite-48]

⟪ar-quote:وَلْيَكُنْ آثَرُ رُؤوسِ جُنْدِكَ عِنْدَكَ مَنْ وَاسَاهُمْ فِي مَعُونَتِهِ، وَأَفْضَلَ عَلَيْهِمْ مِنْ جِدَتِهِ بِمَا يَسَعُهُمْ يَسَعُ مَنْ وَرَاءَهُمْ مِنْ خُلُوفِ أَهْلِيهِمْ حَتَّى يَكُونَ هَمُّهُمْ هَمّاً وَاحِداً فِي جِهَادِ الْعَدُوِّ، فَإِنَّ عَطْفَكَ عَلَيْهِمْ يَعْطِفُ قُلُوبَهُمْ عَلَيْكَ. وَإِنَّ أَفْضَلَ قُرَّةِ عَيْنِ الْوُلاَةِ اسْتِقَامَةُ الْعَدْلِ فِي الْبِلاَدِ، وَظُهُورُ مَوَدَّةِ الرَّعِيَّةِ، وَإِنَّهُ لاَ تَظْهَرُ مَوَدَّتُهُمْ إِلاَّ بَسَلاَمَةِ صُدُورِهِمْ، وَلاَ تَصِحُّ نَصِيحَتُهُمْ إِلاّ بِحِيطَتِهِمْ عَلَى وُلاَةِ أُمُورِهِمْ، وَقِلَّةِ اسْتِثْقَالِ دُوَلِهِمْ، وَتَرْكِ اسْتِبْطَاءِ انْقِطَاعِ مُدَّتِهِمْ. فَافْسَحْ فِي آمَالِهِمْ، وَوَاصِلْ فِي حُسْنِ الثَّنَاءِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَتَعْدِيدِ مَا أَبْلى ذَوُوالْبَلاَءِ مِنْهُمْ، فَإِنَّ كَثْرَةَ الذِّكْرِ لِحُسْنِ أَفْعَالِهِمْ تَهُزُّ الشُّجَاعَ، وَتُحَرِّضُ النَّاكِلَ، إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ⟫

Recognize the service of each; do not transfer the achievement of one to another, nor diminish reward below the measure of performance. Do not allow the high rank of a man to magnify his small deeds, nor his low station to belittle his great ones.[^cite-49]

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ اعْرِفْ لِكُلِّ امْرِىء مِنْهُمْ مَا أَبْلى، وَلاَ تَضُمَّنَّ بَلاَءَ امْرِىء إِلَى غَيْرِهِ، وَلاَ تُقَصِّرَنَّ بِهِ دُونَ غَايَةِ بَلاَئِهِ، وَلاَ يَدْعُوَنَّكَ شَرَفُ امْرِىء إِلَى أَنْ تُعْظِمَ مِنْ بَلاَئِهِ مَا كَانَ صَغِيراً، وَلاَضَعَةُ امْرِىء إِلَى أَنْ تَسْتَصْغِرَ مِنْ يَلاَئِهِ مَاكَانَ عَظيِماً⟫

Refer to Allah and His Messenger those matters that trouble you and those that appear unclear. For Allah has addressed those whom He wishes to guide, saying:

> ⟪quran 4:59⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوٓا۟ أَطِيعُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ وَأَطِيعُوا۟ ٱلرَّسُولَ وَأُو۟لِى ٱلْأَمْرِ مِنكُمْ ۖ فَإِن تَنَزَعْتُمْ فِى شَىْءٍۢ فَرُدُّوهُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِ وَٱلرَّسُولِ إِن كُنتُمْ تُؤْمِنُونَ بِٱللَّهِ وَٱلْيَوْمِ ٱلْآخِرِ ۚ ذَلِكَ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَحْسَنُ تَأْوِيلًا ‎⟫
> *"O you who believe! Obey Allah and obey the Messenger and those of you who are in authority. And if you dispute over anything, refer it to Allah and His Messenger, if you believe in Allah and the Last Day. That is better and more suitable for final determination."*

<!-- section 11 (id=3594, raw_sort=11): عدل اور ظلم -->

## Justice and Tyranny

Justice in all its dimensions finds its source in piety and righteousness ⟪ar:'صالح'⟫. The principle cannot be separated from the person. A just ruler cannot exist without righteous subjects, nor can subjects be righteous if their ruler lacks righteousness. When subjects fulfill their obligations to the ruler and the ruler fulfills his obligations to them, then truth becomes manifest, religion flourishes, and the standards of justice become established. This is why Ali places such insistent emphasis on the piety of the governor.

Examine the life of Amir al-Mu'minin himself: his entire conduct has been governed by these divine ordinances. When his caliphate was established following the death of ⟪ar:ابن عباس⟫'Uthman, the crucial choice arose. The cousin ⟪ar:ابن عباس⟫ counseled him to retain Uthman's appointed officials initially, then to dismiss them after consolidating power—a stratagem that promised worldly advantage. Yet Ali's reply was unequivocal: "Though what you say is indeed the most politic course for reconciliation in this world, ⟪ar:الادھی یلزمنی من الحق⟫I am obligated to what truth demands of me. How can I retain in office those appointed by Uthman when I know their corruption? Never shall I keep them in their positions!"[^cite-50] He deposed Mu'awiya and every governor appointed by his predecessor immediately upon assuming the caliphate. What appeared to historians as a political miscalculation revealed instead Ali's absolute rejection of worldly expedience when it compromised the principles of the Hereafter. As he himself declared in his correspondence, "When people abandon a portion of their religion for worldly gain, Allah opens upon them the gates of calamity in this world itself."[^cite-51]

The potential for evil dwells within every human soul. When power combines with personal desire, and the ruler is deprived of divine grace, that latent capacity transforms into manifest wickedness. Thus Ali begins his letter to Malik with the injunction: "Make obedience to Allah your highest priority, for obedience to Him is a covenant of the Qur'an. Those who follow ⟪ar:'سعد'⟫ it prosper; those who disobey ⟪ar:'خبیث'⟫ it are ruined." This opening contains more than mere exhortation—it grants spiritual freedom, for it liberates the soul from the tyranny of its base desires, as the tradition teaches: ⟪ar-quote:ان انفس أمارۃ بالسوء الا ما رحم ربی⟫ (the soul incites toward evil save when the mercy of Allah attends it).[^cite-52]

The Prophet ⟪ar:حضرت یوسف علیہ السلام⟫ Joseph himself, when vindicated before the king, proclaimed:

> ⟪quran 12:53⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ وَمَآ أُبَرِّئُ نَفْسِىٓ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلنَّفْسَ لَأَمَّارَةٌۢ بِٱلسُّوٓءِ إِلَّا مَا رَحِمَ رَبِّىٓ ۚ إِنَّ رَبِّى غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *"I do not exonerate myself. Verily, the soul incites toward evil, save when my Lord bestows His mercy. My Lord is indeed Forgiving, Merciful."*

This declaration illuminates the relationship between divine mercy ⟪ar:رحم⟫ and the self. Without the Lord's mercy, the soul inclines perpetually toward sin; by that mercy, it escapes the snare of base desire and returns to its original nature—that state of satisfaction toward which the Qur'an points:

> ⟪quran 89:27-29⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎ ‏ٱرْجِعِىٓ إِلَىٰ رَبِّكِ رَاضِيَةًۭ مَّرْضِيَّةًۭ ‎ ‏فَٱدْخُلِى فِى عِبَدِى ‎⟫
> *"O soul at peace! Return to your Lord, well-pleased and pleasing to Him. Enter among My honored servants."*

Nature constitutes both the beginning and the end of the soul's journey, for the soul is inscribed with the divine nature and its return is likewise toward that primordial state.

<!-- section 12 (id=3595, raw_sort=12): روحانیت اور اخلاق -->

## Spirituality and Moral Character

In his First Sermon, Amir al-Mu'minin declares:

⟪ar-quote:وَاصْطَفى سُبْحَانَهُ مِنْ وَلَدِهِ أَنْبيَاءَ أَخَذَ عَلَى الْوَحْيِ مِيثَاقَهُم، وَعَلَى تَبْليغِ الرِّسَالَةِ أَمَانَتَهُمْ، لَمَّا بَدَّلَ أَكْثَرُ خَلْقِهِ عَهْدَ اللهِ إِلَيْهِمْ، فَجَهِلُوا حَقَّهُ، واتَّخَذُوا الاْنْدَادَ مَعَهُ، وَاجْتَالَتْهُمُ الشَّيَاطِينُ عَنْ مَعْرفَتِهِ، وَاقتَطَعَتْهُمْ عَنْ عِبَادَتِهِ، فَبَعَثَ فِيهمْ رُسُلَهُ، وَوَاتَرَ إِلَيْهِمْ أَنْبِياءَهُ،**لِيَسْتَأْدُوهُمْ مِيثَاقَ فِطْرَتِهِ**، وَيُذَكِّرُوهُمْ مَنْسِيَّ نِعْمَتِهِ، وَيَحْتَجُّوا عَلَيْهِمْ بَالتَّبْلِيغِ، **وَيُثِيرُوا لَهُمْ دَفَائِنَ الْعُقُولِ**، وَيُرُوهُمْ آيَاتِ الْمَقْدِرَةِ⟫

From humankind Allah chose prophets, taking their covenant upon His revelation and entrusting them with the message. When most of creation violated their covenant with Allah, forgetting His due and taking compeers alongside Him, when Satan turned them from His knowledge and alienated them from His worship, Allah sent forth His messengers and succeeded them with His prophets, to call them back to the covenant of their original nature, to remind them of His forgotten blessings, to establish proof through preaching, to awaken within them those buried treasures of intellect, and


<!-- section 13 (id=3596, raw_sort=13): کبر اور غرور سے بچنے کی نصیحت -->

## Warning Against Arrogance and Pride

He warns the owner of such conduct against grave spiritual peril: "Do not prepare your soul for war with Allah!" What constitutes such warfare? Upon close examination, one perceives that this admonition concerns attitudes whose outward expressions appear merely as vices, yet whose inward reality stands opposed to the very spirit those actions purport to embody. Consider arrogance as a cardinal example—one to which Maulana Ali returns repeatedly throughout his teachings. When a ruler becomes arrogant, he usurps one of the supreme attributes reserved for the Divine alone. He deems himself entitled to a station of greatness worthy of Allah, forgetting that ⟪ar:'المتکبر'⟫ (al-Mutakabbir, the Mighty One) alone possesses this title by absolute right.[^cite-33] To boast before the people and display one's grandeur constitutes inward opposition to Allah and a denial of His ⟪ar:أحدیت⟫ (aḥadiyyat, absolute oneness). This concealed denial manifests, when viewed aright, as rebellion against Allah—for enmity toward ⟪ar:الحق⟫ (al-Ḥaqq, the Real/Truth) forms the hidden substance that every arrogant ruler exhibits through his tyranny and oppression toward those beneath him. The ruler's sense of superiority over his subjects becomes, in truth, a declaration of rebellion against the One who stands above him.[^cite-34] Thus the oppressor inflicts not only the just wrath of the Creator upon himself through his cruelty toward creation, but actively opposes the Creator through his deeds. The root of this worldly malice lies in a spiritual defect—denial of the Lord ⟪ar:أحدیت⟫ (who possesses all sovereignty and authority), coupled with forgetfulness of His ⟪ar:حقانیت⟫ (ḥaqāniyyat, absolute truth). This forgetfulness causes one to ignore the verse of the Qur'an:

> ⟪quran 40:16⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَوْمَ هُم بَرِزُونَۖ لَا يَخْفَىٰ عَلَى ٱللَّهِ مِنْهُمْ شَىْءٌۭۚ لِّمَنِ ٱلْمُلْكُ ٱلْيَوْمَۖ لِلَّهِ ٱلْوَحِدِ ٱلْقَهَّارِ ‎⟫
> *The Day when they will (all) come out, nothing of them will be hidden from Allah. Whose is the kingdom this Day? (Allah Himself will reply to His Question): It is Allah's the One, the Irresistible!*

This ⟪ar:'الیوم'⟫ (al-yawm, "the day") does not refer solely to the Resurrection; rather, it encompasses every single day. In his celebrated sermon known as the ⟪ar:'القاصیۃ'⟫ (al-Qāṣiyah, the Sermon on Steadfastness), Maulana Ali describes the humiliation of the arrogant Iblis—how he became the first to confront Allah in the realm of pride, thereby establishing himself as the source and exemplar of all subsequent arrogance. When the Divine commanded him to prostrate before Adam, he refused outright. Swollen with great vanity, he deemed himself superior to Adam, declaring: "I am created of fire, and man is created of clay." By virtue of this arrogance, Iblis not only became the first enemy of Allah, but also assumed the station of ⟪ar:أمام المتعصبین و صلف المستکبرین⟫ (imām al-mutaʿaṣṣibīn wa ṣalf al-mustakbirīn, leader of all the fanatical and the haughty) who would follow him.[^cite-35] Guard yourselves against the disease his whispers transmit! Always don the garment of humiliation! Crush self-praise beneath your feet! Cast off the chains of vanity from your neck! Fortify yourselves within the secure fortress of humility.

This reveals that humility stands as the supreme weapon against Satan, whose purpose is precisely to instil arrogance in the human breast. Arrogance proves not merely a terrible trait in itself; it functions as a poison that corrupts every ⟪ar:خصال محمودۃ⟫ (khiṣāl maḥmūdah, praiseworthy quality)—transforming goodness itself into evil. He states: "A sin that grieves you is better than a good deed accompanied by arrogance." Moments of praise and self-satisfaction open the gates for Satan to launch his assault.

*Verses referenced in this section (curated from KASHKOLE. TopicAyats — 7 of 7 not already cited above):*

> ⟪quran 7:181⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمِمَّنْ خَلَقْنَآ أُمَّةٌۭ يَهْدُونَ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَبِهِۦ يَعْدِلُونَ ‎⟫
> *And of those whom We have created, there is a community who guides (others) with the truth, and establishes justice therewith.*

> ⟪quran 7:182⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا۟ بِـَٔايَتِنَا سَنَسْتَدْرِجُهُم مِّنْ حَيْثُ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *Those who reject Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs, revelations, etc.), We shall gradually seize them with punishment in ways they perceive not.*

> ⟪quran 9:85⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تُعْجِبْكَ أَمْوَلُهُمْ وَأَوْلَدُهُمْ ۚ إِنَّمَا يُرِيدُ ٱللَّهُ أَن يُعَذِّبَهُم بِهَا فِى ٱلدُّنْيَا وَتَزْهَقَ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَهُمْ كَفِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *And let not their wealth or their children amaze you. Allah's Plan is to punish them with these things in this world, and that their souls shall depart (die) while they are disbelievers.*

> ⟪quran 17:81⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَقُلْ جَآءَ ٱلْحَقُّ وَزَهَقَ ٱلْبَطِلُ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلْبَطِلَ كَانَ زَهُوقًۭا ‎⟫
> *And say: "Truth (i.e. Islamic Monotheism or this Quran or Jihad against polytheists) has come and Batil (falsehood, i.e. Satan or polytheism, etc.) has vanished. Surely! Batil is ever bound to vanish."*

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other ilah (god) along with Allah, La ilaha illa Huwa (none has the right to be worshipped but He). Everything will perish save His Face. His is the Decision, and to Him you (all) shall be returned.*

> ⟪quran 55:26⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍۢ ‎⟫
> *Whatsoever is on it (the earth) will perish.*

> ⟪quran 55:27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَيَبْقَىٰ وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ ‎⟫
> *And the Face of your Lord full of Majesty and Honour will abide forever.*

<!-- section 14 (id=3601, raw_sort=14): شرک خفی -->

## Hidden Associationism (*Shirk* of the Inner Soul)

Although outward shirk (associationism) denotes the worship of idols, a more subtle form exists—the worship of false gods dwelling within the self, manifest as intentions, attitudes, inclinations, pride, ostentation, boasting, and fabrication. The Prophet, upon him be peace, alluded to this reality when he said: "Shirk is hidden in my Community like the creeping of a black ant upon a black stone in a black night."[^cite-36] He taught further: "Know that even the slightest hypocrisy constitutes shirk." To act for the approval of others rather than for the sake of Allah alone is to associate partners with Him. Whoever performs deeds for other than Allah, Allah entrusts that servant to those others.

Iblis's inner arrogance deteriorated into outward disobedience, which sealed his fate of humiliation. He was humiliated because he disobeyed Allah, and his disobedience sprang from pride. This demonstrates that arrogance itself is a disgrace—a seed of destruction planted in one's own being. Do you not observe how Allah abasement him? To be arrogant is, in reality, to be humiliated; self-exaltation is truly self-abasement. Therefore, Ali instructed Malik al-Ashtar: "Do not say, 'I possess authority; I command and am obeyed.'"[^cite-37] Such a notion corrupts the heart and ruins religion. From this counsel emerges an essential truth: for religion to appear rightly in the outer world, inner intentions and conceptions must first be corrected. This is why he exhorted that when power ascends to the head, faith descends from the heart. For faith to endure in this world, it must spring from the heart and manifest as humility—a form of maintaining proper order and justice (*ʿadl*).

He then addresses Malik al-Ashtar with further precision: "When your position breeds arrogance and display, contemplate the magnificence of Allah, above whom you stand under His dominion."[^cite-38] This reflection will subdue your passions and restore your intellect by protecting you from the rigidity of self-deception. The relationship between intellect and humility merits careful consideration. That faculty of intellect distracted by arrogance and pretense is precisely the part that grasps the reality of Allah and perceives the branches of truth flowing from that reality. In Arabic, arrogance is called ⟪ar:'مَخِلا'⟫ (mikhāl), which derives from *khayāl*—illusion, fancy. Arrogance is thus an "imagining" with deep roots in both the real and deceptive dimensions of existence. It constitutes a severe form of delusion arising from intellectual disorder. It is recognized as evil and branded as immoral, for it involves not only inflating one's own importance but also ⟪ar:الحق⟫ (al-Ḥaqq, the Truth) diminishing. Only one whom ⟪ar:ولی اللہ⟫ (walī Allāh, a Friend of Allah) can fully grasp the import of the following verses and extract from them the humility that eradicates ⟪ar:'أنائیت'⟫ (anāniyyat, "I-ness," egoism)—the root of all arrogance, display, and pride, the very sustenance of every oppression:

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other ilah (god) along with Allah, La ilaha illa Huwa (none has the right to be worshipped but He). Everything will perish save His Face. His is the Decision, and to Him you (all) shall be returned.*

> ⟪quran 55:26-27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍۢ ‎ ‏وَيَبْقَىٰ وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ ‎⟫
> *Whatsoever is on it (the earth) will perish. And the Face of your Lord full of Majesty and Honour will abide forever.*

> ⟪quran 17:81⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَقُلْ جَآءَ ٱلْحَقُّ وَزَهَقَ ٱلْبَطِلُ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلْبَطِلَ كَانَ زَهُوقًۭا ‎⟫
> *And say: "Truth has come and falsehood has vanished. Surely falsehood is ever bound to vanish."*

With these realities understood, one may fully grasp his admonition: "Be fearful of imitating Allah and confronting Him, for Allah loathes every wrongdoer and humiliates every arrogant person." He who denies justice to Allah and His creation will find, on the Day of Standing, not merely the creation as his adversary but Allah Himself arrayed against him. Man remains in a state of war with Allah until he abandons oppression and repents before the Divine. Even should he escape retribution in this world, he cannot escape it in the Hereafter.

As the oppressor persists, his soul grows ever more corrupt, soaked deeper in torment. The Qur'an presents this truth through the concept of ⟪ar:'استدراج'⟫ (istidrāj, gradual seduction into punishment)—degrees of chastisement that distinguish those who do justice to the Truth from those who perpetrate wrong:

> ⟪quran 7:181-182⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمِمَّنْ خَلَقْنَآ أُمَّةٌۭ يَهْدُونَ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَبِهِۦ يَعْدِلُونَ ‎ ‏وَٱلَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا۟ بِـَٔايَتِنَا سَنَسْتَدْرِجُهُم مِّنْ حَيْثُ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *And of those whom We have created, there is a community who guides (others) with the truth, and establishes justice therewith. Those who reject Our Ayat, We shall gradually seize them with punishment in ways they perceive not.*

This punishment manifests not only as poverty, illness, and suffering, but also through worldly success, glory, and offspring—as Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 9:85⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تُعْجِبْكَ أَمْوَلُهُمْ وَأَوْلَدُهُمْ ۚ إِنَّمَا يُرِيدُ ٱللَّهُ أَن يُعَذِّبَهُم بِهَا فِى ٱلدُّنْيَا وَتَزْهَقَ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَهُمْ كَفِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *And let not their wealth or their children amaze you. Allah's Plan is to punish them with these things in this world, and that their souls shall depart while they are disbelievers.*

The wrongdoer may simultaneously be a ⟪ar:'مسلمان'⟫ (muslimān, Muslim) outwardly and a ⟪ar:'کافر'⟫ (kāfir, denier) inwardly—a denier because *kufr* means concealment. He has hidden the truth from himself through his deeds, and all good that flows from it remains veiled.

<!-- section 15 (id=3597, raw_sort=15): اخلاقی و روحانی ضمیر -->

## The Moral and Spiritual Conscience

Another mode of warfare against Allah involves conflict with one's own conscience. The nafs (soul), which possesses knowledge and understanding of its moral obligations, speaks to the self as the voice of the inner conscience—as if the voice of conscience were the utterance of an awakened soul.

> ⟪quran 91:7-8⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَنَفْسٍۢ وَمَا سَوَّىٰهَا ‎ ‏فَأَلْهَمَهَا فُجُورَهَا وَتَقْوَىٰهَا ‎⟫
> *And by Nafs (the soul), and Him Who perfected it in proportion; Then He showed it what is wrong for it and what is right for it;*

This verse reveals that the one who corrects and guides toward the right path is the conscience—that faculty upon which both good and evil arguments present themselves. A morally awakened soul inspires goodness; a debased soul inspires evil. Allah the Most High has inscribed within every soul, amidst conscience, a capacity for discrimination—to which the above verse points. Thus every soul not only distinguishes between right and wrong but also instinctively recognizes its own ⟪ar:'عبدیت'⟫ (ʿubūdiyyat, servitude) and that of Allah—His ⟪ar:'الہیت'⟫ (ilāhiyyat, divinity). The Qur'an memorializes the moment when the Lord extracted a covenant from the children of Adam:

> ⟪quran 7:172⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِنۢ بَنِىٓ آدَمَ مِن ظُهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّتَهُمْ وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ ۖ قَالُوا۟ بَلَىٰ ۛ شَهِدْنَآ ۛ أَن تَقُولُوا۟ يَوْمَ ٱلْقِيَمَةِ إِنَّا كُنَّا عَنْ هَذَا غَفِلِينَ ‎⟫
> *And (remember) when your Lord brought forth from the Children of Adam, from their loins, their seed (or from Adam's loin his offspring) and made them testify as to themselves (saying): "Am I not your Lord?" They said: "Yes! We testify," lest you should say on the Day of Resurrection: "Verily, we have been unaware of this."*

This demonstrates that the wrongdoer is one who violates his covenant with Allah and takes himself—the ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ بالسوء⟫ (nafs al-ammārah bi-al-sūʾ, the soul commanding to evil)—as his lord instead of believing in Allah as his Master. For this reason, Ali instructed Malik al-Ashtar: "Do not say, 'I command, and obey me,' for such is the path of the ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ بالسوء⟫—that which commands the body, imagination, intellect, intention, emotion, and consciousness."[^cite-39] The way to establish justice toward oneself is ⟪ar:مجاہدۃ النفس⟫ (mujāhadat al-nafs, the struggle against the soul)—to first excise one's own shortcomings. Therefore he advised: "If you desire to reform others, begin first with yourself, for to attempt improvement of others' souls while evil dwells within you is the greatest sin."

Before ⟪ar:مالک اشتر⟫ (Malik al-Ashtar), he had appointed ⟪ar:محمد بن ابی بکر⟫ (Muhammad ibn Abī Bakr) as governor of Egypt. He counseled him likewise, saying: "I have appointed you guardian of the people of Egypt. It devolves upon you by necessity to oppose your own self and protect your religion!"[^cite-40] This counsel is remarkable in its profundity. Ali entrusted power to Muhammad ibn Abī Bakr and imposed two obligations upon him: first, to restrain one's soul and its passions; second, to safeguard one's faith. The greater the power and authority, the greater the obligation to master oneself and impose restraint. Should the soul become enslaved to desire and fulfill its appetites through the instruments of power, man destroys not only himself but also religion itself. The outward manifestation of a Muslim's faith depends entirely upon the inner integrity of the soul for its preservation. This too exemplifies the maintenance of proper order. Upon attaining power, the ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ⟫ (nafs al-ammārah, the commanding soul)—that which creates arrogance, desire for dominion, and lust for authority—becomes thus described by the Qur'an:

> ⟪quran 96:6-7⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كَلَّآ إِنَّ ٱلْإِنسَنَ لَيَطْغَىٰٓ ‎ ‏أَن رَّآهُ ٱسْتَغْنَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *Nay! Verily, man does transgress all bounds. Because he considers himself self-sufficient.*

The more the soul is deluded by autonomy and flees from reliance upon Allah, the more it will imagine itself as divine—and this represents the greatest injustice against oneself. Such a person becomes the one to whom Allah directs His words:

> ⟪quran 45:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ وَأَضَلَّهُ ٱللَّهُ عَلَىٰ عِلْمٍۢ وَخَتَمَ عَلَىٰ سَمْعِهِۦ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَجَعَلَ عَلَىٰ بَصَرِهِۦ غِشَوَةًۭ فَمَن يَهْدِيهِ مِنۢ بَعْدِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أَفَلَا تَذَكَّرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Have you seen him who takes his own lust (vain desires) as his ilah (god), and Allah knowing (him as such), left him astray, and sealed his hearing and his heart, and put a cover on his sight. Who then will guide him after Allah? Will you not then remember?*

The more a person acquires keen awareness of his own poverty and recognizes his absolute need for Allah, the more the ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ بالسوء⟫ loosens its stranglehold upon his neck. Only the soul that commands itself to evil can compel others to do likewise; conversely, the soul that humbles itself before Allah treats people with gentleness, mercy, and justice.

He states: "In your judgment, your own actions should be the most worthy, most equitable, and most acceptable to people—yet do not allow people's disapproval to weaken your approval."[^cite-41] You have insisted upon "the approval of ordinary human beings" in your words! He who despises himself in the sight of Allah will dwell among common folk with humility; he who is arrogant will consort only with the arrogant. Such a person rightly understands this verse:

> ⟪quran 35:15⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلنَّاسُ أَنتُمُ ٱلْفُقَرَآءُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِۖ وَٱللَّهُ هُوَ ٱلْغَنِىُّ ٱلْحَمِيدُ ‎⟫
> *O mankind! It is you who stand in need of Allah, but Allah is Rich (Free of all wants and needs), Worthy of all praise.*

In this matter, the life of Amīr al-Muʾminīn, Master of the Universe, stands as a living proof. ⟪ar:آثم بن زیاد⟫ (A family of ascetics, once complained to him that they were living in unnecessary poverty. He called them and advised them to care for their families and not reject the bounties Allah had bestowed. Yet one of them replied: "O Ali! You counsel us thus, and you yourself wrap yourself in a rough woolen garment and sustain yourself on dry bread!"[^cite-42] He answered: "Woe to you! I am not like you! Allah has enjoined upon the ⟪ar:ائمۃ الحق⟫ (aʾimmat al-Ḥaqq, the Guides to Truth) that they live as the poorest among their people, so that they feel the poverty of the destitute and do not become greedy for wealth."

This encounter illuminates an essential principle: a ruler must live at the material level of the poorest of his subjects. Ali chose for himself the least he could obtain—and this choice flowed from his profound connection with ⟪ar:'الحق'⟫ (al-Ḥaqq, the Real), in whose light every material object became contemptible, vile, and worthless to his eyes.

<!-- section 16 (id=3587, raw_sort=16): عدل اور ہمدردی -->

## Justice and Compassion

The capacity to feel the sufferings of the poor deepens one's awareness of complete dependence upon one's Lord, enabling one to traverse life between hope and fear, sustained by divine mercy. Living thus, the natural human disposition (*fiṭra*) inspires compassion for one's fellow beings. The ability to empathize neither contradicts the requirements of justice nor stands opposed to them; rather, it constitutes an essential component of justice itself. Such empathy not only preserves proper order but aligns with the nature of the cosmos and manifests one of the supreme attributes of ⟪ar:الحق⟫ (al-Ḥaqq, the Real). For this reason, Allah has prefaced every chapter of the Qur'an with *Bismillāh al-raḥmān al-raḥīm*—invoking His mercy and compassion. The Prophet, upon him be peace, and Amīr al-Muʾminīn embodied this reality: they invariably treated people with tenderness. Yet they did so not from personal sentiment alone, but because it reflected the command of Allah, as He declared:

> ⟪quran 7:156⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ وَٱكْتُبْ لَنَا فِى هَذِهِ ٱلدُّنْيَا حَسَنَةًۭ وَفِى ٱلْآخِرَةِ إِنَّا هُدْنَآ إِلَيْكَ ۚ قَالَ عَذَابِىٓ أُصِيبُ بِهِۦ مَنْ أَشَآءُ ۖ وَرَحْمَتِى وَسِعَتْ كُلَّ شَىْءٍۢ ۚ فَسَأَكْتُبُهَا لِلَّذِينَ يَتَّقُونَ وَيُؤْتُونَ ٱلزَّكَوٰةَ وَٱلَّذِينَ هُم بِـَٔايَتِنَا يُؤْمِنُونَ ‎⟫
> *And ordain for us good in this world, and in the Hereafter. Certainly we have turned unto You." He said: (As to) My Punishment I afflict therewith whom I will and My Mercy embraces all things. That (Mercy) I shall ordain for those who are the Muttaqun (pious), and give Zakat; and those who believe in Our Ayat;*

> ⟪quran 6:54⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذَا جَآءَكَ ٱلَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِـَٔايَتِنَا فَقُلْ سَلَمٌ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ كَتَبَ رَبُّكُمْ عَلَىٰ نَفْسِهِ ٱلرَّحْمَةَ ۖ أَنَّهُۥ مَنْ عَمِلَ مِنكُمْ سُوٓءًۢا بِجَهَلَةٍۢ ثُمَّ تَابَ مِنۢ بَعْدِهِۦ وَأَصْلَحَ فَأَنَّهُۥ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *When those who believe in Our Ayat come to you, say: "Salamun 'Alaikum" (peace be on you); your Lord has written Mercy for Himself, so that, if any of you does evil in ignorance, and thereafter repents and does righteous good deeds (by obeying Allah), then surely, He is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful.*

The teachings of Maulana Ali brim with reflections upon mercy. He declared: "Acts of mercy draw Allah's mercy upon you. You will be shown mercy according as you show mercy to others. I marvel at one who expects mercy from above yet shows none to those below!"[^cite-43] According to this principle, the more compassionate a person becomes in spiritual outlook and moral conduct toward others, the nearer he draws to the Almighty. In a just society, people must be treated with compassion wherever possible; only when no other remedy exists should severe punishment be imposed. Thus, in his letter to Malik al-Ashtar, Ali commanded the punishment of corrupt officials who had usurped the public wealth, so that divine justice might be established. In another missive to his cousin, whom he had appointed governor of Basra, he wrote with solemn oath: "By Allah, with complete sincerity—if it reaches me that you have misappropriated the wealth of the Muslims, whether little or much, I will inflict upon you a punishment that will diminish your riches, break your back, and bring ruin to your deeds!"[^cite-44]

Whenever someone petitioned him for favor, he treated the matter with utmost seriousness, showing no leniency even to his own relatives. Once his brother Aqeel requested an additional stipend from the public treasury; Ali placed a burning iron bar in his hand. Aqeel shrieked in agony. Ali said: "Brother Aqeel, if you cannot endure this brief fire, how shall I bear the blazing fire of Allah's Hell on the Day of Resurrection—a fire to which you invite me?"[^cite-45] Similarly, upon learning that his cousin ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿAbbās had misappropriated Muslim funds, he declared: "Fear Allah and restore to the people their due. If you do not, and Allah grants me power over you, I shall strike you with my sword. Whomever I strike enters the realm of the jinn![^cite-46] By Allah, if al-Ḥasan and al-Ḥusayn did the same, they would receive no special dispensation from me."

This illustrates that regardless of rank or station, all stand equal before justice. His conduct differed markedly from his predecessors, who had distributed governorships among relatives and plundered Muslim wealth. As Ali stated: "In spring a camel swallows soft shoots,"[^cite-47] implying that wealth-seekers must be restrained early. The Qur'an affirms:

> ⟪quran 4:135⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ كُونُوا۟ قَوَّمِينَ بِٱلْقِسْطِ شُهَدَآءَ لِلَّهِ وَلَوْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِكُمْ أَوِ ٱلْوَلِدَيْنِ وَٱلْأَقْرَبِينَ ۚ إِن يَكُنْ غَنِيًّا أَوْ فَقِيرًۭا فَٱللَّهُ أَوْلَىٰ بِهِمَا ۖ فَلَا تَتَّبِعُوا۟ ٱلْهَوَىٰٓ أَن تَعْدِلُوا۟ ۚ وَإِن تَلْوُۥٓا۟ أَوْ تُعْرِضُوا۟ فَإِنَّ ٱللَّهَ كَانَ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ خَبِيرًۭا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Stand out firmly for justice, as witnesses to Allah, even though it be against yourselves, or your parents, or your kin, be he rich or poor, Allah is a Better Protector to both (than you). So follow not the lusts (of your hearts), lest you may avoid justice, and if you distort your witness or refuse to give it, verily, Allah is Ever Well-Acquainted with what you do.*

A remarkable passage in the letter demonstrates how Ali universalizes compassion, drawing all humanity into a single egalitarian plane where distinctions dissolve. This passage carries within it a cure for prejudice and sectarianism in all forms:

> Habituate your heart to mercy for the subjects and to affection and kindness for them. Do not stand over them like greedy beasts who feel it is enough to devour them, since they are of two kinds—either your brother in religion or one like you in creation. They will commit slips and encounter mistakes. They may act wrongly, wilfully or by neglect. So, extend to them your forgiveness and pardon, in the same way as you would like Allah to extend His forgiveness and pardon to you, because you are over them and your responsible Commander (Imam) is over you while Allah is over him who has appointed you. He (Allah) has sought you to manage their affairs and has tried you through them.[^cite-48]

Through this counsel on mercy, Ali directs attention to Allah's compassion itself, reminding every ruler that no matter how elevated his station, he remains a servant of Allah, absolutely dependent upon His mercy. Therefore, the ruler who acknowledges his dominion over human beings must also remember his servitude before Allah. This awareness transforms him into one compassionate and sympathetic toward his subjects, drawing Allah's mercy upon himself. He reminds Malik al-Ashtar that though a ruler, he remains a human being like all others.

Once Maulana Ali observed a blind beggar seeking alms, yet no one came to his aid. He was told the man was Christian. Ali responded: "You have worn him down so greatly that he has grown old and weak, and now you refuse to assist him? From today, sustenance for him shall come from the public treasury." This deed teaches a universal lesson: Muslims and non-Muslims alike possess equal claim to justice. Social justice and religious equity flow from compassion; mercy thus becomes an incumbent duty upon believers.

He instructed Malik al-Ashtar that rulership is not an honor from Allah but a test—one that reveals the heart. During his caliphate, he had declared in a sermon: "Had Allah not sworn to the scholars that they would oppose the oppressor and support the oppressed, I would have cast the reins of this caliphate from my hands. You would see that this world is less valuable to me than the nasal mucus of a goat."[^cite-49] Here lies a kinship with Platonic thought: the true philosopher rules only for the people's welfare. He views rulership not as personal honor but as an indispensable duty whose sole purpose is the establishment of justice. The foundation and restoration of any society rests upon this single attribute alone.

From his teachings emerges this principle: governance operates under the mandate of the poor's welfare. Should Allah grant a servant knowledge and grant him consciousness of justice, his responsibility multiplies. The greater God's grace upon a person, the greater his obligation to extend benevolence to creation. In one sermon, he affirmed: "Allah's grace does not increase upon His servant until the right of Allah becomes great in his eyes."[^cite-50]

<!-- section 17 (id=3588, raw_sort=17): اللہ کے بارے میں خوش گمانی -->

## Good Opinion of Allah (*Ḥusn al-Ẓann*)

Now consider the passage wherein Amīr al-Muʾminīn instructs Malik al-Ashtar regarding the selection of a minister and counselor. He advised against the miserly and the cowardly, observing: "Stinginess, cowardice, and greed stem surely from distrust of Allah."[^cite-51] This mistrust arises from failure to understand the divine *Fiṭrah* (natural disposition); ignorance of *Fiṭrah* springs from inadequate knowledge of Allah's attributes. From this perspective, all human corruptions trace themselves to an intellect weakened by insufficient faith. Conversely, robust faith generates a sound perception of Allah, strengthens intellect, and cultivates a penetrating conception of divine reality—a conception that illuminates the divine attributes within. One should not suppose that because these attributes belong to Allah alone, one ought not to strive toward them. Rather, one should make these qualities exemplary in oneself and a guide for conduct, purging the soul's defects. This does not mean competing with the Divine in greatness; the goal is to become like Allah in His attributes. Such spiritual development occurs through worship of the Almighty. A person should be generous because Allah is generous; merciful because Allah is merciful and compassionate. Yet simultaneously, one must establish humility and servitude, acknowledging that no quality one cultivates can ever match the dignity of Allah's attributes.

All divine attributes describe humanity's complete dependency and reliance upon Allah—humanity's utter need for His absolute oneness (*tawḥīd*) and companionship. Thus a dual relationship forms between Allah and His servant: affirmative and negative. Affirmative, as when Maulana Ali said, "Whoever does not show mercy to another, Allah shows no mercy to him"; negative, according to Allah's word:

> ⟪quran 35:15⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلنَّاسُ أَنتُمُ ٱلْفُقَرَآءُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِۖ وَٱللَّهُ هُوَ ٱلْغَنِىُّ ٱلْحَمِيدُ ‎⟫
> *O mankind! it is you who stand in need of Allah, but Allah is Rich (Free of all wants and needs), Worthy of all praise.*

In this synthesis, humanity's virtues and noble deeds become a reflection of Allah's divine attributes, while one maintains unwavering conviction of one's nothingness before Allah's magnificence. The human being becomes simultaneously the representative of Allah and His slave—⟪ar:خلیفۃ اللہ و عبد اللہ⟫ (khalīfat Allāh wa ʿabd Allāh). Servitude maintains one within the bounds of one's station, preventing transgression and usurpation of the Divine's glory; representation reminds one that servitude does not exempt one from obligation toward Allah's creation, which He has entrusted to one's care. This balance between representation and servitude—between service to Allah and service to His creatures—exemplifies another manifestation of maintaining proper order, and constitutes the means of harmonizing moral action with self-purification.

<!-- section 18 (id=3590, raw_sort=18): شہر اور معاشرا -->

## The City and Society

The letter proceeds to enumerate the various segments of society—armies, scribes, judiciary, officers, tax collectors, peasants, merchants, artisans, and the destitute—describing the obligations each category bears. His counsel regarding them represents practical justice in action. A ruler must fulfill the rights of all these classes, recognizing that he himself remains answerable to Allah. Allah has established all these classes, apportioned their livelihoods, fixed their boundaries, and taken from them a covenant to abide by the Book and the Sunnah of the Prophet.

The ruler's obligation toward society forms part of his covenant with Allah, as the verse attests:

> ⟪quran 13:19-20⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ أَفَمَن يَعْلَمُ أَنَّمَآ أُنزِلَ إِلَيْكَ مِن رَّبِّكَ ٱلْحَقُّ كَمَنْ هُوَ أَعْمَىٰٓ ۚ إِنَّمَا يَتَذَكَّرُ أُو۟لُوا۟ ٱلْأَلْبَبِ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ يُوفُونَ بِعَهْدِ ٱللَّهِ وَلَا يَنقُضُونَ ٱلْمِيثَقَ ‎⟫
> *Shall he then who knows that what has been revealed unto you from your Lord is the truth be like him who is blind? But it is only the men of understanding that pay heed. Those who fulfill the Covenant of Allah and break not the Mîthaq;*

And:

> ⟪quran 17:34⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَقْرَبُوا۟ مَالَ ٱلْيَتِيمِ إِلَّا بِٱلَّتِى هِىَ أَحْسَنُ حَتَّىٰ يَبْلُغَ أَشُدَّهُۥ ۚ وَأَوْفُوا۟ بِٱلْعَهْدِ ۖ إِنَّ ٱلْعَهْدَ كَانَ مَسْـُٔولًۭا ‎⟫
> *And come not near to the orphan's property except to improve it, until he attains the age of full strength. And fulfil (every) covenant. Verily! the covenant, will be questioned about.*

Following this, Ali advises the ruler to surround himself with scholars and wise counselors, that they may bring prosperity to his regime and increase among his subjects the welfare of those who came before them. Each segment of society is then addressed individually, with the ruler conceived as the center around whom all classes revolve—a center whose connection binds them all to the Divine itself.

Regarding the army, he emphasizes that soldiers form a fortress for the people. The commander must be chosen for his utter sincerity to Allah, His Messenger, and the Imam of the Age—one whose heart is pure and free of rancor, forbearing, slow to anger, swift to forgive, gentle with the weak, and stern with the strong.[^cite-52] Such a leader does not panic in adversity nor does weakness deter him. Observe that these qualities shine prominently in the character of the Prophet himself. The emphasis on compassion, gentleness, and forbearance is striking, for these are not virtues one might expect in warfare. Yet the Qur'an presents warriors who are fierce only toward enemies while filled with mercy among themselves:

> ⟪quran 48:29⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مُّحَمَّدٌۭ رَّسُولُ ٱللَّهِ ۚ وَٱلَّذِينَ مَعَهُۥٓ أَشِدَّآءُ عَلَى ٱلْكُفَّارِ رُحَمَآءُ بَيْنَهُمْ ۖ تَرَىٰهُمْ رُكَّعًۭا سُجَّدًۭا يَبْتَغُونَ فَضْلًۭا مِّنَ ٱللَّهِ وَرِضْوَنًۭا ۖ سِيمَاهُمْ فِى وُجُوهِهِم مِّنْ أَثَرِ ٱلسُّجُودِ ۚ ذَلِكَ مَثَلُهُمْ فِى ٱلتَّوْرَىٰةِ ۚ وَمَثَلُهُمْ فِى ٱلْإِنجِيلِ كَزَرْعٍ أَخْرَجَ شَطْـَٔهُۥ فَـَٔازَرَهُۥ فَٱسْتَغْلَظَ فَٱسْتَوَىٰ عَلَىٰ سُوقِهِۦ يُعْجِبُ ٱلزُّرَّاعَ لِيَغِيظَ بِهِمُ ٱلْكُفَّارَ ۗ وَعَدَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ مِنْهُم مَّغْفِرَةًۭ وَأَجْرًا عَظِيمًۢا ‎⟫
> *Muhammad (PBUH) is the Messenger of Allah, and those who are with him are severe against disbelievers, and merciful among themselves. You see them bowing and falling down prostrate (in prayer), seeking Bounty from Allah and (His) Good Pleasure. The mark of them (i.e. of their Faith) is on their faces (foreheads) from the traces of (their) prostration (during prayers). This is their description in the Taurat (Torah). But their description in the Injeel (Gospel) is like a (sown) seed which sends forth its shoot, then makes it strong, it then becomes thick, and it stands straight on its stem, delighting the sowers that He may enrage the disbelievers with them. Allah has promised those among them who believe and do righteous good deeds, forgiveness and a mighty reward (i.e. Paradise).*

Regarding judges, Ali specifies that they must not be confused by complexity, nor irritated by perpetual petitions; they must stand firm as mountains in truth, unmoved by superficial stratagems, excel in dispute, and pursue truth single-mindedly—always guarded against praise and desire.[^cite-53] He acknowledges such individuals are rare. Judges must receive generous compensation so that they have no need to seek payment from those who come before them.

Concerning the learned and wise, he counsels testing their integrity before appointing them to office, ensuring selection remains unbiased. After their appointment, their conduct must be monitored, and any abuse of position punished severely.

Regarding peasants who till the soil and collect taxes, Ali states: "You must prioritize the cultivation of the land over tax collection. Without cultivation, no tax follows. Whoever imposes taxation without inspecting the cultivation destroys the people."[^cite-54] The devastation of land flows from the ruin of those who inhabit it. Poverty overwhelms them when the desire to accumulate wealth overtakes the rulers, when they doubt their own survival, and when they cannot benefit from the examples of their predecessors. Doubt about one's survival signifies belief that one shall live forever, answerable to none. To such persons Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 104:1-4⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَيْلٌۭ لِّكُلِّ هُمَزَةٍۢ لُّمَزَةٍ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِى جَمَعَ مَالًۭا وَعَدَّدَهُۥ ‎ ‏يَحْسَبُ أَنَّ مَالَهُۥٓ أَخْلَدَهُۥ ‎ ‏كَلَّا ۖ لَيُنۢبَذَنَّ فِى ٱلْحُطَمَةِ ‎⟫
> *Woe to every slanderer and backbiter. Who has gathered wealth and counted it, He thinks that his wealth will make him last forever! Nay! Verily, he will be thrown into the crushing Fire.*

When one forgets the inevitability of death, the desire to accumulate overwhelms reason. Instead of acquiring true spiritual treasures, one squanders life accumulating false material wealth—and from this springs oppression.

Regarding the selection of officials, Ali counsels: do not appoint those merely because they have demonstrated virtue to you. Look instead to their past record and the public's opinion of them; entrust office only to those of proven trustworthiness.

Concerning merchants, he notes they greatly benefit society and should be treated most fairly. They are generally peace-loving and should be permitted to conduct their affairs, yet any evils—hoarding, miserliness, or deceit—must be firmly prevented.

### The Poor, Most Needing the Ruler's Justice

Amīr al-Muʾminīn speaks with particular solemnity about the poor, the disabled, the orphaned, and the aged. These are people in direst need of the ruler's justice, yet they cannot extend their hands to entreat anyone.[^cite-55] He teaches: "The ruler must give special care to these people if he hopes for Allah's forgiveness on the Day of Resurrection." A dedicated officer should be assigned to address their needs and present their circumstances to the ruler. Then Ali adds: "This burden weighs upon the ruler, yet Allah lightens it for those who look toward the Hereafter, who exhort themselves to patience, and who maintain certainty in what Allah has promised them."[^cite-56]

Here he links this duty once more to spirituality: if one's vision transcends this world toward the Hereafter, even the most difficult tasks become manageable. But those whose aspirations remain bound to the world will fall into heedlessness concerning the poor. From a purely worldly calculus, helping the poor yields no political advantage—the ruler gains no apparent benefit from such expenditure. Yet when this vision is accompanied by recognition of Allah's infinite justice, His boundless mercy, and the desire to attain the Hereafter through benevolence toward the poor, the task becomes light, and rulers of genuine faith are stirred to sincere and sustained support.

This transcends ordinary charity and alms-giving. When one elevates the concept of aiding the poor to a state of perfection, one cannot become enslaved by selfish desire, pride, or heedlessness—whether intentional or unconscious. The next quality Ali describes—patience—emerges spontaneously from this refined state. The act is not confined to personal effort and will; it draws divine grace flowing from faith's deepest roots. Consequently, such rulers trust in Allah's reward, His justice, His promise of mercy—and their resolve to assist the poor and establish justice strengthens immeasurably.

These moral realities of the Hereafter remain hidden from worldly rulers, obscured by their hidden prejudices and outward corruption. Such wrongdoers neither believe in the blessings of the next life nor in its punishments and torments. They are called oppressors (*ẓālimūn*) because they transgress the requirements of divine justice, denying that supreme attribute of mercy which constitutes the very essence of God's nature.


<!-- section 19 (id=3591, raw_sort=19): The Importance of Intention -->

## The Importance of Intention

The most essential element in all the commands you have given is intention (nīyat). Even when a person's endeavor to establish justice cannot reach full fruition owing to the transience of the material world, his sincere intention becomes the foundation of his moral life and infuses him with the taste of Allah's grace. If God's promise is true—and if man believes in this reality with unshaken conviction—then such belief exerts a transformative effect upon the soul: it converts a personal inclination into an unconditional necessity, and elevates a desirable attribute into an absolute reality. Thereby morality is fortified by spirituality, and all the commands of the Sharīʿa (Islamic law) become manageable. Thereafter the person establishes justice not in expectation of future reward in the Hereafter, but as a grateful response to what he has already received from Allah. The Qur'ān speaks of the blessings of Paradise as though they were already given to the believers, as if what shall occur in time to come has already passed into their possession:

> ⟪quran 108:1-2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَعْطَيْنَكَ ٱلْكَوْثَرَ ‎ ‏فَصَلِّ لِرَبِّكَ وَٱنْحَرْ ‎⟫
> *Verily, We have granted you (O Muhammad (Peace be upon him)) Al-Kauthar (a river in Paradise); Therefore turn in prayer to your Lord and sacrifice (to Him only).*
> indeed We have given you abundance, so perform the prayer to your Lord and sacrifice.
> — **Quran 108:1-2 (inline widget)**

In elucidation of this principle, Maulānā ʿAlī distinguishes three modes of worship: one group worships Allah in desire for Paradise—this is mercantile worship; another worships from fear of Hell—this is the worship of the servant in bondage; and a third worships from gratitude—this is the worship of the free. For this reason he declared in one place: ⟪ar-quote:یا الہی ما عبدتک من شوق جنتک ولا من خوف النارک بل وجدت مستحق لی العبادۃ فالعبدتک⟫ "O Allah, I do not worship You through longing for Your Paradise, nor through fear of Your Fire, but I have found You worthy of worship, therefore I worship You."[^cite-46]

A person is absolved of the deficiencies in his actions through the sincerity of his intention; his action's worth does not depend on its outcome but on the purity of his intention. The establishment of justice becomes not a means to any worldly end, but an end in itself—the fulfillment of the requirements of justice, for the justice of the just person is integral to his very nature. Justice is not associated with Allah in the sense of being something He performs; rather, He is Justice itself. Therefore, the just person acts justly to conform with the will of Allah, not merely to obey His command nor from worldly desire. The Qur'ān states:

> ⟪quran 92:17-21⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَسَيُجَنَّبُهَا ٱلْأَتْقَى ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِى يُؤْتِى مَالَهُۥ يَتَزَكَّىٰ ‎ ‏وَمَا لِأَحَدٍ عِندَهُۥ مِن نِّعْمَةٍۢ تُجْزَىٰٓ ‎ ‏إِلَّا ٱبْتِغَآءَ وَجْهِ رَبِّهِ ٱلْأَعْلَىٰ ‎ ‏وَلَسَوْفَ يَرْضَىٰ ‎⟫
> *And Al-Muttaqun (the pious and righteous - see V.2:2) will be far removed from it (Hell). He who spends his wealth for increase in self-purification, And have in his mind no favour from anyone for which a reward is expected in return, Except only the desire to seek the Countenance of his Lord, the Most High; He surely will be pleased (when he will enter Paradise).*
> And away from it is the God-fearing one who gives his wealth so that he may be purified; and no soul has any favour against it, but he who is recompensed only with the Countenance of his Lord, the Most High, and he shall soon be well-pleased.
> — **Quran 92:17-21 (inline widget)**

This is the definition of ⟪ar:'ابرار'⟫ (al-abrār, the righteous). All Islamic scholars are unanimous that these verses were revealed in honor of Maulānā ʿAlī and his family when they fasted for three consecutive days and distributed the bread of their own household to the poor, the destitute, and the orphan:

> ⟪quran 76:8-9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَيُطْعِمُونَ ٱلطَّعَامَ عَلَىٰ حُبِّهِۦ مِسْكِينًۭا وَيَتِيمًۭا وَأَسِيرًا ‎ ‏إِنَّمَا نُطْعِمُكُمْ لِوَجْهِ ٱللَّهِ لَا نُرِيدُ مِنكُمْ جَزَآءًۭ وَلَا شُكُورًا ‎⟫
> *And they give food, inspite of their love for it (or for the love of Him), to Miskin (poor), the orphan, and the captive, (Saying): "We feed you seeking Allah's Countenance only. We wish for no reward, nor thanks from you.*
> And they feed the needy, and the orphan, and the captive, out of love for Him. Whatever We feed you, it is only for the sake of Allah; it is not for us to take any retribution from you, nor to be grateful.
> — **Quran 76:8-9 (inline widget)**

[^cite-46]

The more an action is performed solely for the sake of Allah, unattended by praise or blame from any other being, the more it approaches acceptability—an action neither weakened by external hardship nor strengthened by internal reward. This relationship between intention and outward act illuminates ʿAlī's profound statement: his heart dwells in heaven while his body labors in the world. It is instructive here that worldly morality fluctuates with results—if success attends the deed, one persists; if failure comes, one desists. Yet the action of one who looks toward the Hereafter is sustained by sincerity of intention alone. This does not signify that one should abandon striving; rather, the mark of sincere intention is that regardless of outcome, one perseveres in good deeds and never tires nor ceases. An action that falters under circumstance, or diminishes to mere formality, betrays deficiency in intention. Pure intention demands relentless, unwearying effort toward one's purpose.

The just person never despairs, never abandons the struggle to establish justice. His purpose is not to achieve results, but the spiritual fulfillment of justice itself; he understands that his physical existence is bound to external circumstance and ultimately to God's pleasure. Yet he does not lose heart when results do not manifest; his effort endures as permanently as his certitude in God's eternal blessings. His actions are strengthened by the attribute of divine justice itself.

Jesus Christ observed that when the principles of justice are conceived in isolation from spirituality, personal idealism arises—a fragile construct, swayed by external consequence and shattered by the weight of difficulty and despair. But when spirituality is wedded to justice, the indestructible attribute of divine justice supports it and grants it power to persist. Inasmuch as one's principles are grounded in spiritual knowledge, despair and desperation cannot touch him in the face of trial. We witness this truth exemplified in the biography of Amīr al-Muʾminīn (the Commander of the Faithful) himself: when he assumed the apparent caliphate, waves of warfare and rebellion crashed upon him one after another, preventing him from fully enacting all the principles and strategies he desired. Yet despite these tribulations, he was never disheartened, never discouraged, nor ever relaxed in the pursuit and establishment of justice. He would say: "No action is trivial if piety is joined with it"—meaning that despair has no place with the God-fearing person, for he is ever conscious of truth. This station of piety becomes for him an escape from the injustices of this world. As ʿAlī (peace be upon him) declared: ⟪ar-quote:من یتق اللہ یجعل لہ مخرجا من الفتن وا نور من الظلم⟫ "Whoever fears Allah, Allah shall make for him a way out from trials and light in darkness."[^cite-47]

<!-- section 20 (id=3592, raw_sort=20): The Excellence of Worship -->

## The Excellence of Worship

We come now to the point in your letter wherein you delineate the essence of all virtue—which is prayer. At the outset, you advise the ruler to fulfill the duties of prayer; here you counsel Mālik al-Ashtar that he should dedicate the finest portion of his time, after completing his administrative charge, to labor for the sake of Allah through worship and consecration. Specifically, he is instructed to purify his religion through obligatory acts of worship and to refine his devotion. By "purifying your religion," your intention is to purify the substance of the relationship with Allah through worship—that intimate communion between the soul and the Divine. For the depth of this relationship marks the quality of all human virtue.

He says: "Know that your every action depends on your worship." By worship here is not meant merely the outward bowing and prostration, but the inner sincerity fused with that outward form, which sustains it with life. The sincerity, fervor, and perfection of this prayer achieve its purpose. He instructed: "Use your strength night and day for the sake of Allah, and perfect the deeds through which you draw near to Him; perform them without weariness, and take your body to its utmost limit." The most significant word here is *nearness*, which arises from the dedication springing from the depths of the heart in the solitude of night's darkness. That is, all outward action is governed by the person's pure intention of surrender to Allah. When the inner life is illuminated by the light of prayer, its rays shine forth also in the outward conduct of life. For this reason, he urged Mālik to consecrate the best portion of his time to Allah: every moment of the ruler's day belongs to Allah, provided his intention is sincere and people are protected as a result. At such a time, one perceives how the fountains of obligatory and supererogatory prayer overflow, and their effects manifest in the outward actions of life. The Hadīth of the Messenger of Allah illustrates this beautiful truth: [^cite-48]

"My servant draws not near to Me with anything more beloved to Me than the obligatory duties I have imposed upon him. My servant continues to draw near to Me through supererogatory deeds until I love him. When I love him, I am his hearing by which he hears, his sight by which he sees, his hand by which he grasps, and his feet by which he walks."

To see and to act through Allah signifies two things: to perceive things according to their reality, and then to act in accordance therewith—in other words, to establish justice, to maintain each thing in its proper place. It is crucial to observe in this Hadīth that while obligatory and supererogatory prayers are the means of drawing near to Allah, the locus of divine action is through the acts of worship themselves, not through prayer alone. As ʿAlī says: take your actions to the limits of your body. This demonstrates that mere careless, mechanical worship bears no fruit. He observed: "The likeness of one who prays without striving is like one who shoots an arrow without a bow."

As was noted earlier, to connect with Allah and achieve unity with Him (tawḥīd—the affirmation of divine oneness), pure integration of the self is required. Prayer is the ground upon which the deep dimensions of the human soul are revealed, cultivated, and merged with the Divine. Therefore, the perfection of prayer is not attained through tongue and body alone, but through the totality of soul and body. Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 24:36⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فِى بُيُوتٍ أَذِنَ ٱللَّهُ أَن تُرْفَعَ وَيُذْكَرَ فِيهَا ٱسْمُهُۥ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ فِيهَا بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ ‎⟫
> *In houses (mosques), which Allah has ordered to be raised (to be cleaned, and to be honoured), in them His Name is glorified in the mornings and in the afternoons or the evenings,*
> in houses which Allah has commanded to be venerated and His name to be remembered therein, glorifying Him in the mornings and evenings.
> — **Quran 24:36 (inline widget)**

Regarding nearness to Allah, ʿAlī (peace be upon him) proclaimed: "Verily, Allah has set remembrance in hearts, through which they may hear when deaf and see when blind." In every age there have arisen special servants of Allah with whom Allah speaks through their thoughts, addressing them through the essence of their intellect. They diffuse the light of Allah in their hearts, their hearing and their sight, calling people to the remembrance of Allah's days. [^cite-49]

The importance of *dhikr* (remembrance) is manifest in your saying, through which consciousness of the truth is awakened. By dhikr you do not mean only the recitation of a specific divine name, but the perpetual awareness of Allah—the essence of all worship, meditation, and contemplation. The purpose is not merely to remember Allah or to chant His names, but to contemplate His divine realities through the manifest and hidden dimensions of His attributes. In another passage, Maulānā ʿAlī speaks thus of dhikr:

"Indeed, there are those who have adopted the remembrance of Allah in such a way that neither commerce nor livelihood diverts them from His remembrance. They spend the days of their lives in it. They exhort people to justice, and they themselves stand forth as exemplars of justice—they show people how all things are maintained in their proper place and explain the means of that maintenance. Spirituality is not separate from action; it is a connection to the moral depths that ⟪ar:'الہ'⟫ arise from the relationship itself—a relationship effected through worship in general and through remembrance in particular."[^cite-50]

Just as it has been established that sincerity of intention is the primary substance, so now it becomes clear that sincerity is the most vital element in prayer, which stretches the body to its limit. If the attribute of justice resides in the essence of God, then the closer one attains to Allah through prayer and remembrance, the more just one becomes and the more one develops within oneself positive capacities, spirituality, intellect, and moral character. Justice is both the cause and the consequence of worship. This clarifies the connection between worship and justice: justice teaches us to preserve each thing in its proper place. Justice toward Allah is fulfilled through prayer and remembrance; justice toward oneself and toward people is the fruit of the nearness achieved through worship of Allah, from which all virtues spring.

Amīr al-Muʾminīn (peace be upon him) has emphasized both the manifest prayer and its source—remembrance. Plato taught that the supreme knowledge ⟪ar:'خیر'⟫ (knowledge of the good) is the highest, for all goodness and rectitude flow from it. If one acquires all worldly knowledge but not knowledge of goodness, one has acquired nothing of worth. He drew a parallel between virtue and the sun, saying that what the sun accomplishes for sight, virtue accomplishes for intellect and being.

Once, Zalīb al-Yamānī asked ʿAlī: "O ʿAlī, have you seen the purpose of your sincerity?" He replied: "Had I not seen him, I would not have worshipped him." The questioner asked: "How did you see him?" ʿAlī answered: "He cannot be seen with the eyes of the head, but the heart sees him with the truth of faith."[^cite-51] From this utterance we understand the supreme importance of dhikr, for through it the heart is purified and made luminous. However, dhikr does not refer to knowledge of outward forms; rather, it is knowledge of the Creator of those forms, which in Islam is described by the divine attribute ⟪ar:'المصور'⟫ (the Shaper, the Former). Yet this remembrance cannot be expressed in words as other sciences are; it requires tireless worship and exertion day and night. It is like a spark struck by friction—once this flame is kindled, it never extinguishes, but continues to nourish itself throughout one's life.

The essence of justice in Amīr al-Muʾminīn's letter is this: for any society to establish justice, it must understand these Islamic principles not merely through intellect but through the heart, for the heart is attached to inner realities and only it can perceive them by the light of Allah's grace—an understanding impossible without His mercy. The prophetic requirement of justice is that all components of human life—worship, morality, action—be harmoniously connected through the principle of monotheistic affirmation. The domain of ethics cannot be separated from the domain of spirituality, for in ʿAlī's view, true virtue is that which is original, fortified, and directed toward the Truth. Therefore, these qualities of justice in the soul can be created only through worship whose spirituality flows from remembrance. Only this final analysis demonstrates that remembrance is what establishes the measure of human virtue.


<!-- section 21 (id=3602, raw_sort=21): ذکر اللہ -->

## The Remembrance of Allah

Ali al-Hajwiri, the author of *Kashf al-Mahjoob*, writes of the Commander of the Faithful ʿAlī ibn Abī Ṭālib with profound reverence. Among the great spiritual guides, ʿAlī stands foremost—a cousin of the Prophet Muḥammad consumed by the trials of faith and illuminated by the flames of love. He is counted among the chiefs of the sanctified ones (aṣfiyāʾ) and the friends of Allah (awliyāʾ), occupying a station of incomparable nobility on the spiritual path. His mastery of the realities of the higher world was so complete that the great Sufi Junayd declared: "ʿAlī is our master in the knowledge of principles." As Imam of both the intellectual and practical domains, ʿAlī exemplifies the Sufi understanding of the path—one in which knowledge of spiritual realities must be coupled with steadfast endurance through tribulation.

This tolerance of suffering echoes ʿAlī's own teaching: that he loves those from whom the ignorant turn away. What is it that the Sufis cherish, yet the heedless abandon? It is worship—a devoted attention to the Creator so exclusive that all other concerns fade into insignificance. In such worship, the soul offers itself as a sacrifice; it dies to all distractions in the presence of Allah's majesty. To serve the Truth is to annihilate oneself utterly.[^cite-52]

The word *dhikr* (ذکر), the remembrance of Allah, is remarkable for its semantic richness—a term untranslatable without loss. It encompasses remembrance, reflection, lamentation, recitation, and glorification (*tasbīḥ*); it denotes praise, celebration, renown, dignity, admonition, and warning. The Qurʾān itself is called *dhikr*. Yet the most precise definition comes from the lexicographer al-Rāghib al-Iṣfahānī: remembrance is the faculty by which knowledge is preserved and retained in consciousness. Though memory (*ḏikr*) looks to the past, remembrance (*tadhakkur*) brings presence into the moment—the actualization of something within consciousness and speech. Two categories comprise it: the remembrance of the heart and the remembrance of the tongue; each in turn divides into that which passes away and that which endures eternally. True remembrance of Allah, however, demands the presence of the heart.[^cite-53]

The remembrance of Allah constitutes a conscious state saturated with divine presence, yet it is simultaneously a disciplined spiritual practice. It is at once goal and means, knowledge and action in service of knowledge. For the Sufis and saints, *dhikr* is the instrument through which the intellect (ʿaql) becomes absorbed into the heart; through it, abstract truths crystallize into lived spiritual reality. When prayer forms the foundation of worship, the remembrance of Allah surpasses even that, as the Qurʾān declares:

> ⟪quran 29:45⟫
