> ⟪ar:‏ٱتْلُ مَآ أُوحِىَ إِلَيْكَ مِنَ ٱلْكِتَبِ وَأَقِمِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ ۖ إِنَّ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ تَنْهَىٰ عَنِ ٱلْفَحْشَآءِ وَٱلْمُنكَرِ ۗ وَلَذِكْرُ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ يَعْلَمُ مَا تَصْنَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *Recite (O Muhammad PBUH) what has been revealed to you of the Book (the Quran), and perform As-Salat (Iqamat-as-Salat). Verily, As-Salat (the prayer) prevents from Al-Fahsha' (i.e. great sins of every kind, unlawful sexual intercourse, etc.) and Al-Munkar (i.e. disbelief, polytheism, and every kind of evil wicked deed, etc.) and the remembering (praising, etc.) of (you by) Allah (in front of the angels) is greater indeed [than your remembering (praising, etc.) Allah in prayers, etc.]. And Allah knows what you do.*

Countless prophetic traditions illuminate the virtue of this remembrance. The Messenger of Allah once asked his companions: "Shall I not tell you of the purest of your deeds, the most exalted before your Lord, the best of recompense, and what is superior to giving gold and silver or than confronting your enemies?" When they cried for him to speak, he replied: "The remembrance of Allah." So too Mawlānā ʿAlī taught: "Remember Allah continuously, for it illuminates the hearts and is the noblest worship." And Imām Jaʿfar al-Ṣādiq (peace be upon him) said: "Our Shīʿa are those who, when alone, remember Allah frequently."[^cite-54]

### Remembrance of Allah Strengthens Hearts

The Commander of the Faithful opens his sermon by reciting verses of luminous power. At their center lies the affirmation that remembrance ignites the heart:

> ⟪quran 24:35-37⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ ٱللَّهُ نُورُ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ ۚ مَثَلُ نُورِهِۦ كَمِشْكَوٰةٍۢ فِيهَا مِصْبَاحٌ ۖ ٱلْمِصْبَاحُ فِى زُجَاجَةٍ ۖ ٱلزُّجَاجَةُ كَأَنَّهَا كَوْكَبٌۭ دُرِّىٌّۭ يُوقَدُ مِن شَجَرَةٍۢ مُّبَرَكَةٍۢ زَيْتُونَةٍۢ لَّا شَرْقِيَّةٍۢ وَلَا غَرْبِيَّةٍۢ يَكَادُ زَيْتُهَا يُضِىٓءُ وَلَوْ لَمْ تَمْسَسْهُ نَارٌۭ ۚ نُّورٌ عَلَىٰ نُورٍۢ ۗ يَهْدِى ٱللَّهُ لِنُورِهِۦ مَن يَشَآءُ ۚ وَيَضْرِبُ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْأَمْثَلَ لِلنَّاسِ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ بِكُلِّ شَىْءٍ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎ ‏فِى بُيُوتٍ أَذِنَ ٱللَّهُ أَن تُرْفَعَ وَيُذْكَرَ فِيهَا ٱسْمُهُۥ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ فِيهَا بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ ‎ ‏رِجَالٌۭ لَّا تُلْهِيهِمْ تِجَرَةٌۭ وَلَا بَيْعٌ عَن ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ وَإِقَامِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةِ وَإِيتَآءِ ٱلزَّكَوٰةِ ۙ يَخَافُونَ يَوْمًۭا تَتَقَلَّبُ فِيهِ ٱلْقُلُوبُ وَٱلْأَبْصَرُ ‎⟫
> *Allah is the Light of the heavens and the earth. The parable of His Light is as (if there were) a niche and within it a lamp, the lamp is in glass, the glass as it were a brilliant star, lit from a blessed tree, an olive, neither of the east (i.e. neither it gets sun-rays only in the morning) nor of the west (i.e. nor it gets sun-rays only in the afternoon, but it is exposed to the sun all day long), whose oil would almost glow forth (of itself), though no fire touched it. Light upon Light! Allah guides to His Light whom He wills. And Allah sets forth parables for mankind, and Allah is All-Knower of everything. In houses (mosques), which Allah has ordered to be raised (to be cleaned, and to be honoured), in them His Name is glorified in the mornings and in the afternoons or the evenings, Men whom neither trade nor sale diverts them from the Remembrance of Allah (with heart and tongue), nor from performing As-Salat (Iqamat-as-Salat), nor from giving the Zakat. They fear a Day when hearts and eyes will be overturned (from the horror of the torment of the Day of Resurrection).*

When the Imam reaches the verse describing those whom commerce cannot divert from remembrance, he expounds its inner meaning with characteristic profundity:

Indeed, Allah has made the remembrance of Allah a polish for the hearts—a burnishing force through which the deaf hear, the blind see, and the rebellious submit. In every age, Allah has raised servants to whom He speaks through the depths of their intellect and cognition. Through their hearing, sight, and the light kindled in their hearts, they spread guidance and call creation to the remembrance of Allah. Among them is a community that prefers this remembrance to the pursuits of the world, so that neither trade nor transaction distracts them. They expend their days in *dhikr*, living as though already in the Hereafter while yet in this world—inhabitants of both realms simultaneously.[^cite-55]

The link between the burning of hearts and the imagery of light is profound. The concealed luminescence within the heart blazes forth through remembrance. The inner light of consciousness is kindled by the outer light of *dhikr*. When the heart ignites with this radiance, its brilliance spreads to every faculty; all are illuminated. This illumination corresponds to what the Qurʾān expresses as ⟪ar:نُور ⟪ar:علی نُور⟫—light upon light. The very word "burning" (lit. "polishing") denotes purification, revelation, the emergence into luminosity. The Qurʾān itself attests:

> ⟪quran 92:1-2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلَّيْلِ إِذَا يَغْشَىٰ ‎ ‏وَٱلنَّهَارِ إِذَا تَجَلَّىٰ ‎⟫
> *By the night as it envelops; And by the day as it appears in brightness;*

And elsewhere:

> ⟪quran 91:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلنَّهَارِ إِذَا جَلَّىٰهَا ‎⟫
> *And by the day as it shows up (the sun's) brightness;*

Through remembrance, consciousness dormant in the heart stirs and manifests in deed. The heart's role here merits reflection: it receives divine light through *dhikr* and reflects that radiance upon all other faculties; simultaneously, remembrance awakens the buried consciousness in its depths, unveiling truths. Mawlānā ʿAlī spoke of ⟪ar:'دفائن العقول'⟫—the treasures hidden in intellects. It becomes evident that *dhikr*'s true purpose is the purification of the heart (*qalb*), that seat of sovereignty and source of authentic insight.[^cite-56]

The Qurʾān makes this unmistakable:

> ⟪quran 7:179⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنَا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيرًۭا مِّنَ ٱلْجِنِّ وَٱلْإِنسِ ۖ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌۭ لَّا يَفْقَهُونَ بِهَا وَلَهُمْ أَعْيُنٌۭ لَّا يُبْصِرُونَ بِهَا وَلَهُمْ آذَانٌۭ لَّا يَسْمَعُونَ بِهَآ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ كَٱلْأَنْعَمِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْغَفِلُونَ ‎⟫
> *And surely, We have created many of the jinns and mankind for Hell. They have hearts wherewith they understand not, they have eyes wherewith they see not, and they have ears wherewith they hear not (the truth). They are like cattle, nay even more astray; those! They are the heedless ones.*

Allah employs the term "heedless" (*ghāfilūn*), the opposite of remembrance. The succeeding verse describes the practical method of spiritual remembrance:

> ⟪quran 7:180⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلِلَّهِ ٱلْأَسْمَآءُ ٱلْحُسْنَىٰ فَٱدْعُوهُ بِهَا ۖ وَذَرُوا۟ ٱلَّذِينَ يُلْحِدُونَ فِىٓ أَسْمَٓئِهِۦ ۚ سَيُجْزَوْنَ مَا كَانُوا۟ يَعْمَلُونَ ‎⟫
> *And (all) the Most Beautiful Names belong to Allah, so call on Him by them, and leave the company of those who belie or deny (or utter impious speech against) His Names. They will be requited for what they used to do.*

The following verses render the bond between remembrance and heart crystalline:

> ⟪quran 13:28⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَتَطْمَىِٕنُّ قُلُوبُهُم بِذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۗ أَلَا بِذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ تَطْمَىِٕنُّ ٱلْقُلُوبُ ‎⟫
> *Those who believe (in the Oneness of Allah - Islamic Monotheism), and whose hearts find rest in the remembrance of Allah, Verily, in the remembrance of Allah do hearts find rest.*

> ⟪quran 50:37⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ فِى ذَلِكَ لَذِكْرَىٰ لِمَن كَانَ لَهُۥ قَلْبٌ أَوْ أَلْقَى ٱلسَّمْعَ وَهُوَ شَهِيدٌۭ ‎⟫
> *Verily, therein is indeed a reminder for him who has a heart or gives ear while he is heedful.*

> ⟪quran 8:2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّمَا ٱلْمُؤْمِنُونَ ٱلَّذِينَ إِذَا ذُكِرَ ٱللَّهُ وَجِلَتْ قُلُوبُهُمْ وَإِذَا تُلِيَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ آيَتُهُۥ زَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَنًۭا وَعَلَىٰ رَبِّهِمْ يَتَوَكَّلُونَ ‎⟫
> *The believers are only those who, when Allah is mentioned, feel a fear in their hearts and when His Verses (this Quran) are recited unto them, they (i.e. the Verses) increase their Faith; and they put their trust in their Lord (Alone);*

> ⟪quran 39:22⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَمَن شَرَحَ ٱللَّهُ صَدْرَهُۥ لِلْإِسْلَمِ فَهُوَ عَلَىٰ نُورٍۢ مِّن رَّبِّهِۦ ۚ فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْقَسِيَةِ قُلُوبُهُم مِّن ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ فِى ضَلَلٍۢ مُّبِينٍ ‎⟫
> *Is he whose breast Allah has opened to Islam, so that he is in light from His Lord (as he who is non-Muslim)? So, woe to those whose hearts are hardened against remembrance of Allah! They are in plain error!*

> ⟪quran 39:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱللَّهُ نَزَّلَ أَحْسَنَ ٱلْحَدِيثِ كِتَبًۭا مُّتَشَبِهًۭا مَّثَانِىَ تَقْشَعِرُّ مِنْهُ جُلُودُ ٱلَّذِينَ يَخْشَوْنَ رَبَّهُمْ ثُمَّ تَلِينُ جُلُودُهُمْ وَقُلُوبُهُمْ إِلَىٰ ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ ذَلِكَ هُدَى ٱللَّهِ يَهْدِى بِهِۦ مَن يَشَآءُ ۚ وَمَن يُضْلِلِ ٱللَّهُ فَمَا لَهُۥ مِنْ هَادٍ ‎⟫
> *Allah has sent down the best statement, a Book (this Quran), its parts resembling each other in goodness and truth, oft-repeated. The skins of those who fear their Lord shiver from it (when they recite it or hear it). Then their skin and their heart soften to the remembrance of Allah. That is the guidance of Allah. He Guides therewith whom He pleases and whomever Allah sends astray, for him there is no guide.*

These verses establish beyond question that remembrance is intrinsically bound to the heart—that faculty which transforms consciousness into reality. The heart requires enrichment through *dhikr*. As the Prophet taught: "For everything there is a polish"—and the polish of the heart is remembrance of Allah. This hadith points to a systematic discipline that unites action with awareness, recalling another prophetic directive: "Worship Allah as though you see Him." On one level, *dhikr* serves to purify thought and deepen contemplation; on another, it unfolds as deliberate action manifesting in various forms: ⟪ar:تسبیح⟫ glorification, ⟪ar:تمجید⟫ magnification, ⟪ar:تحمید⟫ praise, ⟪ar:تقدیس⟫ sanctification, and ⟪ar:تحلیل⟫ declaration of divine unity—each removing the rust of forgetfulness from the heart. The Prophet called such people "people of remembrance" and declared: "There are angels of Allah who travel the roads seeking those who remember Allah, and when they find them, they say to one another, 'Come to what you long for.'"[^cite-57]

The heart perceives through remembrance a direct sight (*baṣīra*) that the *dhikr* has purified and revived through faith. Mawlānā ʿAlī teaches that this insight surpasses even ordinary seeing and is akin to the vision of Allah Himself. He calls the purified heart the throne of Allah's vision and proclaims: "Whoever purifies his heart sees Allah." His declaration resonates in your instruction: "Where are those whose deeds are performed purely for Allah, who purify their hearts through remembrance so that they become a dwelling-place for Allah?" This accords with the prophetic tradition in which Allah says: "My servant does not cease drawing near to Me through supererogatory deeds until I love him. When I love him, I am his hearing with which he hears, his sight with which he sees, his hand with which he grasps, and his feet with which he walks." At this station, human faculties ascend into the divine realm; the heart transcends physicality, its inner essence unites with the Truth, and it begins to see as Allah sees—until, finally, it witnesses Allah Himself.[^cite-58]

The Sufi master Abū Ṭālib al-Makkī writes with piercing clarity: if Allah enters human faculties through human action, then the pinnacle of spiritual consciousness arrives when the vision of Allah becomes not the sight of a human beholding the divine, but rather Allah's own sight manifesting through the purified heart. Mawlānā ʿAlī expresses this mystery: "Acquire knowledge of Allah through Allah." In this ultimate analysis, Allah is both the Seer and the Seen—as the Qurʾān affirms:

> ⟪quran 85:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَشَاهِدٍۢ وَمَشْهُودٍۢ ‎⟫
> *And by the witnessing day (i.e. Friday), and by the witnessed day [i.e. the day of 'Arafat (Hajj) the ninth of Dhul-Hîjjah];*

What is witnessed is the inner essence of human consciousness; what witnesses is divine reality. In other words, when faith penetrates the depths of a human soul, Allah becomes present everywhere and at all times. As Mawlānā ʿAlī proclaims in his sermon: "By Your magnificence, which encompasses all things; by Your names, which are the foundation of all existence; by Your knowledge, which embraces all things; by the light of Your face, by which all objects are illuminated."

Nothing subsists without its foundation. The names of Allah—their totality and their reality—provide that ground. To perceive things rightly is to behold the divine attributes which are truly real, while objects become their physical reflection and self-disclosure. When the heart is purified through *dhikr*, it discerns Allah in all places. The universal presence of Allah is taught in Scripture from two perspectives: the divine and the human:

> ⟪quran 2:115⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلِلَّهِ ٱلْمَشْرِقُ وَٱلْمَغْرِبُ ۚ فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا۟ فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ ٱللَّهِ ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ وَسِعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *And to Allah belong the east and the west, so wherever you turn yourselves or your faces there is the Face of Allah (and He is High above, over His Throne). Surely! Allah is All-Sufficient for His creatures' needs, All-Knowing.*

> ⟪quran 41:53⟫
> ⟪ar:‏سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ حَتَّىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ ۗ أَوَلَمْ يَكْفِ بِرَبِّكَ أَنَّهُۥ عَلَىٰ كُلِّ شَىْءٍۢ شَهِيدٌ ‎⟫
> *We will show them Our Signs in the universe, and in their ownselves, until it becomes manifest to them that this (the Quran) is the truth. Is it not sufficient in regard to your Lord that He is a Witness over all things?*

The heart purified by remembrance perceives these signs everywhere and in all things. Yet such perception does not reduce the infinite to the finite or collapse the transcendent into the sensible. Mawlānā ʿAlī clarifies: "Allah is in all things, yet not through proximity; He is separate from all things, yet not through distance." His presence in creation does not imply spatial nearness to objects, nor does His separation diminish His divinity. Allah draws infinitely nearer to us than we can ever approach Him:

> ⟪quran 50:16⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَا ٱلْإِنسَنَ وَنَعْلَمُ مَا تُوَسْوِسُ بِهِۦ نَفْسُهُۥ ۖ وَنَحْنُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ حَبْلِ ٱلْوَرِيدِ ‎⟫
> *And indeed We have created man, and We know what his ownself whispers to him. And We are nearer to him than his jugular vein (by Our Knowledge).*

> ⟪quran 112:4⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَمْ يَكُن لَّهُۥ كُفُوًا أَحَدٌۢ ‎⟫
> *"And there is none co-equal or comparable unto Him."*

Nothing can exist apart from Allah; yet nothing possesses any affinity with His being. All creatures simultaneously enter from Him and depart from Him. His presence in all things does not diminish His divinity; His transcendence over all things does not remove Him from them. As Mawlānā ʿAlī teaches, Allah is one not through numerical unity but through the impossibility of comparison—that which cannot be counted is not subject to enumeration. To count Allah is polytheism. He makes abundantly clear that no existence is possible without His existence. He alone truly is; all else is illusion. The radical doctrine of unity, which banishes all otherness, reveals a profound truth: every creature besides Allah shares a false divinity, for each appears as a unity standing opposed to the true Unity and Oneness of Allah.

Praise belongs to Allah, present in the hidden essence of things and manifest in the existence of creation. No eye can bear to look upon Him, yet the eye that cannot see cannot deny His reality; no heart that affirms His reality can comprehend Him. He is supremely exalted—no object is higher—yet immeasurably intimate—no object draws nearer. The intellect cannot fathom His attributes, yet knowledge of Him is not withheld from cognition.

This paradox resolves through a crucial dimension of *dhikr*: remembrance that unites understanding and recognition. Humanity is not assembling fragmented pieces of knowledge from external sources; rather, consciousness stirs to wakefulness after the veils of primordial forgetfulness are lifted. Mawlānā ʿAlī opens his sermon with the declaration: "The first of religion is its knowledge"—meaning both the origin and foundation. Knowledge here signifies not mere acquisition but recognition. This reveals a sublime reality: Allah has inscribed the knowledge of truth within human consciousness itself. Through remembrance, humanity recalls what it once knew and had forgotten, acknowledging truths that dwell eternally within.[^cite-59]

In his sermon, ʿAlī continues:

"Allah has sent Messengers to take a covenant from them regarding the original nature of creation, to remind them of the blessings they have forgotten, to argue with them through the message, to awaken for them the treasures of intellect, and to show them the signs of divine power."

These treasures are the knowledge Allah placed in the depths of consciousness and to which Allah bore witness at creation itself:

> ⟪quran 7:172⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِنۢ بَنِىٓ آدَمَ مِن ظُهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّتَهُمْ وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ ۖ قَالُوا۟ بَلَىٰ ۛ شَهِدْنَآ ۛ أَن تَقُولُوا۟ يَوْمَ ٱلْقِيَمَةِ إِنَّا كُنَّا عَنْ هَذَا غَفِلِينَ ‎⟫
> *And (remember) when your Lord brought forth from the Children of Adam, from their loins, their seed (or from Adam's loin his offspring) and made them testify as to themselves (saying): "Am I not your Lord?" They said: "Yes! We testify," lest you should say on the Day of Resurrection: "Verily, we have been unaware of this."*

These divine realities also encompass the Spirit of Allah breathed into Adam:

> ⟪quran 32:9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ثُمَّ سَوَّىٰهُ وَنَفَخَ فِيهِ مِن رُّوحِهِۦ ۖ وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ ٱلسَّمْعَ وَٱلْأَبْصَرَ وَٱلْأَفْـِٔدَةَ ۚ قَلِيلًۭا مَّا تَشْكُرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Then He fashioned him in due proportion, and breathed into him the soul (created by Allah for that person), and He gave you hearing (ears), sight (eyes) and hearts. Little is the thanks you give!*

> ⟪quran 2:31⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَعَلَّمَ آدَمَ ٱلْأَسْمَآءَ كُلَّهَا ثُمَّ عَرَضَهُمْ عَلَى ٱلْمَلَٓئِكَةِ فَقَالَ أَنۢبِـُٔونِى بِأَسْمَآءِ هَٓؤُلَآءِ إِن كُنتُمْ صَدِقِينَ ‎⟫
> *And He taught Adam all the names (of everything), then He showed them to the angels and said, "Tell Me the names of these if you are truthful."*

> ⟪quran 30:30⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَأَقِمْ وَجْهَكَ لِلدِّينِ حَنِيفًۭا ۚ فِطْرَتَ ٱللَّهِ ٱلَّتِى فَطَرَ ٱلنَّاسَ عَلَيْهَا ۚ لَا تَبْدِيلَ لِخَلْقِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ ذَلِكَ ٱلدِّينُ ٱلْقَيِّمُ وَلَكِنَّ أَكْثَرَ ٱلنَّاسِ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *So set you (O Muhammad PBUH) your face towards the religion of pure Islamic Monotheism Hanifa (worship none but Allah Alone) Allah's Fitrah (i.e. Allah's Islamic Monotheism), with which He has created mankind. No change let there be in Khalq-illah (i.e. the Religion of Allah Islamic Monotheism), that is the straight religion, but most of men know not.*

These verses establish that knowledge of Allah is woven into the primordial nature (*fiṭra*) of humanity—the covenant Allah drew from them at creation's dawn. Imām al-Bāqir (peace be upon him) explained that Allah created creatures upon the original nature of affirming divine unity: that there is no god but Allah, and that He is our Lord. This demonstrates that the knowledge of God is the explication of human nature itself. As Mawlānā ʿAlī affirms, the knowledge of Allah cannot be hidden from the human intellect.

Yet though this knowledge remains eternally present in human consciousness, forgetfulness—the antithesis of remembrance—has obscured it. No measure of external learning can repair this amnesia; only when the flame of *dhikr* kindles within the heart and joins with the light of revealed guidance can the divine knowledge illuminate both intellect and spirit. The treasures buried in consciousness awaken.[^cite-60]

Mawlānā ʿAlī declares: "Praise is for Allah, who is known without being seen." This paradox deepens in his further teaching: "Through created things, the Creator appears to the intellect; through created things, He is veiled from sight." Here emerges the veil born of creation itself. Every creature is a ⟪ar:'حجاب'⟫ veil in the deepest sense—at once concealing divine mystery and bearing witness to the Creator through its own existence. That is why he proclaims: "No veil can obscure Him." The veil is constrained to reveal its Observer, for in revealing its own existence to the veil, the veil is forced to testify. The Master of Existence says: "Were the veil lifted, my certainty would not increase"—for certainty is not the product of sensation but the clarity of a heart purified through remembrance, a heart that now sees what was blind before. He adds to this subtle paradox: "The veil between Him and His creation is the creation itself, to maintain distinction between Creator and created, between infinite and finite, between Lord and servant."

All creation, all the veils born of creation, exemplify the divine attribute of manifest revelation (*al-Ẓāhir*), whereby things appear, are seen, made manifest, rendered visible. They express the divine reality of the Creator (⟪ar:'خالق'⟫) through their contingent being—for Allah causes His hidden treasures to shine forth as apparent creation. Allah reveals the 'outward' reality of the cosmos (⟪ar:'الظاہر'⟫) while simultaneously veiling the inner mystery of His being (⟪ar:'الباطن'⟫) within that expression. The creature's veil is therefore the Creator's manifestation. What, then, do these outer veils conceal? The Oneness of Allah, the sacred foundation of their very essence. As noted before, the divine attributes constitute the ground of all creation. Thus all existence rests upon one singular reality. Creation's deepest truth is the divine attributes of the Truth itself. To associate a creature with Allah is to commit shirk, the greatest deception. Therefore, the vision of divine unity shields us from this error, maintaining forever the distinction between Creator and created, infinite and finite, Master and servant.

The veil of creation guards nature from pantheism and preserves the infinite transcendence of Allah from reduction into finite human forms. Similarly, transcendence (*tanzīh*—the divine unity declaring Allah beyond all attributes) and affirmation (*tasb*īḥ—the divine unity affirming Allah's perfect attributes) are themselves veils, though each illuminates the other. When the spiritual vision unites the two—the manifested and the hidden, the apparent and the concealed—they each reveal their complementary reality. To emphasize Allah's manifestation unilaterally renders it a veil, concealing His hiddenness. To stress only His inner hiddenness becomes an impenetrable veil, obscuring His manifestation within creation. The veils, then, arise not solely from creation but from the weakness and limitations of human concepts and the narrow aperture through which divine attributes can manifest themselves. Thus negation of attributes becomes necessary. Through this negation, consciousness transcends the veil it cannot pierce, beginning to perceive the divinity beyond.

When the great Sufi Abū Saʿīd al-Khurrāz was asked, "How did you come to know Allah?", he replied by recognizing the joining of opposites. He then recited:

> ⟪quran 57:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هُوَ ٱلْأَوَّلُ وَٱلْآخِرُ وَٱلظَّهِرُ وَٱلْبَاطِنُ ۖ وَهُوَ بِكُلِّ شَىْءٍ عَلِيمٌ ‎⟫
> *He is the First (nothing is before Him) and the Last (nothing is after Him), the Most High (nothing is above Him) and the Most Near (nothing is nearer than Him). And He is the All-Knower of every thing.*

Spiritual inspiration grants vision by which seemingly disparate realities appear as one truth when beheld in the light of monotheism. At this profound level of consciousness, reconstruction commences; from it springs knowledge of the Truth. The heart begins to see Allah through the seeing of faith's innermost truth. Only the realities transcendent and sublime deserve magnification—truths veiled in the depths of faith, visible only to hearts kindled by the remembrance of Allah, hearts that perceive and comprehend the facts that vindicate the reality of Allah Himself.[^cite-61]


<!-- section 22 (id=3603, raw_sort=22): ذکر اللہ عبادت کی معراج ہے -->

## Remembrance of God as the Ascension of Worship

God Most High declares in His infinite wisdom:

> ⟪quran 76:25⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ بُكْرَةًۭ وَأَصِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *And remember the Name of your Lord every morning and afternoon.*

And again He commands:

> ⟪quran 73:8⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ وَتَبَتَّلْ إِلَيْهِ تَبْتِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *And remember the Name of your Lord and devote yourself to Him with complete devotion.*

The Almighty further exhorts the believers:

> ⟪quran 33:41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ ذِكْرًۭا كَثِيرًۭا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Remember Allah with much remembrance.*

The Prophet (upon whom be peace) is instructed to invoke his Lord with profound humility:

> ⟪quran 7:55⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱدْعُوا۟ رَبَّكُمْ تَضَرُّعًۭا وَخُفْيَةً ۚ إِنَّهُۥ لَا يُحِبُّ ٱلْمُعْتَدِينَ ‎⟫
> *Invoke your Lord with humility and in secret. He likes not the aggressors.*

And again:

> ⟪quran 7:205⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُر رَّبَّكَ فِى نَفْسِكَ تَضَرُّعًۭا وَخِيفَةًۭ وَدُونَ ٱلْجَهْرِ مِنَ ٱلْقَوْلِ بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ وَلَا تَكُن مِّنَ ٱلْغَافِلِينَ ‎⟫
> *And remember your Lord within yourself, humbly and with fear, without loudness of speech, in the mornings and afternoons, and be not among the heedless.*

These verses collectively illuminate the proper manner of dhikr—the remembrance of God. They emphasize that remembrance must be undertaken with sincere humility, profound reverence, and inner contrition; it must be performed quietly and without ostentation, whether in the solitude of one's heart or through the motion of one's lips. Yet what stands foremost among all these injunctions is the insistence upon *frequency* and *constancy* of remembrance. The intensity of the Prophet's (upon whom be peace) own practice, and that of the Commander of the Faithful, ʿAlī, has been preserved in Sūrat al-Muzzammil:

> ⟪quran 73:20⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ إِنَّ رَبَّكَ يَعْلَمُ أَنَّكَ تَقُومُ أَدْنَىٰ مِن ثُلُثَىِ ٱلَّيْلِ وَنِصْفَهُۥ وَثُلُثَهُۥ وَطَآئِفَةٌۭ مِّنَ ٱلَّذِينَ مَعَكَ ۚ وَٱللَّهُ يُقَدِّرُ ٱلَّيْلَ وَٱلنَّهَارَ ۚ عَلِمَ أَن لَّن تُحْصُوهُ فَتَابَ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ فَٱقْرَءُوا۟ مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ ٱلْقُرْآنِ ۚ عَلِمَ أَن سَيَكُونُ مِنكُم مَّرْضَىٰ ۙ وَآخَرُونَ يَضْرِبُونَ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ يَبْتَغُونَ مِن فَضْلِ ٱللَّهِ ۙ وَآخَرُونَ يُقَتِلُونَ فِى سَبِيلِ ٱللَّهِ ۖ فَٱقْرَءُوا۟ مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنْهُ ۚ وَأَقِيمُوا۟ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ وَآتُوا۟ ٱلزَّكَوٰةَ وَأَقْرِضُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ قَرْضًا حَسَنًۭا ۚ وَمَا تُقَدِّمُوا۟ لِأَنفُسِكُم مِّنْ خَيْرٍۢ تَجِدُوهُ عِندَ ٱللَّهِ هُوَ خَيْرًۭا وَأَعْظَمَ أَجْرًۭا ۚ وَٱسْتَغْفِرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ ۖ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۢ ‎⟫
> *Truly your Lord knows that you stand [in prayer] near two-thirds of the night, and [sometimes] half of it, and [sometimes] a third of it, and [so do] a party of those with you. And Allah determines the night and the day. He knows that you cannot keep count of it, so He has turned to you in mercy. Recite, therefore, of the Qur'an as much as may be easy for you. He knows that among you are those who are sick, and others who travel through the land seeking of Allah's bounty, and yet others who fight in the cause of Allah. So recite of it as much as may be easy [for you], and establish prayer, and give the poor-due, and lend to Allah a goodly loan. Whatever good you send forward for yourselves, you shall find it with Allah—better and mightier in reward. And seek forgiveness of Allah; truly Allah is All-Forgiving, All-Merciful.*

In the opening verse of this same sūra, the Almighty enjoins His Messenger in the most direct terms:

> ⟪quran 73:8⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ وَتَبَتَّلْ إِلَيْهِ تَبْتِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *And remember the Name of your Lord and devote yourself to Him with complete devotion.*

The word *ism* (name) here encompasses a profound theological meaning. It denotes not merely a conventional appellation, but rather the essential attributes and qualities by which the Divine manifests Itself to creation. God Himself is utterly beyond all linguistic formulations and sensory comprehension, yet He is accessible to human consciousness precisely *through* His Names—those beautiful attributes which He has chosen to reveal and which are not the inventions of human convention but the self-disclosure of the Divine. Thus, devotion to the Names of God constitutes devotion to God Himself.[^cite-62] To remain ignorant of these Names is tantamount to a kind of spiritual heedlessness. This truth has been made clear in the Qur'an:

> ⟪quran 58:19⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱسْتَحْوَذَ عَلَيْهِمُ ٱلشَّيْطَنُ فَأَنسَىٰهُمْ ذِكْرَ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ حِزْبُ ٱلشَّيْطَنِ ۚ أَلَآ إِنَّ حِزْبَ ٱلشَّيْطَنِ هُمُ ٱلْخَسِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Satan has gained mastery over them and caused them to forget the remembrance of Allah. Those are Satan's faction. Verily, it is Satan's faction that shall be the losers.*

And again:

> ⟪quran 63:9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ لَا تُلْهِكُمْ أَمْوَلُكُمْ وَلَآ أَوْلَدُكُمْ عَن ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ وَمَن يَفْعَلْ ذَلِكَ فَأُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْخَسِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Let not your wealth nor your children distract you from the remembrance of Allah. And whosoever does that—those are truly the losers.*

The connection between love of God and the constancy of His remembrance finds its clearest expression in the saying of the Commander of the Faithful: "He who loves a thing is consumed by the mention of it." The verb *lahija* ⟪ar:لھج⟫ carries the sense both of dedication and of unceasing repetition—a tongue that cannot refrain from mentioning what the heart cherishes.[^cite-63] The Prophet (upon whom be peace) himself attested to this reality when he declared in his invocation: "My tongue has dedicated itself without cease to Your remembrance." Indeed, he taught that the Names of God function not as abstract concepts but as remedies and sources of spiritual healing: "O He whose Name is medicine, and whose remembrance is cure." The Name is not a mere word or conventional designation, but rather a salve for the sickness of human error and the negligence that has become second nature to fallen humanity.[^cite-64] Yet just as the power of medicine lies not in contemplation but in consumption, so too does the efficacy of dhikr—the remembrance of God—depend upon its *practice*, not upon intellectual reflection alone.

The Qur'an itself has spoken of its verses as dhikr and has commanded the believers to recite them abundantly. In a celebrated tradition, a man approached the Messenger of Allah (upon whom be peace and blessings) saying: "O Messenger of Allah! The commands of Islam are many for me. Tell me of one thing to which I may hold fast!" The Prophet replied: "Let your tongue remain ever moist with the remembrance of Allah." This teaching finds its resonance in another verse of supreme importance:

> ⟪quran 33:41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ ذِكْرًۭا كَثِيرًۭا ‎ ‏وَسَبِّحُوهُ بُكْرَةًۭ وَأَصِيلًا ‎ ‏هُوَ ٱلَّذِى يُصَلِّى عَلَيْكُمْ وَمَلَٓئِكَتُهُۥ لِيُخْرِجَكُم مِّنَ ٱلظُّلُمَتِ إِلَى ٱلنُّورِۚ وَكَانَ بِٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ رَحِيمًۭا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Remember Allah with much remembrance, and glorify Him in the early morning and in the evening. It is He who sends His blessings upon you, and His angels [likewise], that He may bring you forth from darkness into light. And He is Ever Merciful to the believers.*

In this verse, observe the sacred reciprocity: the remembrance of the believers invokes the remembrance of God for them; the unification of the heart through dhikr opens the pathway by which divine mercy descends and transforms darkness into illumination. The Almighty has made this bond explicit:

> ⟪quran 2:152⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَٱذْكُرُونِىٓ أَذْكُرْكُمْ وَٱشْكُرُوا۟ لِى وَلَا تَكْفُرُونِ ‎⟫
> *Therefore remember Me, and I shall remember you; and be grateful to Me, and be not ungrateful to Me.*

The Commander of the Faithful, ʿAlī (upon whom be peace), has spoken of this mystery in one of his addresses: "Whosoever mentions God, God revives his heart and illuminates the innermost substance of his being—that subtle inner reality which the Qur'an calls *al-qalb*." The Qur'an refers to those possessed of such illuminated hearts as *ūlū al-albāb*—those who possess understanding—in the verse:

> ⟪quran 3:190-191⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ فِى خَلْقِ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱخْتِلَفِ ٱلَّيْلِ وَٱلنَّهَارِ لَآيَتٍۢ لِّأُو۟لِى ٱلْأَلْبَبِ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ يَذْكُرُونَ ٱللَّهَ قِيَمًۭا وَقُعُودًۭا وَعَلَىٰ جُنُوبِهِمْ وَيَتَفَكَّرُونَ فِى خَلْقِ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ رَبَّنَا مَا خَلَقْتَ هَذَا بَطِلًۭا سُبْحَنَكَ فَقِنَا عَذَابَ ٱلنَّارِ ‎⟫
> *Verily, in the creation of the heavens and the earth, and in the alternation of night and day, there are indeed signs for those of understanding—those who remember Allah standing, sitting, and upon their sides, and who contemplate upon the creation of the heavens and the earth, saying: "Our Lord! Thou hast not created this in vain. Exalted are Thou above all that they associate with Thee as partners. Preserve us from the torment of the Fire."*

This verse illuminates the inseparable connection between remembrance and contemplation. The act of dhikr enlivens the heart, awakening within it a consciousness that deepens the capacity for spiritual comprehension. When the heart becomes animated by love—as the Prophet (upon whom be peace) taught, saying that "He who loves a thing mentions it with passion"—a sacred circle of faith is established wherein each element strengthens all the others. The more intently one reflects upon the Divine Names, the more one perceives their splendor and beauty; the more one perceives this beauty, the more the soul is drawn to love the Divine; the more one loves God, the more one is impelled to remember Him constantly; and the more one engages in remembrance, the more one penetrates the hidden mysteries concealed within the verses of revelation. In this way, reflection leads to the deepening of remembrance, while remembrance itself opens the doors of understanding.

Dhikr represents the very summit and pinnacle of all devotional practice. It assumes many outward forms—the standing posture of prayer, the bowings and prostrations, the utterances of praise, the silent contemplation accompanied by humility and reverential fear. These various forms of worship each require their appointed times and prescribed places, yet dhikr alone transcends such limitations. It may be performed at any moment, in any place, in any circumstance—while eating, while walking, in solitude or amid others. For this reason, dhikr is not merely one act of worship among others, but rather an integral dimension of the believer's continuous existence. Imam Jaʿfar al-Ṣādiq (upon whom be peace) has stated: "Every action possesses a limit beyond which it cannot proceed, save the remembrance of God." Just as all prescribed obligations reach their completion—the one who fasts the thirty days of Ramaḍān fulfills the obligation of the fast—so too with all formal acts. Yet with dhikr, there exists no terminus, no point of sufficiency, no conceivable limit to which one might arrive. The Commander of the Faithful would engage in remembrance even while partaking of sustenance; Muḥammad al-Bāqir (upon whom be peace), a later inheritor of the Prophetic wisdom, maintained this very practice, uniting the action of walking with the invocation of God's Name.[^cite-65]

In this practice, we recognize the truth of that verse of the Qur'an which speaks of those who are neither distracted by commerce nor by gain from the remembrance of God:

> ⟪quran 70:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَلَىٰ صَلَاتِهِمْ دَآئِمُونَ ‎⟫
> *Those who are ever constant in their prayers.*

These are the souls who dwell perpetually in the station of prayer—in the presence and remembrance of God. The Divine wisdom has equated prayer with the remembrance of God when it declares:

> ⟪quran 20:14⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّنِىٓ أَنَا ٱللَّهُ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّآ أَنَا۠ فَٱعْبُدْنِى وَأَقِمِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ لِذِكْرِىٓ ‎⟫
> *Verily, I am Allah! There is no god save Me. So worship Me, and establish prayer for My remembrance.*

The Commander of the Faithful has taught that the perpetual remembrance of God is the nourishment of the soul and the very key (*miftāḥ*) that unlocks the door to prayer itself. The Qur'an has captured this relationship most eloquently:

> ⟪quran 29:45⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱتْلُ مَآ أُوحِىَ إِلَيْكَ مِنَ ٱلْكِتَبِ وَأَقِمِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ ۖ إِنَّ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ تَنْهَىٰ عَنِ ٱلْفَحْشَآءِ وَٱلْمُنكَرِ ۗ وَلَذِكْرُ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ يَعْلَمُ مَا تَصْنَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *Recite what has been revealed to you of the Book, and establish prayer. Verily, prayer forbids indecency and evil-doing, and the remembrance of Allah is greater. And Allah knows all that you do.*

In this verse, prayer is presented as a restraining force—a guardian that protects the soul from depravity and transgression. Though prayer itself possesses both a formal dimension and a rational structure, consisting as it does of prescribed movements and utterances performed at specified times, it is ultimately something defined and bounded by these very constraints. It cannot occur outside its appointed hours, nor can it take forms other than those ordained. But the remembrance of God transcends all such limitations; it is the living spirit that animates prayer itself, the positive and creative force that revivifies the letter of the law with meaning and substance. The excellence of dhikr over prayer is thus analogous to the excellence of the soul over the body: the soul does not negate the corporeal form, but rather encompasses it, gives it life, and through this vital union achieves its own perfection and wholeness.

<!-- section 23 (id=3604, raw_sort=23): ذکر اللہ کی حقیقت -->

## The Reality of the Remembrance of Allah

We now turn to the fruit of the remembrance of Allah (dhikr, the invocation and commemoration of the Divine) and its fundamental purpose: *realization*, the process by which divine truth becomes an immediate existential reality. ⟪ar:تَوَحٌُد⟫ This process resembles *tawhīd* (the integration of consciousness into absolute divine oneness)—a self-unification wherein the soul assimilates into itself, distinct from the monotheistic acknowledgment of unity with an external other. We may grasp the fruit of dhikr by understanding its antithesis: *heedlessness*, forgetfulness, and distraction from the Divine presence.

Allah condemns most severely the prayer of hypocrisy and the hypocrite's false devotion. He declares:

> ⟪quran 107:4-6⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْمُصَلِّينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَن صَلَاتِهِمْ سَاهُونَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ يُرَآءُونَ ‎⟫
> *So woe unto those performers of Salat (prayers) (hypocrites), Who delay their Salat (prayer) from their stated fixed times, Those who do good deeds only to be seen (of men),*
> — **Quran 107:4–6**

Woe to those who pray yet are heedless of their prayers, and who show off their devotion.

Similarly, Maulana Ali (the Commander of the Faithful) forbids the invocation of Allah with negligence and pretense. Yet when negligence is entirely removed from remembrance, a perfect dhikr emerges—one in which the person forgets himself utterly. Maulana Ali thus weaves together two seemingly contradictory imperatives: that carelessness must not dwell in remembrance, and yet that attention must become so intense that the self dissolves. He teaches:

> Do not mention Allah carelessly, nor forget Him in your heedlessness. Rather, remember Him with complete presence—a remembrance wherein your heart and tongue are in harmony, and what you conceal agrees with what you manifest. Yet you shall never truly remember Him until you become oblivious of your own soul in this remembrance!

This teaching encapsulates the essence of the spiritual path. It opens to us all those states from which perfect sincerity flows. The heart of the spiritual way is indeed *Ihlas*, sincerity. On one hand, dhikr enlivens the heart and kindles sincere intention; on the other, sincerity itself becomes the virtue that brings both perfection and maturity to remembrance. In this consummate state, the utterance of the tongue achieves perfect consonance with the intention of the heart, so that not the slightest gap remains between word and inner reality. This harmony signifies that the divine reality released upon the tongue becomes a true echo of the heart's glorification—that heart which is the mirror of inward nature, the nursery from which all spiritual virtues are born.[^cite-66]

When the soul has become entirely purified and transparent, and has unified with the utterances of intellect and tongue, it becomes pellucid to the spiritual standards (the divine realities) embedded within it, and begins to perceive the treasures concealed in its depths. These are the virtues that sparkle in the heart through the remembrance of Allah, then manifest themselves in external deeds. Without these moral and spiritual treasures, the apparent act of dhikr becomes mere heedlessness and ostentation. The ignorant one is he who does not strive for sincerity and turns away from the Greater Struggle (al-Jihad al-Akbar), neglecting to fulfill the commands of Allah.

Maulana Ali's teaching unlocks the door to the reality of dhikr through which we may advance toward divine truth. To reach this highest station requires the annihilation of the self (fana, self-effacement). To perceive divine connection, one must remove the veil of selfhood that lies between truth and oneself. The beginning of knowledge is self-forgetting; its culmination is the annihilation of the separate self. The reality of remembrance thus demands a revolutionary forgetting of all else. Man advances from human perfection to divine reality (al-Haqq). The first stage is the elimination of hypocrisy and the pursuit of sincerity, honesty, and integrity—qualities that produce *kamāl awwal* (primary perfection). In this state, the person's individual identity yet remains. This harmony of intention and deed is called perfection; yet because it is still mediated through the human being himself, it ranks as secondary.[^cite-67]

In true reality, the self-identity does not survive, for the person has become oblivious to himself. At this station, ⟪ar:'ذاکر'⟫ the *dhakir* (one who remembers) ceases to be the focus; instead, all attention turns wholly toward ⟪ar:'مذکور'⟫ the *madhkur* (the One remembered). The reality of dhikr becomes one with the absolute Truth. At such a moment, one perceives inwardly that it is Allah Himself who is invoking—and this invocation merely resonates through the human tongue. The existence of the person becomes a phantom that is erased by the very remembrance it performs.

In this light, we return to the divine saying transmitted as a hadith qudsi (a sacred tradition): "My servant ceases not to draw nigh unto Me through the performance of the supererogatory devotions (Nawafil) until I love him. When I love him, I become his hearing by which he hears, his sight by which he sees, his hand by which he grasps, and his foot by which he walks."[^cite-68] Now we understand: by Nawafil is meant the remembrance of Allah. Observe that Allah is the root and source of every action of the one who remembers. Allah sees and hears the deeds of those whom He loves. Allah does not alter Himself to enter into the person's intentions and actions; rather, He becomes unified with intention and action. In other words, divine realities descend and obscure the false self of the rememberer, allowing him to perceive beyond the suspicion of his apparent existence, and to comprehend the inner realities of the Qur'anic verses. Thus it is written:

> ⟪quran 37:96⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ‎⟫
> *"While Allah has created you and what you make!"*
> — **Quran 37:96**

And in another verse:

> ⟪quran 8:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَلَمْ تَقْتُلُوهُمْ وَلَكِنَّ ٱللَّهَ قَتَلَهُمْ ۚ وَمَا رَمَيْتَ إِذْ رَمَيْتَ وَلَكِنَّ ٱللَّهُ رَمَىٰ ۚ وَلِيُبْلِىَ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْهُ بَلَآءً حَسَنًا ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *You killed them not, but Allah killed them. And you (Muhammad PBUH) threw not when you did throw but Allah threw, that He might test the believers by a fair trial from Him. Verily, Allah is All-Hearer, All-Knower.*
> — **Quran 8:17**

This very truth was exemplified by the Prophet (upon whom be peace) and by Maulana Ali. During a battle, an arrow pierced Ali's foot as he stood in prayer. He instructed those present: "Remove the arrow whilst I am in prostration." They did so as he began his prayer and entered his bow. When he had finished, he asked, "Have you taken it out?" as though he had felt nothing. This marks the zenith of remembrance: the physical existence of man—all sensation and self-awareness—vanishes.

The Messenger of Allah taught: "Excellence (Ihsan) is that you worship Allah as if you see Him, and if you do not see Him, know that He sees you."[^cite-69] This hadith, when pondered carefully, reveals depths: in one reading, only Allah perceives Allah; the servant cannot. True manifestation of the Divine cannot be attained so long as any creature remains in the vision. In the narrative of Moses:

> ⟪quran 7:143⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَمَّا جَآءَ مُوسَىٰ لِمِيقَتِنَا وَكَلَّمَهُۥ رَبُّهُۥ قَالَ رَبِّ أَرِنِىٓ أَنظُرْ إِلَيْكَ ۚ قَالَ لَن تَرَىٰنِى وَلَكِنِ ٱنظُرْ إِلَى ٱلْجَبَلِ فَإِنِ ٱسْتَقَرَّ مَكَانَهُۥ فَسَوْفَ تَرَىٰنِى ۚ فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّىٰ رَبُّهُۥ لِلْجَبَلِ جَعَلَهُۥ دَكًّۭا وَخَرَّ مُوسَىٰ صَعِقًۭا ۚ فَلَمَّآ أَفَاقَ قَالَ سُبْحَنَكَ تُبْتُ إِلَيْكَ وَأَنَا۠ أَوَّلُ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ ‎⟫
> *And when Musa (Moses) came at the time and place appointed by Us, and his Lord spoke to him, he said: "O my Lord! Show me (Yourself), that I may look upon You." Allah said: "You cannot see Me, but look upon the mountain if it stands still in its place then you shall see Me." So when his Lord appeared to the mountain, He made it collapse to dust, and Musa (Moses) fell down unconscious. Then when he recovered his senses he said: "Glory be to You, I turn to You in repentance and I am the first of the believers."*
> — **Quran 7:143**

The radiance of divine Reality struck Moses into unconsciousness. God did not shine upon Moses himself, but upon the mountain—a splendor that Moses, in his creaturely state, could not endure.

The companion Abu al-Darda once observed Maulana Ali lying motionless in a garden of Medina, his body void of all sensation. Abu al-Darda hastened to the house of Fatima (upon her be peace) in great concern. She replied: "My husband Ali has not passed away. He has rather fallen into a state of ecstasy through awe of Allah. Such states come upon him often." The fear spoken of here signifies knowledge of God's overwhelming majesty. Allah mentions this fear as the hallmark of true perfection:

> ⟪quran 79:40-41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِۦ وَنَهَى ٱلنَّفْسَ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰ ‎ ‏فَإِنَّ ٱلْجَنَّةَ هِىَ ٱلْمَأْوَىٰ ‎⟫
> *But as for him who feared standing before his Lord, and restrained himself from impure evil desires, and lusts. Verily, Paradise will be his abode.*
> — **Quran 79:40–41**

Though fear ordinarily brings terror, the fear of Allah brings not dread but beauty. This fear grants the soul a magnetic attraction toward divine truth. As the spiritual masters teach: when one fears a creature, one flees from it; but when one fears Allah, one runs toward Him. The Qur'an confirms this:

> ⟪quran 9:118⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَعَلَى ٱلثَّلَثَةِ ٱلَّذِينَ خُلِّفُوا۟ حَتَّىٰٓ إِذَا ضَاقَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ ٱلْأَرْضُ بِمَا رَحُبَتْ وَضَاقَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَظَنُّوٓا۟ أَن لَّا مَلْجَأَ مِنَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَّآ إِلَيْهِ ثُمَّ تَابَ عَلَيْهِمْ لِيَتُوبُوٓا۟ ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ هُوَ ٱلتَّوَّابُ ٱلرَّحِيمُ ‎⟫
> *And (He did forgive also) the three [who did not join the Tabuk expedition (whom the Prophet PBUH)] left (i.e. he did not give his judgement in their case, and their case was suspended for Allah's Decision) till for them the earth, vast as it is, was straitened and their ownselves were straitened to them, and they perceived that there is no fleeing from Allah, and no refuge but with Him. Then, He accepted their repentance, that they might repent (unto Him). Verily, Allah is the One Who accepts repentance, Most Merciful.*
> — **Quran 9:118**

This utterance of Maulana Ali attests to his spiritual love and the fusion of his consciousness with divine Reality. Thus, as Maulana Fatima noted, he often enters such a state of absorption.

There is a tradition: Surely Allah has for His saints a draught; when they drink it, they become intoxicated; when intoxicated, they rejoice; when they rejoice, they are blessed; when blessed, they dissolve; when dissolved, they are freed; when freed, they are purified. Seeking, they find; finding, they attain; attaining, they become one with Him such that no distinction remains between them and their Beloved.

The Messenger of Allah (upon whom be peace) said: "There have come upon you nights and days of knowledge of perfect tawhīd that no angel or prophet can bear."[^cite-70] This tawhīd—this feeling of absolute divine unity—is the fruit of all worship, the most intoxicating of all states. The rememberer drinks of this wine. In the beginning, it appears that the servant drinks the wine of the remembrance of the Names of Allah and the servant does the remembering. But in the highest degrees, Allah Himself drinks the wine of His servant's name and begins to invoke Himself through the servant's tongue. This occurs when the person has destroyed his selfhood in the remembrance of Allah. Maulana Ali teaches that the remembrance of Allah is neither mere speech nor mere thought. ⟪ar:'مذکور'⟫ It is first *the One remembered* and then ⟪ar:'ذاکر'⟫ *the rememberer* (⟪ar:اول من المذکور و ثانی من الذاکر⟫).

That is: Allah is first in remembrance, and man's remembrance is but a reflection of Divine remembrance—its fruit and sign. Allah says: "Remember Me, and I shall remember you." When we plumb the depths of dhikr, we perceive the command of Allah (may He be exalted) revealed through the word ⟪ar:'کُن'⟫ (*kun*, "Be!")—the utterance from which all existence emerged. Allah invoked the possible (al-mumkin) and summoned it forth, bringing it into being from absolute nonexistence. Allah was the remembrance of creation, and creation became His remembrance. The Qur'an poses to us this question:

> ⟪quran 76:1⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هَلْ أَتَىٰ عَلَى ٱلْإِنسَنِ حِينٌۭ مِّنَ ٱلدَّهْرِ لَمْ يَكُن شَيْـًۭٔا مَّذْكُورًا ‎⟫
> *Has there not been over man a period of time, when he was nothing to be mentioned?*
> — **Quran 76:1**

Here man is designated as something brought into being by Allah's creation. His nonexistence implies that there was a time when Allah did not yet invoke him into being. At that moment, man was known—but known to Allah alone. Thus the remembrance of Allah for man precedes man's own existence; the Divine invocation surpasses all human memory. Man invokes Allah through His Names, whereas Allah invokes man through the word *kun*. Yet this word was not uttered once and then fell silent; rather, it reverberates continually in the human soul until the Day of Judgment, a witness to the divinity of Allah the Almighty. Through this word, Allah breathed the spirit into the form of existence itself.

When Hazrat Kamil asked Amir al-Mu'minin, "What is *al-Haqiqa* (the Reality)?", he replied: "Al-Haqiqa is the name of unveiling the glory of Allah, stripped of all veils." In the light of that unveiling, to annihilate all that is not Allah is called *Haqiqa*. To dissolve entirely into the attribute of *tawhīd* is called *Haqiqa*. It is a light radiating from the dawn of eternity, whose rays illumine the sanctuary of oneness.

By "sanctuary" is meant the locus where Allah manifests Himself as the One. The Names that animate the soul and sustain it—the soul is the manifestation wherein Allah reveals Himself in a particular mode. Ibn al-'Arabi writes in his *Futuhat al-Makkiyya* that all praise belongs to Him who created things from nothing and negated them, then brought them into existence through the attention of His Word. When the Divine Word inclines toward the possible (objects of possibility), the attributes of this world come into being. The spirit of possibility is thereby breathed into existence, which is related to the body. The heart within this body is the Name of Allah which gives it life. Every servant has a name derived from his Master. Thus the servant becomes the body of the Master, and the Master becomes the heart of the servant.[^cite-71]

This analogy recalls the saying of Amir al-Mu'minin: "The remembrance of Allah sets hearts ablaze." The Name descending from above is reflected in the Name resonating in the heart. This reflection occurs when the rust of the heart is burned away by the fire of dhikr. It is the union of an outer light with an inner light—what the Qur'anic verse of light (ayat al-nur) describes.

Now the question arises: what distinguishes the divine Names—which are the origin of all things—from the Names mentioned specifically in the Qur'an? On one hand, all creation is the Book of Allah, and all appearances are the words of this Book. Yet on the other hand, certain Names are singled out in the Qur'an for our glorification and invocation. Why? The Qur'an itself provides an answer:

> ⟪quran 17:110⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلِ ٱدْعُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ أَوِ ٱدْعُوا۟ ٱلرَّحْمَنَ ۖ أَيًّۭا مَّا تَدْعُوا۟ فَلَهُ ٱلْأَسْمَآءُ ٱلْحُسْنَىٰ ۚ وَلَا تَجْهَرْ بِصَلَاتِكَ وَلَا تُخَافِتْ بِهَا وَٱبْتَغِ بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ سَبِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *Say (O Muhammad PBUH): "Invoke Allah or invoke the Most Beneficent (Allah), by whatever name you invoke Him (it is the same), for to Him belong the Best Names. And offer your Salat (prayer) neither aloud nor in a low voice, but follow a way between.*
> — **Quran 17:110**

In this verse, Allah Himself directs the believers to invoke the Names that have been revealed in the Qur'an—Names wholly distinct from the names of idols:

> ⟪quran 53:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنْ هِىَ إِلَّآ أَسْمَآءٌۭ سَمَّيْتُمُوهَآ أَنتُمْ وَآبَآؤُكُم مَّآ أَنزَلَ ٱللَّهُ بِهَا مِن سُلْطَنٍ ۚ إِن يَتَّبِعُونَ إِلَّا ٱلظَّنَّ وَمَا تَهْوَى ٱلْأَنفُسُ ۖ وَلَقَدْ جَآءَهُم مِّن رَّبِّهِمُ ٱلْهُدَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *They are but names which you have named, you and your fathers, for which Allah has sent down no authority. They follow but a guess and that which they themselves desire, whereas there has surely come to them the Guidance from their Lord!*
> — **Quran 53:23**

The names of idols are mere appellations attached to worldly appearances that are self-referential, or signs bearing no connection to the Reality they falsely represent. But the Names of Allah are intrinsically linked to His Essence and constitute the reality of the substances He created. Therefore, these Names possess not merely the power to inform, but the transformative power to illuminate. They unveil the greatness and reality of Allah within the human heart and intellect. For this reason, Allah's existence is inevitable—no existence lies outside His scope. Yet the rust upon the heart obscures His presence, even though the heart itself is His creation.

Therefore it is necessary to purify the heart from within through the remembrance of Allah, so that the inward reality may be unveiled to it. The divine Names of Allah are the pinnacle of manifestations, gathering all appearances within their compass while themselves transcending it. This inward and outward substance may be likened to light and shadow—both manifestations of a single essence, yet bearing no relation to one another. As Ibn al-'Arabi taught, the Existence of the Real is a fixed light, and all creation is the shadow that follows it.

Maulana Ali declares in his invocations: "I call upon You by all the Names You have chosen for Yourself." The fact that Allah Himself has named Himself testifies to the majesty and potency of these Names. And he taught: "You shall never invoke Him until you forget yourselves in His remembrance." What is meant by forgetting oneself and becoming oblivious to one's existence? It is impossible for a conscious person to be wholly unaware of his own existence during remembrance. If a person attempts to force self-forgetfulness, that very effort will prevent oblivion. We understand, then, that to be oblivious to oneself means to direct all attention toward the Names of Allah, leaving no room or space within soul, spirit, intellect, or being where remembrance is absent—such that the soul has no ground upon which to plant itself. This capacity for annihilation comes by the grace of Allah when a person strives to polish away the rust that veils the heart. That rust which deprives us of the vision of Allah's absolute oneness.

Allah said to His Prophet: "We shall make you recite, so you shall not forget":

> ⟪quran 87:6-7⟫
> ⟪ar:‏سَنُقْرِئُكَ فَلَا تَنسَىٰٓ ‎ ‏إِلَّا مَا شَآءَ ٱللَّهُ ۚ إِنَّهُۥ يَعْلَمُ ٱلْجَهْرَ وَمَا يَخْفَىٰ ‎⟫
> *We shall make you to recite (the Quran), so you (O Muhammad (Peace be upon him)) shall not forget (it), Except what Allah, may will, He knows what is apparent and what is hidden.*
> — **Quran 87:6–7**

Why would you forget? Because We shall cleanse your pure heart of all rust and impurity. And He commanded: "Remember your Lord when you forget":

> ⟪quran 18:24⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِلَّآ أَن يَشَآءَ ٱللَّهُ ۚ وَٱذْكُر رَّبَّكَ إِذَا نَسِيتَ وَقُلْ عَسَىٰٓ أَن يَهْدِيَنِ رَبِّى لِأَقْرَبَ مِنْ هَذَا رَشَدًۭا ‎⟫
> *Except (with the saying), "If Allah will!" And remember your Lord when you forget and say: "It may be that my Lord guides me unto a nearer way of truth than this."*
> — **Quran 18:24**

When a person forgets all that is not Allah, then he becomes capable of remembering Allah. If Allah dwells in the station of affirmation, then man dwells in the station of negation in contrast to Him. When this negation (creaturely nothingness) is itself negated, there emerges the complete affirmation of Allah—just as multiplying negation by negation produces affirmation.

The Creator of all existence declared: "I am the death of death!" Rumi captured the meaning of Ali's teachings in his *Masnavi*, writing: He said, "I have drawn the sword for Allah's sake. I am a servant of Allah, not subject to my body's commands. I am the Lion of Allah, not the lion of my desires. My deeds witness to my faith. In battle, I am Allah's sword, carried in the hand of Allah. I have cast off the burden of my self from my path. I have forgotten all save Allah. Allah is my sun, and I am His reflection. I am the key! I am the veil between Allah and His creation. I am filled with pearls of tawhīd like a jeweled sword. I do not slay men in war—I give them life in the Hereafter!"[^cite-72]

Allah's movement toward His servant is possible only after the annihilation of the servant's existence. This negation is the nothingness from which Allah Almighty created all existence. Allah created man from nonexistence; now man must annihilate himself and find Allah. By negating the substance that never truly existed (for human substance is transient and impermanent), man acknowledges what has always been. Thus it is written:

> ⟪quran 55:26-27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍۢ ‎ ‏وَيَبْقَىٰ وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ ‎⟫
> *Whatsoever is on it (the earth) will perish. And the Face of your Lord full of Majesty and Honour will abide forever.*
> — **Quran 55:26–27**

Every creature bears two aspects, or faces. One is the divine face—the reality of all things; the other is the mortal face—perishable and transient. Therefore, the Face of Allah, which is immortal, is not merely the divine reality but the reality that subsists within all things. Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other ilah (god) along with Allah, La ilaha illa Huwa (none has the right to be worshipped but He). Everything will perish save His Face. His is the Decision, and to Him you (all) shall be returned.*
> — **Quran 28:88**

Al-Ghazali taught that creatures are not annihilated at some particular moment in time; rather, they exist in perpetual annihilation. This is because everything except Allah is imperfect in itself. Through the Face of Allah, all things receive their continuance from the Almighty—what we perceive as existence. Their being flows not from themselves but from the Face of Allah. Therefore, the Face of Allah is the sole reality; all else is illusion. He wrote of the Sufis: "There remains in them no power save the remembrance of Allah; they no longer possess the power to remember themselves." When a person reaches this station, he dwells simultaneously in annihilation and subsistence. Yet even this annihilation passes away, for the soul is heedless of itself and oblivious to its own annihilation—for were it aware of its annihilation, it would be aware of itself.

Al-Qushayri taught that whoever has not tasted the solitude of annihilation cannot receive the sustenance of Allah's remembrance. Here, solitude refers to the soul's proximity to itself as manifested in self-praise, desire, and egoism. This proximity cannot be removed without the remembrance of Allah. This is the reality of dhikr, which the Lord has encapsulated in a single utterance: that you become forgotten in the remembrance of Allah. Thus He declares:

> ⟪quran 2:198⟫
> ⟪ar:‏لَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَن تَبْتَغُوا۟ فَضْلًۭا مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ ۚ فَإِذَآ أَفَضْتُم مِّنْ عَرَفَتٍۢ فَٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ عِندَ ٱلْمَشْعَرِ ٱلْحَرَامِ ۖ وَٱذْكُرُوهُ كَمَا هَدَىٰكُمْ وَإِن كُنتُم مِّن قَبْلِهِۦ لَمِنَ ٱلضَّآلِّينَ ‎⟫
> *There is no sin on you if you seek the Bounty of your Lord (during pilgrimage by trading, etc.). Then when you leave 'Arafat, remember Allah (by glorifying His Praises, i.e. prayers and invocations, etc.) at the Mash'ar-il-Haram. And remember Him (by invoking Allah for all good, etc.) as He has guided you, and verily, you were, before, of those who were astray.*
> — **Quran 2:198**

Here, guidance refers to elevation in the levels of remembrance. The first is ⟪ar:'ذکر السان'⟫ *dhikr al-lisan*, remembrance of the tongue, which is bound to the self. Then comes ⟪ar:'ذکر القلب'⟫ *dhikr al-qalb*, remembrance of the heart, which is bound to acts of worship that release the grace of Allah. Next is ⟪ar:'ذکر السر'⟫ *dhikr al-sirr*, remembrance of the secret or innermost mystery, which relates to the vision of worship, unveiling the truths of divine attributes. Then follows ⟪ar:'ذکر الروح'⟫ *dhikr al-ruh*, remembrance of the spirit, which contemplates the Essence in the light emanating from that vision. Finally, ⟪ar:'ذکر الکھفی'⟫ *dhikr al-khafi*, the hidden remembrance, which relates to the beauty of the Origin wherein duality yet subsists, and finally the remembrance of the source itself, which pertains to true vision beyond duality's end.[^cite-73]

Maulana Ali teaches:

> Do not abandon dhikr because you perceive no presence of Allah within it, for it is better that you do not find Him in your remembrance than that you forget Him. He will lead you from heedlessness to vigilance, and thence to a remembrance in which all vanishes save the One remembered. It is no difficult thing for Allah to accomplish.

Ibn al-'Ajiba wrote in his *Hikam*: The more a person is annihilated in the Name of Allah, the more he errs in knowing the origin. He observed: "The Name of Allah is the joy of my heart and the coolness of my eyes." Yet any designation is merely a name; true happiness flows ever from the essence of a thing, not from its appellation. Imam Ja'far al-Sadiq (upon whom be peace) declared:

> The Name of Allah is distinct from His Essence. All upon which His Name appears is a creation, and thus is separate from Allah. All that is described is created; the Creator cannot be circumscribed within the limits that define His creation. The Names of Allah are ninety-nine. Were the Name and the Named identical, each Name would itself be a god. But Allah is He to whom the Names point; they are distinct from Him and from His creation.

Each Name points to an attribute yet also bears its own identity. For instance, *al-Rahman* (the Merciful), *al-Karim* (the Generous), and *al-Sattar* (the Concealer) all designate Allah; yet these Names themselves possess identities distinct from one another. *Al-Rahman* differs from *al-Karim*, and *al-Karim* from *al-Sattar*. The separation of these Names indicates their limitation. Though real in themselves, they become as shadows and phantasms before Allah, their status in His sight that of "imagined realities." The true reality of all Names returns to the Self, which is Allah Himself. Thus, from one perspective there is distinction between Name and Named; from another, the two are one. In one sense, the Name is naught but a divine attribute pointing to the Named; in another sense, the Name is a vocalized designation. *Al-Rahman*, for instance, has an origin which is Mercy (rahma), just as *al-Karim* originates in Generosity (karam). Thus *al-Rahman* is the Name of Mercy, and *al-Karim* is the Name of Generosity—in this respect, Name and Named are identical.

The attributes dissolve into the Named because they become unified with the Named and subsist not of themselves; this is the reality of tawhīd. After this knowledge, the word of *shahada* (testimony) ceases to be a formula, for all false gods have merged into the Essence of Allah and have vanished. The meaning of this word is: there is no reality save the one Reality (the Self alone). From this perspective, only ⟪ar:'اللہ'⟫ Allah remains, for He is the One with no peer, and none can know Him save Allah Himself.[^cite-74]

The Messenger of Allah (upon whom be peace and blessings) exemplifies the perfect human being. Maulana Ali declared: "We are the Most Beautiful Names of Allah." ⟪ar:ھو علامۃ العظمی و آیاتہ الکبری⟫ He is the Supreme Sign and His Greatest Verses. The Messenger said: "Whoever sees me has seen the Truth." Thus the Messenger, Ali, and the Imams (upon whom be peace) are those who manifested the divine attributes in human form. They are mirrors wherein the divine attributes are reflected. The brighter the light of Truth shines upon them, the brighter its reflection in these perfected beings.

In the first sermon of the *Nahj al-Balagha*, Maulana Ali states: "The perfection of sincerity is to purify Allah of all attributes, because every attribute testifies to the one to whom it is attributed."[^cite-75] Whoever ascribes an attribute to Allah has made it an attribute; whoever imagines it a partner has created duality; whoever divides has fractured; and whoever fragments remains ignorant.

When Maulana Ali teaches that purifying Allah from His attributes constitutes tawhīd, he does not mean that these divine attributes lack reality. Rather, he denies the notion that these attributes are autonomous and external, attached to the Truth as separate accessories, or existing outside Allah, or distinct from His Essence. Allah is the One whose attributes are boundless. What is denied here is that the reality of any divine attribute can be confined within human imagination and language. If these attributes are not separate from the Essence, and if Allah's Essence is eternal and infinite, then the attributes too must be infinite. When the Essence cannot be comprehended, how can the attributes be grasped?

In one respect it is affirmation; in another, negation. Affirmation that the attributes are not separate from the Essence; negation that these attributes cannot be contained within our thought and categories. Such is the relationship between the human soul and divine Truth. Man himself is desolate and possesses no being, yet he is not severed from Truth; rather, he becomes oblivious to himself in his worship. When man ceases to exist, the Existence of Allah alone remains. Though great contradiction appears in this, it is true: the sense of perfect divine Existence is conjoined with the feeling of the nonexistence of self.

The Prophet (upon whom be peace) said: "On the night of the Mi'raj, I learned the true significance of the Names, and I saw them return to their object and reality. What I saw was not myself; my journey was within me, pointing to me. Through it, I came to know that I am a pure servant bearing not the slightest trace of divinity."[^cite-76]

Similarly, when Maulana Ali describes his own greatness in his sermons, he unveils the greatness of Allah manifesting through him. He is the embodiment of Allah's majesty, and His majesty is the highest degree of self-denial. When one said to Imam Ja'far al-Sadiq (upon whom be peace), "You are arrogant!", he replied: "I am not arrogant, for majesty belongs to Allah alone. I have completely purged my soul of arrogance. In its place has come the majesty of Allah. So long as selfish arrogance persists, the presence of divine Greatness is impossible. When the divine Greatness takes its place, what appears is pride through the Existence of the Divine. At this point, the divine attributes shine with greater brilliance and force upon the mirror of the self, which has been made transparent by divine realities. This radiance was kindled when I burnished away the dust of ego and desire ⟪ar:ھوی⟫ from the mirror of my heart."[^cite-77]

Now we return to the sacred hadith: My servant draws nigh to Me through obligatory duties, dearer to Me than all else; and ceases not to approach Me through supererogatory acts until I love him. When I love him, I become his hearing through which he hears, his sight through which he sees, his hand with which he grasps, and his feet with which he walks.

Observe the paradox contained therein. On the one hand, Allah declares that the obligatory duties are most beloved in His sight. Yet on the other hand, it is the supererogatory devotions (the Nawafil) that cause Allah to love the servant—a love that penetrates the senses and faculties, manifesting as tawhīd. How may this apparent contradiction be resolved? When Allah loves the obligatory duties, He loves something that appears distinct from His Essence. But when Allah loves the servant who has become oblivious to himself in remembrance and knowledge of Him, that servant becomes multiple in expression because he has become a manifestation of Allah, having united with Allah. At that moment, Allah's love for the servant becomes Allah's love for Himself. Allah desired to know Himself; therefore He created this world. When a person annihilates his self in the remembrance and knowledge of Allah, the Divine command to know Himself is fulfilled.

Maulana Ali says: "It rains knowledge from me, and no bird can soar to me!" Knowledge pours from you because you have become one with the source of all knowledge. Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 76:5-6⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ ٱلْأَبْرَارَ يَشْرَبُونَ مِن كَأْسٍۢ كَانَ مِزَاجُهَا كَافُورًا ‎ ‏عَيْنًۭا يَشْرَبُ بِهَا عِبَادُ ٱللَّهِ يُفَجِّرُونَهَا تَفْجِيرًۭا ‎⟫
> *Verily, the Abrar (pious, who fear Allah and avoid evil), shall drink a cup (of wine) mixed with water from a spring in Paradise called Kafur. A spring wherefrom the slaves of Allah will drink, causing it to gush forth abundantly.*
> — **Quran 76:5–6**

This camphor wine is in truth the Essence of Allah itself. Those righteous ones amplify the source of this wine because the wine is camphor itself—containing no admixture, no duality. The remembrance of Allah not only polishes away the dust of the heart and grants it life; it also erases all traces and names of duality through the grace of the One remembered. It purifies the heart from all forms of association (*shirk*) and establishes the principle of pure monotheism. To grasp this reality is to negate all other apparent facts.

On one hand, a person knows Allah through the fact that He is unknowable, for He lies beyond the veil of the universe. On the other, in the remembrance of Allah, when a person becomes oblivious to himself, the distinction between Creator and creature dissolves. At that moment, the soul does not intermix with anything else; rather, that state of being itself becomes a state of annihilation. Existence vanishes, leaving only consciousness—a consciousness that belongs to nothing, that is bound to no entity. At such a station, the person reaches the position of *Arif billah* (one who knows through Allah), whereas otherwise he remains in *ilm billah* (knowledge of Allah).[^cite-78] As Maulana Ali taught: "Know Allah through Allah!" The purpose of remembrance is not merely to make a person forget all save Allah, but to understand that there is naught but Allah. As Ali (upon whom be peace) declared: "When the heart is illuminated by the remembrance of Allah, then the state of sight after blindness and hearing after deafness comes to be. Wherever he looks, he beholds the Face of Allah."

> ⟪quran 2:115⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلِلَّهِ ٱلْمَشْرِقُ وَٱلْمَغْرِبُ ۚ فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا۟ فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ ٱللَّهِ ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ وَسِيعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *And to Allah belong the east and the west, so wherever you turn yourselves or your faces there is the Face of Allah (and He is High above, over His Throne). Surely! Allah is All-Sufficient for His creatures' needs, All-Knowing.*
> — **Quran 2:115**

> ⟪quran 24:41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ مَن فِى ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱلطَّيْرُ صَٓفَّتٍۢ ۖ كُلٌّۭ قَدْ عَلِمَ صَلَاتَهُۥ وَتَسْبِيحَهُۥ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ عَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا يَفْعَلُونَ ‎⟫
> *See you not (O Muhammad PBUH) that Allah, He it is Whom glorify whosoever is in the heavens and the earth, and the birds with wings out-spread (in their flight). Of each one He (Allah) knows indeed his Salat (prayer) and his glorification, [or everyone knows his Salat (prayer) and his glorification], and Allah is All-Aware of what they do.*
> — **Quran 24:41**

In his sermons, Amir al-Mu'minin proclaims: "I am the Supreme Sign of Allah! I know the secrets of God! I am the extremity of all extremities! I am the companion of the rays of divine glory! I am the first, the last, the outward, the inward! I am the Face of Allah! I am Allah's mirror, His pen, His tablet! I am he called Elijah in the Gospels! I am the keeper of the mysteries of the Messenger of Allah!"

Though such words evoke the concept of *shirk* (association) in the outward worshipper, those possessed of inner knowledge grasp their true meaning. If we first understand the statement "I am the Supreme Sign of Allah!", all else becomes clear. In this sermon, Maulana Ali identifies himself with the knowledge of Allah, not with his own knowledge of Him. The knowledge that Allah possesses of Himself is not the knowledge that man possesses of Allah. Knowledge and knower and knowledge coalesce when they reach this supreme knowledge—just as knowledge and existence become one upon reaching the summit of consciousness. At this station, the knower becomes consciousness itself, and knowledge becomes the awareness that the Truth has of Itself. Consciousness attains this knowledge when it annihilates every particle of its being in Allah. One must forget oneself to remember Allah; one must become what Allah Himself is in order to become His knowledge. At that moment, man becomes a ray of divine majesty. All mysteries, ⟪ar:'السر'⟫ the secrets, dwell hidden in the Ultimate Secret—the Essence and innermost Reality of Allah—which encompasses all Names within Itself. Therefore you say: I am the first, I am the last, I am the outward, I am the inward.

Then you name yourself the Face of Allah. This utterance may be understood in light of the comparison to a mirror. When a person gazes in a mirror, the mirror ceases to exist; all attention fixes upon the face reflected within. The viewer does not even perceive the mirror's existence. The mirror loses its identity. Conversely, when attention falls upon the mirror itself, the reflected face cannot be seen. Thus the mirror identifies itself with the form the viewer perceives. At that moment, mirror and form become one, though they remain two distinct objects. So long as a person's attention rests upon the mirror, he is veiled from the face; but the moment he beholds the face, the veil lifts, revealing his own countenance. To forget the mirror's existence is the inverse of man's annihilation before divine majesty; to fix upon the face reflected in the mirror is the inverse of remembrance of Allah.

Once again we encounter paradox: the saints of Allah, cognizant that they are the opposite of annihilation and annulation before divine majesty, are those who rightly interpret the Names and attributes of Allah. The attributes that belong to Allah are not theirs. This is why these saints and the purified ones are the embodiments of Allah's Beautiful Names. The light of these attributes shines through them because they have burned the mirror of their hearts with the remembrance of Allah and erased all traces of egoism. Corporeality cannot impede the reflection of this light. These are beings whose hearts dwell in heaven whilst their bodies toil in this world. Though they live in this realm, their very life has been annihilated, as Allah has declared:

> ⟪quran 29:64⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمَا هَذِهِ ٱلْحَيَوٰةُ ٱلدُّنْيَآ إِلَّا لَهْوٌۭ وَلَعِبٌۭ ۚ وَإِنَّ ٱلدَّارُ ٱلْآخِرَةَ لَهِىَ ٱلْحَيَوَانُ ۚ لَوْ كَانُوا۟ يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *And this life of the world is only amusement and play! Verily, the home of the Hereafter, that is the life indeed (i.e. the eternal life that will never end), if they but knew.*
> — **Quran 29:64**

Therefore, their instincts are forever bound to divine realities. When Maulana Ali was struck by the sword of Ibn Muljam, his instinct was to cry: "I have succeeded by the Lord of the Ka'ba!" At the moment of his death, there remained naught but remembrance of Allah. Upon his tongue resonated: *La ilaha illallah*—there is no god but Allah. He departed this world upon the same principle upon which he had lived it, fulfilling the teaching of the Messenger of Allah who declared: "The most mysterious death is that in which the tongue remains moist with the remembrance of Allah."[^cite-79]


<!-- section 24 (id=5722, raw_sort=24): The Spirit Of The Intellect -->

## The Spirit of the Intellect

Our purpose is to outline some of the key dimensions of the spiritual ethos of Maulana Ali, with particular stress on its intellectual aspects. We shall demonstrate the pivotal role played by the intellect (al-ʿAql, the faculty of direct contemplative vision) in the elaboration and assimilation of Maulana Ali's spiritual teachings. A central aim here is to illuminate the '**spirit of the intellect**' in his worldview—a spirit that not only encompasses the operations of the rational mind, but surpasses it, embracing domains far removed from what modernity associates with intellect: moral behavior, aesthetic sensibility, and the very principle of conscious existence itself. We shall further show how this spiritual understanding of intellect stands in direct relation to the Qur'anic concept of the spirit (al-Rūḥ, the divine breath that animates consciousness), and explore the fruits of engaging deeply with this unifying spirit proper to the intellect.

It is useful to clarify at the outset our preference for 'intellect' rather than 'reason' as the rendering of al-ʿAql. The Latin *intellectus* originally signified that faculty capable of direct contemplative vision of transcendent realities. Reason, by contrast, operates indirectly and discursively—it works through logic and arrives only at mental concepts of those realities.
